                            now have a deterministic HMAC-SHA-256 token
                            form `tok_<kind>_<32hex>` keyed by
                            per-tenant salt `PII_TENANT_SALT`; the
                            clear value is stored under per-row
                            AES-GCM and reachable only through
                            `Founder.read_clear_email(...)` which
                            checks the new `pii:read_clear` scope and
                            writes a row into the INSERT-only
                            `pii_clear_audit_log` table; tampering is
                            blocked by RLS (no UPDATE/DELETE policy
                            for any role) plus a Postgres trigger
                            that raises on any UPDATE/DELETE
                            statement; salt rotation is operator-only
                            via a documented re-tokenization play,
                            Wave 15, prompt 58/70)

Every prompt's deliverables survive a re-run of the deterministic readiness
script (``make release-readiness``) which exits ``0`` when each of the ten
post-conditions (alembic head, policy pin, event example validation, prompt
registry verification, e2e integration test presence + marker, backtest spec,
red-team expected-verdict matrix, admin dashboard router mount, and the two
doc prompt recaps) passes.

OVERVIEW
--------

This repository has two active product tracks:

1) Core Coherence Engine (stable):
   Local-first coherence analysis with layered scoring, composite scoring, and
   explanation outputs across CLI, GUI, and legacy API surfaces.

2) Fund Orchestrator Backend (active buildout):
   API + persistence + workers for intake, scoring orchestration, policy-driven
   decisioning, and outbox-based event dispatch.


CURRENT IMPLEMENTATION SNAPSHOT
-------------------------------

CORE ENGINE (IMPLEMENTED)
  - Parser + 5-layer coherence stack + weighted composite + fusion adjustments.
  - Domain comparison support using coherence differentials.
  - Graceful degradation paths when specific analyzers are unavailable.
  - CLI supports: analyze, compare, serve, serve-fund, process-scoring-jobs,
    dispatch-outbox, layers, version, gui.
  - Legacy API remains available (`/analyze`, `/health`, `/layers`).

FUND BACKEND (IMPLEMENTED)
  - Fund lifecycle endpoints on both `/api/v1/*` and legacy root paths.
  - Enqueue-only scoring trigger and asynchronous scoring worker.
  - SQLAlchemy + Alembic persistence for applications, sessions, jobs, decisions,
    artifacts, idempotency, and outbox.
  - Outbox dispatch worker with pluggable backends (Kafka/SQS/Redis).
  - Worker reliability hardening:
      - Atomic scoring-claim semantics with lease expiry reclaim for multi-worker protection.
      - Exponential retry scheduling for scoring failures and outbox publish failures.
      - Dead-letter replay CLI tooling (`replay-scoring-jobs`, `replay-outbox`).
  - Security baseline:
      - DB-backed API key authentication (`X-API-Key` or Bearer).
      - Route-level role checks (`viewer`, `analyst`, `admin`).
      - Request rate limiting.
      - Audit logging for auth failures and privileged actions.
      - API key lifecycle endpoints (create/list/revoke/rotate).
      - Secret-manager bootstrap token support (AWS/GCP/Vault policy paths).
      - Startup provider-policy enforcement + `/secret-manager/ready`.
      - CI provider-policy matrix tests and deploy preflight script.
      - `deploy-preflight-gate.yml` blocks `release.yml` deployment path.
  - Security hardening completion:
      - Cloud-backed staging integration test workflow for provider policy
        (`secret-manager-staging-integration.yml`).
      - Dedicated non-prod release smoke workflow for helm/k8s/systemd paths
        (`nonprod-release-smoke.yml`).
      - Endpoint-level role ownership documented in API contracts + OpenAPI
        (`x-required-roles` annotations).
  - Model correctness completion:
      - Coherence superiority uncertainty now uses calibrated deterministic
        interval modeling (`fund-cs-superiority-v1`) instead of heuristic width.
      - Decision policy expanded toward `R(S, portfolio_state)` with
        portfolio-aware capacity/concentration/pressure adjustments.
  - Ops completeness completion:
      - Dedicated scoring-worker deploy assets added across systemd, k8s, and
        helm bundles (with HPA/PDB parity where applicable).
      - Worker telemetry snapshots now include queue depth, oldest latency, and
        failed/dead-letter counters with threshold-based warning tags.
      - Alerting hooks added for `/secret-manager/ready` and deploy preflight
        gate failures.
  - Calibration and policy tuning completion:
      - Added deterministic historical uncertainty calibration pipeline with
        profile generation (`calibrate-uncertainty` CLI command).
      - Runtime uncertainty profiles now support env/file overlays while
        preserving defaults and graceful fallback behavior.
      - Portfolio policy extended with richer `R(S, portfolio_state)` terms:
        domain USD concentration, liquidity reserve pressure, drawdown proxy,
        and regime-aware threshold deltas.
  - Centralized observability completion:
      - Worker telemetry now fans out to centralized sinks via a shared
        telemetry service (log + optional JSONL + optional Prometheus textfile).
      - Added SLO metric catalog and Grafana dashboard import artifact under
        `docs/ops/`.
  - Continuous calibration operations completion:

  - Reproducible decision artifact generator completion (Wave 3, prompt 07/20):
      - JSON Schema (Draft 2020-12, additionalProperties:false) with required
        artifact_id / artifact_kind="decision_artifact" / schema_version="1" /
        application_id / session_id / occurred_at / inputs_digest / scoring
        (composite + per_layer{contradiction,argumentation,embedding,
        compression,structural} + uncertainty{lower,upper} + scoring_version) /
        domain (DomainMix-shaped weights + normative_profile + schema_version
        + notes) / ontology_graph_id / ontology_graph_digest / decision
        (verdict pass|reject|manual_review + cs_superiority + cs_required +
        reason_codes + decision_policy_version) / pins (scoring_version +
        decision_policy_version + optional prompt_registry_digest):
        `server/fund/schemas/artifacts/decision_artifact.v1.json`.
      - Deterministic builder + persistence service:
        `server/fund/services/decision_artifact.py`
        (`build_decision_artifact`, `persist_decision_artifact`,
        `validate_artifact`, `canonical_artifact_bytes`,
        `DecisionArtifactValidationError`). The builder uses
        `json.dumps(sort_keys=True, separators=(",", ":"))` for the inputs
        SHA-256 digest and never reads wall-clock time — `occurred_at` comes
        from the application's authored timestamps. Verdict normalization
        maps internal `fail` to canonical `reject` to match the existing
        `decision_issued.v1` event enum.
      - `Artifact` table extended via Alembic migration
        `alembic/versions/20260417_000002_artifact_kind.py`:
        added `kind` column (server-default `"generic"` backfill) + index,
        added nullable `payload_json` column, relaxed `scoring_job_id` to
        nullable on non-SQLite dialects (SQLite uses ORM-side nullable=True
        because tests rebuild via `Base.metadata.create_all`). Migration is
        idempotent and uses `batch_alter_table` on SQLite for downgrade
        symmetry.
      - `server/fund/models.py`: `ArgumentArtifact` now carries `kind` (default
        `"generic"`) and optional `payload_json`; `scoring_job_id` is nullable.
      - Wired into worker path: after the decision is upserted in
        `process_next_scoring_job`, `application_service.py` builds the
        artifact via a deterministic `_build_artifact_app_state` helper
        (uses the application's `updated_at` timestamp, never wall-clock)
        and persists it before publishing the existing
        `DecisionIssued` event (which already carries the canonical summary
        fields cs_superiority/cs_required/decision_policy_version/
        scoring_version).
      - Tests: `tests/test_decision_artifact.py` (11 cases) covering
        schema-required-keys assertion, byte-identical determinism across
        two builds (canonical_artifact_bytes equal), inputs_digest changes
        when inputs change, happy-path schema validation, tampered-artifact
        rejection (missing `decision_policy_version`), unknown top-level
        key rejection, internal-`fail` -> canonical `reject` normalization,
        pins always include scoring_version + decision_policy_version,
        optional `prompt_registry_digest` round-trip, persisted row carries
        `kind="decision_artifact"`, and validation rejects bad artifacts
        before any DB write.
  - Portfolio state persistence + concentration policy completion (Wave 2, prompt 10/20):
      - New ORM models in `server/fund/models.py`:
        `PortfolioState(id, as_of [indexed], fund_nav_usd,
        liquidity_reserve_usd, drawdown_proxy ∈ [0,1], regime ∈
        {normal, stress, recovery}, optional note, created_at)` and
        `Position(id, application_id [indexed], domain [indexed],
        invested_usd, status ∈ {active, wound_down, exited} [indexed],
        created_at, updated_at)`. Strictly additive; existing models
        untouched.
      - Migration `alembic/versions/20260417_000003_portfolio_state.py`
        creates both tables idempotently with indexes on `as_of` and
        the composite `(domain, status)`; symmetric downgrade drops
        both. Safe under `Base.metadata.create_all` bootstrap.
      - Repository
        `server/fund/repositories/portfolio_repository.py` exposes
        `latest_state`, `latest_state_as_dict`,
        `active_positions_by_domain`, `active_positions_total`,
        `domain_concentration_by_nav`, `set_liquidity_reserve` (append-
        only, carries forward NAV/drawdown/regime), `record_state`,
        `record_position`. All writes are append-only; no trades,
        transfers, or live-ledger writes occur (matches prompt-10
        prohibitions).
      - `server/fund/services/decision_policy.py` introduces a
        `@runtime_checkable` Protocol `PortfolioStateProvider`,
        frozen dataclass `PortfolioSnapshot`, helper
        `portfolio_snapshot_from_repository` (duck-typed; no hard
        dependency on the repo module), and
        `snapshot_to_portfolio_state(snapshot, *, domain_primary)`
        which projects the persisted-state vocabulary
        (`normal | stress | recovery`) onto the legacy policy
        vocabulary (`neutral | stress | defensive | expansion`).
        `DecisionPolicyService.__init__` accepts an optional
        `portfolio_provider`; `evaluate(...)` accepts an optional
        kw-only `portfolio_snapshot` and resolves the effective state
        in this priority order: explicit `portfolio_state` mapping >
        explicit `portfolio_snapshot` > injected provider > pre-
        existing defaults. The legacy-envelope return shape is
        preserved verbatim when no source is active.
        `portfolio_adjustments` (when present) gains one new audit
        key, `portfolio_snapshot_source ∈ {explicit_mapping,
        explicit_snapshot, provider}`.
      - CLI `portfolio-state` subcommand group in `cli.py` with verbs
        `show` (latest snapshot + per-domain active USD totals + per-
        domain concentration as JSON) and `set-reserve --usd <amount>
        [--note ...]` (append-only snapshot row with reserve updated).
        Both verbs ensure the new tables exist on first call.
      - Tests: `tests/test_portfolio_state.py` (14 cases) covering
        Alembic upgrade→downgrade→upgrade round-trip on SQLite (using
        `command.stamp` to bypass an unrelated pre-existing migration
        that emits SQLite-incompatible DDL), repository write+read
        round-trip, append-only `set_liquidity_reserve` preserves
        prior rows, repository input validation, backward-compatibility
        envelope identity (`evaluate` with a no-op provider matches
        `evaluate` without one), provider snapshot routing into
        `portfolio_adjustments`, explicit `portfolio_state` overrides
        the provider, high domain-USD concentration measurably lifts
        `threshold_required` (≥0.005 with non-zero `r_domain_usd`
        audit term), `portfolio_snapshot_from_repository` reflects
        persisted state, `snapshot_to_portfolio_state(None) is None`,
        Protocol compliance via `isinstance`, and CLI smokes for
        `show` (empty DB), `set-reserve` then `show` round-trip, and
        negative-`--usd` rejection (exit 2).
      - Scope note: this prompt only adds persistence + provider
        plumbing and does not change any existing
        `R(S, portfolio_state)` term formulas or thresholds.
        `decision-policy-v1.0.0` and `decision-policy-v1.1.0` envelope
        rules from prompt 01 are preserved unchanged.
  - Red-team adversarial harness (Wave 5, prompt 13/20):
      - New `server/fund/services/red_team.py` exposes
        `run_adversarial_suite(fixtures_dir, labels_path, policy_version)`
        which replays a curated, labeled corpus of synthetic founder
        pitches through the production `ScoringService` +
        `DecisionPolicyService` chain (the same chain used by
        `ApplicationService.process_next_scoring_job`), canonicalizes the
        decision-policy `fail` -> `reject` translation, and returns a
        deterministic `RedTeamReport` (`schema_version=red-team-report-v1`)
        with per-case verdicts, `false_pass`/`false_reject`/`false_review`
        counters, and a 3 x 3 confusion matrix keyed by
        `expected_verdict` -> `actual_verdict`. Reports serialize via
        `to_canonical_bytes()` with sorted keys and fixed separators so
        consecutive runs are byte-identical (asserted by
        `test_report_is_byte_deterministic_across_runs`).
      - Adversarial corpus seeded under `tests/adversarial/`:
        12 fully synthetic JSON fixtures split 4 incoherent / 4 coherent
        + evidenced / 2 template-echo / 2 borderline (all named with
        invented brands such as Meridian Analytics, Orchid Care, Civic
        Beacon — no real founders / companies, no PII, no network
        dependencies), plus `labels.json` mapping each fixture to its
        ground-truth `expected_verdict` and rationale. Fixture loader
        validates required fields (`id`, `category`, `transcript_text`,
        `requested_check_usd`, `compliance_status`, ...) and rejects
        unknown categories or non-canonical verdict labels with
        operator-readable `RedTeamError` messages.
      - New CLI verb: `red-team-run --fixtures-dir <dir> --labels <file>
        [--output <file>] [--policy-version <pin>]`. Always writes the
        canonical JSON report to stdout; `--output` mirrors it to disk.
        Exit `0` when every fixture's actual verdict matches its label,
        `1` when at least one mismatch is recorded, `2` on fixture /
        labels load failure or `--policy-version` mismatch against the
        running `DECISION_POLICY_VERSION`.
      - Tests: `tests/test_red_team_harness.py` (19 cases) — pin the
        current confusion matrix
        (`{pass: {reject: 4}, reject: {reject: 4}, manual_review:
        {reject: 4}}`, totals: `matches=4`, `mismatches=8`,
        `false_reject=8`) as the regression baseline so any drift in
        the scoring stack, anti-gaming detector, decision-policy
        thresholds, or canonicalization fails loudly with a diff;
        verify fixture/label hygiene (>= 12 fixtures, all required
        categories present, every fixture has a label, every label
        verdict is canonical), exercise every `RedTeamError` path
        (missing dir, missing labels, policy-version pin mismatch,
        unlabeled fixture, unknown verdict), and shell out to the
        installed `python -m coherence_engine red-team-run` CLI three
        times to confirm exit-code semantics (`1` on the current
        mismatch baseline, `2` on missing fixtures dir + on policy-
        version pin mismatch, `0` when labels are aligned to the
        currently observed actual verdicts via a tmp-path
        `labels_aligned.json`).
      - Spec: new `docs/specs/red_team_harness.md` documents fixture
        authoring (required fields, categories, name/PII prohibitions),
        verdict vocabulary, per-case + aggregate report schema, CLI
        exit codes, determinism guarantees, and the explicit "bumping
        the pin" workflow for intentional behavior changes.
      - Scope note: this prompt only adds a regression harness + corpus
        + docs. No production scoring, decision-policy, or event-schema
        files were modified; the harness uses only the `tfidf` embedder
        + `heuristic` contradiction backend already configured by
        `ScoringService`, so the suite runs fully offline (per
        prompt 13 prohibition; intentionally NOT marked
        network-dependent).
  - Shadow-mode evaluation + scoring_mode enforcement (Wave 4, prompt 12/20):
      - New per-application `scoring_mode ∈ {"enforce", "shadow"}` column on
        `Application` (String(16), NOT NULL, server_default "enforce"). Existing
        rows retain production behavior via the default; the ORM and the new
        Alembic migration both hold this invariant.
      - Alembic migration `alembic/versions/20260417_000004_scoring_mode.py`
        (revision `20260417_000004`, down_revision `20260417_000003`) adds the
        column idempotently — it is a no-op when the column already exists
        (e.g. when the schema was bootstrapped via
        `Base.metadata.create_all`) — and uses `batch_alter_table` on
        downgrade for SQLite compatibility.
      - `ApplicationService.process_next_scoring_job` now branches on the
        application's `scoring_mode`:
          * In `enforce` mode, behavior is unchanged — the decision
            artifact is persisted with `kind="decision_artifact"` and
            the `DecisionIssued` outbox event carries `mode="enforce"`.
          * In `shadow` mode, the pipeline still builds + validates the
            same deterministic `decision_artifact.v1` bundle via
            `build_decision_artifact(...)` but persists it with
            `kind="shadow_decision_artifact"` through a new
            `_persist_shadow_decision_artifact` helper (same schema
            validation and canonical serialization as
            `persist_decision_artifact`). The `DecisionIssued` event is
            tagged with `mode="shadow"`, and any founder-facing
            notification side effects (e.g. `FounderNotified` in the
            transcript-rejection path) are suppressed.
      - `ApplicationService.create_escalation_packet` refuses partner
        escalation packets for shadow-mode applications with
        `escalation_forbidden_in_shadow_mode` — shadow replays must
        never cause partner-facing side effects.
      - New `ApplicationService.set_scoring_mode(application_id, *,
        new_mode, force=False)` method: validates the target mode
        (`enforce`|`shadow`), treats same-mode as a no-op (idempotent),
        and refuses `enforce -> shadow` after a decision has already
        been issued unless `force=True`. `shadow -> enforce` (the
        prompt's "promote after review" flow) is always allowed and
        never retroactively hides past behavior.
      - `server/fund/services/event_publisher.py` now exports scoring-
        mode vocabulary used by callers and tests:
        `SCORING_MODE_ENFORCE`, `SCORING_MODE_SHADOW`,
        `tag_payload_with_mode(payload, mode)` (shallow-copies and
        attaches `"mode"`, raising `ValueError` on unknown values), and
        `is_shadow_event_payload(payload)` (returns True iff the
        payload was tagged `mode="shadow"`).
      - Event schema `server/fund/schemas/events/decision_issued.v1.json`
        gains an OPTIONAL `mode` property
        (`enum = ["enforce", "shadow"]`, default `"enforce"`). It is
        NOT added to the `required` array, so previously emitted
        events (pre-prompt-12) remain valid — backward-compatible by
        construction.
      - New CLI verb: `application set-mode
        --application-id <id> --mode enforce|shadow [--force]`. Opens
        a short-lived DB session, applies the transition via
        `ApplicationService.set_scoring_mode`, commits, and prints the
        resulting JSON (application_id, previous_mode, new_mode,
        changed). Exits `2` on validation failure (missing
        application, forbidden enforce->shadow without `--force`,
        unknown mode).
      - Tests: `tests/test_shadow_mode.py` (22 cases) cover column
        default + explicit shadow persistence, `tag_payload_with_mode`
        / `is_shadow_event_payload` helpers, all six
        `set_scoring_mode` transition branches (enforce->shadow
        pre-decision allowed, no-op, enforce->shadow post-decision
        forbidden without force, forbidden path succeeds with force,
        shadow->enforce always allowed, bad mode + missing
        application), end-to-end worker runs proving that shadow
        applications yield a `shadow_decision_artifact` row (and NOT a
        production `decision_artifact` row), emit a `DecisionIssued`
        event with `mode="shadow"`, do NOT enqueue any
        `FounderNotified` event, and block
        `create_escalation_packet` with the dedicated error; plus CLI
        smokes for happy-path transition, forbidden transition exit
        code 2, `--force` override, missing-application exit code 2,
        and a shadow->enforce round trip.
      - Prohibitions honored: `decision_issued` event was NOT renamed
        or dropped (schema received only a new OPTIONAL field);
        enforce-mode notification side effects are NOT silently
        swallowed (the shadow-mode suppression is gated exclusively on
        `scoring_mode == "shadow"` and the path is covered by a
        dedicated test); and only files listed in SCOPE were modified
        (plus `decision_issued.v1.json`, which the step-by-step
        explicitly directs as a normative update — the SCOPE list
        omitted it).
  - Historical backtest pipeline completion (Wave 4, prompt 11/20):
      - New offline, deterministic replay service at
        `server/fund/services/backtest.py`. Exposes
        `@dataclass(frozen=True) BacktestConfig` (dataset_path,
        decision_policy_version pin, portfolio_snapshot_path,
        output_path, seed, requested_check_usd, domain_default),
        `@dataclass(frozen=True) BacktestReport` (schema_version
        `backtest-report-v1`, aggregates, reliability_curve, domain
        breakdown, per-row results), `BacktestRowResult`,
        `ReliabilityBin`, `BacktestError`,
        `load_portfolio_snapshot(path)` helper, and the public entry
        point `run_backtest(config) -> BacktestReport`.
      - For each row the service rebuilds the 95% calibrated
        superiority interval via
        `calibrated_superiority_interval_95(...)` and hands a
        synthetic `application` + `score_record` to the current
        `DecisionPolicyService.evaluate(...)` using a **fixed**
        `PortfolioSnapshot` loaded from
        `config.portfolio_snapshot_path`. The live portfolio_state /
        positions tables are never queried, satisfying the prompt-11
        "fixed snapshot" prohibition.
      - Report metrics: verdict counts/rates
        (`pass_rate`, `reject_rate`, `manual_review_rate`),
        Brier score on a `outcome_superiority > 0` binary
        realization, 10-bin equal-width reliability curve with
        closed-right final bin, `mean_predicted_minus_realized`
        signed delta, and a deterministic per-domain breakdown.
        `BacktestReport.to_canonical_bytes()` serializes via
        `json.dumps(..., sort_keys=True, separators=(",", ":"))`
        with a trailing `\n`, so two runs over the same dataset +
        snapshot emit byte-identical bytes (enforced by test).
      - CLI: new `backtest-run` subcommand in `cli.py` with args
        `--dataset`, `--policy-version`, `--portfolio-snapshot`,
        `--output`, `--seed`, `--requested-check-usd`,
        `--domain-default`. Exits `2` on dataset validation failure
        (reusing `validate_historical_outcomes_export`) or on
        `decision_policy_version` pin mismatch; `0` on success, with
        the canonical report bytes written to stdout (and to
        `--output` when supplied).
      - Thin deploy wrapper at `deploy/scripts/run_backtest.py`
        (same `sys.path` parent inclusion as
        `merge_governed_historical_outcomes.py`).
      - Fixtures: `tests/fixtures/backtest/mini_dataset.jsonl` (10
        curated governed-format rows across three domains:
        `market_economics`, `public_health`, `governance`) and
        `tests/fixtures/backtest/snapshot.json` (a fixed
        `PortfolioSnapshot` covering NAV, reserve, drawdown, regime,
        per-domain invested USD).
      - Tests: `tests/test_backtest.py` (18 cases) covering dataset
        + snapshot fixture sanity, snapshot loader happy/error
        paths, report shape + metric ranges + reliability-bin count,
        byte-identical report bytes on repeated runs, SHA256 digest
        stability, Brier-score sensitivity (midpoint flip → Brier
        unchanged; high-predicted row flipped negative → Brier rises
        by the expected `ΔP²/N ≈ 0.030` on this dataset; asymmetric
        flip → directional change), policy-version-pin and invalid-
        row rejection, output-path file write, dataset immutability
        under replay, and CLI smokes for happy path (stdout ==
        file), invalid dataset (exit 2), and policy-version
        mismatch (exit 2).
      - Spec: `docs/specs/backtest_spec.md` documents inputs,
        outputs, metric definitions (including the
        `predicted_probability = clamp((CS+1)/2, 0, 1)` affine map
        and the 10-bin reliability-curve convention), CLI contract,
        and the reproducibility + no-network + no-live-read
        prohibitions.
      - Prohibitions honored: no network I/O, no writes to
        `data/governed/*` on the backtest path, and the live
        portfolio state is never read (always loaded from
        `--portfolio-snapshot`). No files outside SCOPE were
        modified.
  - Anti-gaming detector integration completion (Wave 2, prompt 09/20):
      - Deterministic, offline, lexical/numeric detector at
        `core/anti_gaming.py` producing `AntiGamingReport(score, flags,
        metrics)` where the clean-convention `score ∈ [0.0, 1.0]` (1.0 =
        clean, 0.0 = heavily gamed). Five signals with documented
        weights: `AG_TEMPLATE_OVERLAP` (0.30, char-trigram Jaccard vs
        `templates` > 0.6), `AG_PRIOR_CORPUS_ECHO` (0.25, char-trigram
        Jaccard vs `prior_corpus` > 0.8), `AG_REPETITIVE_FILLER` (0.20,
        mean pairwise length-normalized sublinear-TF cosine > 0.85 —
        stdlib-only, no sklearn), `AG_FLUENCY_WITHOUT_CONTENT` (0.15,
        ratio of long-complex to metric/numeric-bearing propositions
        > 3.0), `AG_CONTRADICTION_DENIAL` (0.25, per-sentence negation
        and content repetition without a concession marker). No ML
        dependencies added; all imports are stdlib.
      - Integrated into `core/scorer.py` behind a new keyword-only flag
        `anti_gaming: bool = True` on `CoherenceScorer.score(...)`, with
        optional `prior_corpus`/`templates` kwargs (defaults `()` for
        backward-compatible single-arg calls). Composite becomes
        `raw_composite * (0.5 + 0.5 * anti_gaming_score)` — a clean
        score leaves the composite unchanged and a worst-case score
        halves it. `CoherenceResult.metadata` now carries
        `raw_composite_score`, `anti_gaming_score`, `anti_gaming_flags`,
        and `anti_gaming_metrics`. The early-return path for
        n_propositions < 2 also fills these fields with clean defaults.
      - `server/fund/services/scoring.py` sources `anti_gaming_score`
        from the detector instead of the previous contradiction-count
        heuristic and adds `anti_gaming_flags` / `anti_gaming_metrics`
        to the returned dict; the canonical sign convention now matches
        the detector (1.0 = clean).
      - Fixtures at `tests/fixtures/anti_gaming/` (clean.json,
        template_echo.json, repetitive.json).
      - Tests: `tests/test_anti_gaming.py` (12 cases) covering the
        clean fixture (no flags, score == 1.0), `AG_TEMPLATE_OVERLAP`
        trigger on template echo, `AG_REPETITIVE_FILLER` trigger on
        the repetitive fixture, `AG_PRIOR_CORPUS_ECHO` trigger on an
        explicit prior-corpus echo, empty-proposition clean default,
        determinism across repeated calls, bounded-penalty property
        (composite >= 0.5*raw), clean pitch preserves composite via
        multiplier of 1.0, `anti_gaming=False` disables the penalty
        and records clean defaults, flag-weight shape invariant, and
        `ScoringService` return dict pass-through.
  - Prompt registry with SHA pinning completion (Wave 1, prompt 08/20):
      - Versioned registry at `data/prompts/registry.json`
        (schema_version `prompt-registry-v1`) pointing at two seed bodies
        (`data/prompts/bodies/interview_opening.v1.md` and
        `data/prompts/bodies/self_critique.v1.md`). Each entry carries
        `id`, semver `version`, `status` in {draft, shadow, prod},
        `body_path`, lowercase hex `content_sha256` over raw on-disk bytes,
        and `owner`. Prompt bodies are never embedded inline.
      - Service module
        `server/fund/services/prompt_registry.py`:
        `load_registry`, `verify_registry` (returns
        `VerificationReport(ok, mismatches, missing)`), `registry_digest`
        (stable SHA-256 over sorted `(id, version, content_sha256)` tuples;
        order-insensitive across declaration order), `resolve`,
        `default_registry_path`, dataclasses `PromptEntry`, `Registry`,
        `Mismatch`, `VerificationReport`, and a `PromptRegistryError`
        type. Loader enforces `schema_version`, required keys, allowed
        statuses, and `(id, version)` uniqueness.
      - CLI subcommand group `prompt-registry` with verbs `list`, `verify`,
        `digest` (all accept `--registry <path>`; `list`/`verify` accept
        `--json`). Exit code 2 on verification failure, matching the
        parity convention set by `validate-historical-export`. The
        `digest` output is the exact value intended for the
        `pins.prompt_registry_digest` slot in `decision_artifact.v1`.
      - Spec: `docs/specs/prompt_registry.md` (schema, digest semantics,
        lifecycle draft -> shadow -> prod, CLI table, invariants).
      - Tests: `tests/test_prompt_registry.py` (17 cases) covering
        load/parse, happy-path `verify` OK, body-mutation detection,
        missing-body reporting, digest determinism, digest
        order-insensitivity, digest changes when a body SHA changes,
        `resolve` hit/miss, schema/status/duplicate rejection, the
        shipped registry self-verifying out of the box, and three CLI
        subprocess smokes (`verify` exit 0, `list` prints all entries,
        `digest` prints a valid hex sha256, and `verify` exit 2 on a
        tampered fixture).

CURRENT GAPS / NOT YET COMPLETE
-------------------------------

  - Production export extraction now has deterministic tooling (CLI + deploy
    script) but the operator must still provide two inputs: (a) CoherenceScored
    event payloads extracted from the production outbox, and (b) an outcomes
    annotation file mapping each `application_id` to its observed
    `outcome_superiority`. The enriched `CoherenceScored` event includes all
    calibration fields going forward; legacy events without `n_contradictions`
    use a best-effort derivation from `anti_gaming_score`.
  - Enrollment coverage, webhook receipts, and tracker handoff governance
    reports surface drift and delivery evidence in CI; operators must keep
    secret-backed expected repo lists, routing maps, and live webhook targets
    aligned with production policy.
  - Write-back enriches local markdown artifacts in the Actions bundle; it does
    not mutate external tracker issues automatically.


NEXT-STAGE PRIORITIES (ORDERED)
-------------------------------

A) Governed calibration operations
   - Production → export extraction is now wired via
     `uncertainty-profile export-historical-outcomes` + deploy script.
     Operators extract CoherenceScored event payloads, provide an outcomes
     annotation file (`application_id → outcome_superiority`), and the tool
     emits rows matching `deploy/ops/uncertainty-historical-outcomes-export.example.json`.
   - Validate each output batch with `validate-historical-export` /
     `validate_historical_outcomes_export.py` before merge; hosted
     recalibration CI also runs the strict example check (workflow + `Makefile`).
   - Merge with `merge-historical-dataset` / `merge_governed_historical_outcomes.py`.

B) Governance / on-call operations hygiene
   - Use `deploy/scripts/report_governance_ops_hygiene_review.py` on downloaded
     artifact JSON for each review cycle; rotate secrets/maps when routing or
     enrollment policy changes (see reminder lines in generated Markdown).

C) Documentation integrity (mandatory process)
   - Keep `COHERENCE_ENGINE_PROJECT_STATUS.txt` and
     `COHERENCE_ENGINE_CONTINUATION_PROMPT.txt` synchronized after every major
     implementation step.
   - When an item is implemented, remove it from "next work" and move it into
     "implemented snapshot" with concise evidence.

OPERATIONS QUICK COMMANDS
-------------------------

Run fund API:
  python -m coherence_engine serve-fund --host 0.0.0.0 --port 8010

Run migrations:
  alembic upgrade head

Run scoring worker:
  python -m coherence_engine process-scoring-jobs --run-mode loop

Run outbox dispatcher:
  python -m coherence_engine dispatch-outbox --backend redis --run-mode loop --redis-url redis://localhost:6379/0

Run all tests:
  python -m pytest tests/ -v

Run uncertainty calibration on historical records:
  python -m coherence_engine calibrate-uncertainty ./path/to/historical_records.json --output ./uncertainty_profile.json

Verify governed dataset checksum:
  python -m coherence_engine uncertainty-profile verify-dataset --dataset data/governed/uncertainty_historical_outcomes.jsonl --manifest data/governed/uncertainty_historical_outcomes.manifest.json

Merge reviewed outcome exports into governed JSONL + refresh manifest (run with repo parent on PYTHONPATH if not installed):
  python -m coherence_engine uncertainty-profile merge-historical-dataset --dataset data/governed/uncertainty_historical_outcomes.jsonl --incoming ./artifacts/new_outcomes.jsonl --output data/governed/uncertainty_historical_outcomes.jsonl --manifest-out data/governed/uncertainty_historical_outcomes.manifest.json

Same via deploy script (adds repo parent to sys.path):
  python deploy/scripts/merge_governed_historical_outcomes.py --dataset data/governed/uncertainty_historical_outcomes.jsonl --incoming ./artifacts/new_outcomes.jsonl --output data/governed/uncertainty_historical_outcomes.jsonl --manifest-out data/governed/uncertainty_historical_outcomes.manifest.json

Validate export JSON/JSONL before merge (PYTHONPATH = parent of repo folder if needed):
  python -m coherence_engine uncertainty-profile validate-historical-export --input ./artifacts/new_outcomes.jsonl

Validate with strict five layer keys:
  python deploy/scripts/validate_historical_outcomes_export.py --input ./artifacts/new_outcomes.jsonl --require-standard-layer-keys

Strict example parity with recalibration CI (committed fixture + five layer keys):
  make validate-historical-export-example

Export governed historical outcome rows from scored events + outcomes annotation file (production → export):
  python -m coherence_engine uncertainty-profile export-historical-outcomes --scored-events ./artifacts/scored_events.json --outcomes ./artifacts/outcomes.json --output ./artifacts/export.json --require-standard-layer-keys

Same via deploy script:
  python deploy/scripts/export_historical_outcomes.py --scored-events ./artifacts/scored_events.json --outcomes ./artifacts/outcomes.json --output ./artifacts/export.json

Governance / on-call ops hygiene review bundle (local; optional artifact paths):
  python deploy/scripts/report_governance_ops_hygiene_review.py --json-out ./artifacts/governance_ops_hygiene_review.json --markdown-out ./artifacts/governance_ops_hygiene_review.md

Promote uncertainty profile to stage:
  python -m coherence_engine uncertainty-profile promote --registry ./artifacts/uncertainty_profile_registry.json --stage shadow --profile ./artifacts/uncertainty_candidate_profile.json --reason "weekly recalibration"

Rollback stage uncertainty profile:
  python -m coherence_engine uncertainty-profile rollback --registry ./artifacts/uncertainty_profile_registry.json --stage shadow

Promote stage with governance policy gates:

Evaluate uncertainty candidate governance gates:

RECENT CHANGES — 2026-04-25 (Wave 16, prompt 64/70)
---------------------------------------------------

Chaos test harness — DB failover, Redis flap, S3 outage, worker death
mid-job. The harness runs locally against a docker-compose topology;
it is intentionally NOT part of default CI (cost + flakiness make
per-PR live runs unviable). CI exercises only the dry-run path; live
runs are gated behind ``CHAOS=1`` and run by hand or on a nightly cron.

Files created:

* ``deploy/chaos/docker-compose.yml`` -- Postgres primary + replica,
  Redis, MinIO (S3-compatible), scoring worker, API. Service names
  are stable so chaos scenarios can refer to them by name; volumes
  are anonymous so ``docker compose down -v`` returns the topology
  to a clean slate between scenarios.

* ``deploy/chaos/run_scenario.py`` -- the runner. Reads a
  ``chaos-scenario-v1`` YAML, validates it structurally, then either
  exits 0 (``--dry-run``) or applies each perturbation via
  ``docker compose stop|start|pause|unpause`` (or ``tc qdisc`` for
  partitions), runs the synthetic workload, and evaluates every
  declared post-condition. Refuses live mode without ``CHAOS=1``
  (exit 3). The validator enforces the determinism contract by
  rejecting any scenario that omits the
  ``byte_identical_artifact_replay`` post-condition.

* ``deploy/chaos/scenarios/db_primary_failover.yaml`` -- ``docker
  stop`` + ``start`` the Postgres primary; assert no orphaned scoring
  jobs, idempotency intact, byte-identical artifact replay, end-to-end
  within 60s SLO.

* ``deploy/chaos/scenarios/redis_flap.yaml`` -- two
  ``pause`` / ``unpause`` cycles on Redis; assert ARQ enqueue retries
  collapse to one job per submission, byte-identical replay,
  end-to-end within 90s.

* ``deploy/chaos/scenarios/s3_outage.yaml`` -- ``docker stop`` MinIO
  for 8 seconds; assert object-storage writes fail retryable (not
  terminal), in-flight retries succeed on resume, byte-identical
  replay, end-to-end within 120s.

* ``deploy/chaos/scenarios/worker_death_mid_job.yaml`` -- ``docker
  stop`` (SIGTERM, never SIGKILL — prompt-30 prohibition) the
  scoring worker; assert the visibility-timeout reaper promotes
  stale ``in_progress`` rows to ``queued`` exactly once,
  byte-identical replay, end-to-end within 90s.

* ``tests/chaos/test_chaos_harness_dry_run.py`` -- 10 assertions:
  the shipped scenario inventory is exactly the four expected
  files; every shipped scenario passes schema validation AND
  declares the determinism contract; ``run_scenario(... dry_run=
  True)`` exits 0 and writes a stable JSON report; the CLI
  ``--dry-run`` path exits 0; four negative-validation cases
  (bad schema_version, missing determinism contract, unknown
  perturbation action, non-mapping doc, zero SLO); the ``CHAOS=1``
  refusal path returns 3 when the env var is unset.

* ``docs/ops/chaos.md`` -- operator-facing reference: when to run
  scenarios, the ``make chaos`` wiring play, the YAML schema, the
  post-condition output shape, the per-failure remediation table,
  and the load-bearing prohibitions.

Verification markers (grep):

* ``deploy/chaos/docker-compose.yml`` : ``services:|postgres|redis``
* ``deploy/chaos/run_scenario.py`` : ``def run_scenario\b|perturbation``
* ``docs/ops/chaos.md`` : ``chaos|failover|partition``
* ``tests/chaos/test_chaos_harness_dry_run.py`` : ``scenario|dry_run``

Run the focused suite with::

  python3 -m pytest -p no:pytest-qt \
    coherence_engine/tests/chaos/test_chaos_harness_dry_run.py -v
  → 10 passed.

Prompt 64 prohibitions honored:

* Chaos NOT in default CI: ``run_scenario.py`` returns exit 3 unless

RECENT CHANGES — 2026-04-25 (Wave 16, prompt 63/70)
---------------------------------------------------

SLO dashboards (Grafana JSON exports) + error-budget burn alerts.

Defines four user-visible SLOs and the multi-window / multi-burn-rate
alerting plumbing that backs them. SLO numbers, burn-rate windows, and
severity routing all live in ``docs/ops/slos.md`` so a future change
to a target updates the recording rules, alert rules, and dashboards
from one anchor.

SLO catalog (target / window):

* ``SLO_avail`` — 99.5% of ``POST /api/v1/applications`` requests
  succeed (non-5xx) over a 30d rolling window.
* ``SLO_latency`` — pipeline P95 ≤ 30s end-to-end (intake → notify),
  bad event = stage warn fired on the ``notify`` stage.
* ``SLO_scoring_success`` — ≥ 99% of scoring jobs succeed
  (``coherence_fund_pipeline_stage_events_total{stage="score",
  status="success"}`` over total).
* ``SLO_calibration_freshness`` — drift report regenerated ≤ 24h
  (event-based; single ticket alert when age > 86400s for 30m).

Files created:

* ``deploy/prometheus/recording_rules.yaml`` -- group
  ``coherence_fund_slo_recording_rules`` materializes per-SLO
  ``error_ratio`` at 5m / 30m / 1h / 2h / 6h / 24h / 72h plus the
  good_events / valid_events pair at 5m for each ratio-based SLO.
  ``coherence_fund:slo_calibration:age_seconds`` carries the freshness
  signal.

* ``deploy/prometheus/alert_rules.yaml`` -- two groups:
  ``coherence_fund_slo_burn_rate_alerts`` defines four burn-rate
  alerts per ratio-based SLO at burn rates {14.4, 6, 3, 1} joining
  long/short window pairs (1h/5m, 6h/30m, 24h/2h, 72h/6h);
  ``coherence_fund_slo_calibration_alerts`` emits the single
  ``CoherenceFundCalibrationStale`` ticket alert. Severity routing is
  enforced by a test: 14.4 + 6 → ``severity=critical`` (page);
  3 + 1 → ``severity=warning`` (ticket, never page).

* ``deploy/grafana/dashboards/decision_pipeline.json`` -- SLO_avail
  + SLO_latency compliance gauges, calibration-freshness stat, a
  burn-rate-window timeseries pair, a per-stage failure ratio
  table. Schema 38, ``editable: false`` so dashboards stay
  source-controlled.

* ``deploy/grafana/dashboards/scoring_layers.json`` -- SLO_scoring
  gauge + burn-rate windows, scoring queue depth + DLQ, per-stage
  last-tick duration, scoring tick throughput.

* ``deploy/grafana/dashboards/cost_telemetry.json`` -- daily cost
  stat, top-N applications by cost, daily-budget headroom gauge,
  budget-exceeded event rate.

* ``docs/ops/slos.md`` -- single source of truth for SLO numbers,
  burn-rate table, severity routing table, dashboard inventory,
  reference back to the Google SRE workbook chapter 5.

* ``tests/test_grafana_json_validity.py`` -- 19 assertions: each
  dashboard parses as JSON, has ``schemaVersion >= 38``, has the
  expected ``uid``, has the contractual panel IDs, has
  ``editable: false``, ends with LF + trailing newline (deterministic
  diff guard), and (for ``decision_pipeline.json``) references the
  SLO recording rules rather than raw metrics.

* ``tests/test_prometheus_rules_validity.py`` -- 9 structural
  assertions + 2 lazy ``promtool check rules`` invocations that
  skip with a clear message if ``promtool`` is not on PATH.
  Structural assertions: each declared SLO has a recording rule for
  every burn-rate long window; each ratio-based SLO has exactly four
  burn-rate alerts at {14.4, 6, 3, 1}; severity routing matches
  ``critical`` for 14.4/6 and ``warning`` for 3/1; alert exprs join
  the recording-rule layer (never a raw metric threshold);
  calibration-freshness alert is ticket-only.

RECENT CHANGES — 2026-04-25 (Wave 16, prompt 62/70)
---------------------------------------------------

Per-application cost telemetry + budget alerts. Every paid external
call (LLM tokens, STT minutes, embeddings, Twilio voice minutes,
Stripe fees) now lands in the new ``fund_cost_events`` table with a
unit-cost derived from the governed YAML pricing registry, NEVER from
a code constant. Per-application and per-day rollups feed two budget
checks that emit a ``cost_budget_exceeded.v1`` outbox event when a
configured cap is crossed -- once per cooldown window per scope, so a
runaway counter cannot page on every tick.

Files added:
  - NEW  alembic/versions/20260425_000017_cost_events.py
         Creates ``fund_cost_events`` (with indexes on
         application_id / provider / sku / occurred_at and a unique
         index on idempotency_key) and ``fund_cost_alert_state``
         (with a unique index on (scope, scope_key) for the cooldown
         lookup). Downgrade is symmetric.
  - NEW  data/governed/cost_pricing.yaml
         ``schema_version: cost-pricing-v1``. Per-SKU price table for
         Deepgram/AssemblyAI/Whisper STT, OpenAI embeddings, GPT-4o
         + Claude Sonnet LLMs, Twilio voice (inbound/outbound/
         recording), and Stripe Connect payout fees. Operator
         obligation: changes go through governance review.
  - NEW  server/fund/services/cost_pricing.py
         ``load_pricing_registry()`` reads + validates the YAML
         (schema-version pin, no negative prices, no duplicate SKUs),
         caches per-path. ``get_price(sku)`` raises
         ``CostPricingError`` on an unknown SKU. ``reset_pricing_cache``
         is the test escape hatch.
  - NEW  server/fund/services/cost_telemetry.py
         ``record_cost(db, *, provider, sku, units, application_id,
         idempotency_key)`` -- derives ``unit_cost_usd`` + ``total_usd``
         from the pricing table, writes a ``CostEvent`` row, and
         returns ``RecordedCost`` with a ``created`` flag so the
         caller can distinguish a fresh insert from an idempotent
         replay. ``compute_idempotency_key`` is the canonical
         ``sha256(provider|sku|application_id|discriminator)``.
         ``sum_application_total_usd`` and ``sum_daily_total_usd``
         are the rollup helpers consumed by the alert service and
         the partner-dashboard cost view.
  - NEW  server/fund/services/cost_alerts.py
         ``check_application_budget(application_id)`` and
         ``check_daily_budget()`` -- compare the rollup against
         ``MAX_COST_PER_APPLICATION_USD`` /
         ``MAX_COST_PER_DAY_USD`` (env defaults: $50 and $500),
         emit ``cost_budget_exceeded.v1`` when over, suppress
         duplicate emits inside the
         ``COST_ALERT_COOLDOWN_HOURS`` (default 24h) window via the
         ``fund_cost_alert_state`` ledger. Returns an
         ``AlertDecision`` dataclass that surfaces both
         ``alert_emitted`` and ``cooldown_active`` so callers can
         distinguish "emitted now" from "blocked by cooldown".
  - NEW  server/fund/schemas/events/cost_budget_exceeded.v1.json
         Draft 2020-12 schema -- envelope + scope (application |
         daily) + scope_key + budget_usd + total_usd + cooldown_hours.
         ``additionalProperties: false`` so a forward-incompatible
         payload fails strict validation.
  - NEW  tests/test_cost_telemetry.py
         15 tests, all green: pricing registry load + unknown-SKU
         failure; ``record_cost`` derives total from YAML; idempotency
         returns the same row twice; negative units rejected;
         multi-SKU per-application rollup; per-UTC-day rollup;
         under-threshold check emits nothing; over-threshold emits
         exactly one ``cost_budget_exceeded`` event; the cooldown
         blocks a second emit (test-asserts a single outbox row);
         ``voice_intake.finalize_session`` records exactly one
         Twilio CostEvent for the session; webhook redeliver does
         not produce a second row.
  - NEW  docs/specs/cost_telemetry.md
         Operator-facing reference -- data model, pricing-registry
         contract, public API, env-var table, prompt-62 prohibitions
         (no client-supplied units, no alerts without cooldown, no
         hardcoded pricing).
  - MOD  server/fund/models.py
         New ``CostEvent`` and ``CostAlertState`` ORM models matching
         the migration above.
  - MOD  server/fund/services/scoring.py
         New ``record_scoring_cost(db, application_id, score_output)``
         helper -- estimates 1k-token buckets from
         ``score_output['input_text']`` length (server-derived, NEVER
         from a client) and writes a ``CostEvent`` for the embedding
         call. SKU defaults to ``openai.text-embedding-3-small.tokens``;
         pricing-misconfig is logged-and-skipped, never fatal.
  - MOD  server/fund/services/stt/router.py
         New ``record_stt_cost(db, application_id, result,
         duration_seconds, discriminator)`` helper -- maps the
         resolved STT provider to a registry SKU
         (``STT_PROVIDER_TO_SKU``) and writes a ``CostEvent`` whose
         units are computed from the *recorded* duration (NEVER a
         client-supplied minute count).
  - MOD  server/fund/services/voice_intake.py
         ``finalize_session`` now records exactly one Twilio voice
         CostEvent per session, units = sum of stored
         ``InterviewRecording.duration_seconds`` / 60. Discriminator
         combines session id with provider call SID so a webhook
         retry collapses to one row.
  - MOD  COHERENCE_ENGINE_PROJECT_STATUS.txt
         Header rolled to prompt 62; this change block.
  - MOD  COHERENCE_ENGINE_CONTINUATION_PROMPT.txt
         Prompt 62 promoted to MOST RECENT PROMPT; prompt 61
         demoted to SUPERSEDED.

RECENT CHANGES — 2026-04-25 (Wave 15, prompt 60/70)
---------------------------------------------------

Quarterly Model-Risk-Management report generator (informed by, not
legally compliant with, OCC / Fed SR 11-7). The engine now ships a
deterministic assembler that consolidates every governance surface
into one quarterly PDF: model purpose & limitations, validation
study summaries, calibration drift, override frequency by partner,
anti-gaming alert rates, decision reproducibility audits, known
weaknesses, and a remediation backlog. The disclaimer string is
rendered verbatim into every report so no compliance claim is
implied.

  • ``server/fund/services/model_risk_report.py`` —
    ``QuarterRef`` (strict ``YYYYQN`` parser; ``parse('2026Q5')``
    raises). ``MRMReportInputs`` carries the quarter and optional
    paths to each source artifact. ``assemble_quarterly_report`` is
    the deterministic entry point: same inputs → byte-identical
    canonical bytes via ``MRMReportData.to_canonical_bytes``. PII is
    aggregated only — partner IDs are hashed with a stable salt
    (``_PARTNER_HASH_SALT``); override ``reason_text`` never appears
    in the report. A missing source path produces an empty section
    rather than aborting, so an early quarter without (say) anti-
    gaming telemetry still produces a runnable PDF — empty sections
    render as ``(no data this quarter)``.

  • ``server/fund/services/model_risk_renderer_pdf.py`` —
    ``render_tex(data)`` is a pure function from ``MRMReportData`` to
    a deterministic ``.tex`` source string; ``render_pdf(data)`` runs
    ``pdflatex`` twice in a fresh ``tempfile.TemporaryDirectory`` so
    concurrent renders cannot interfere, captures the ``.log`` for
    debug, and returns ``(pdf_bytes, log_text, pages)``. Failures
    surface as ``PdflatexNotInstalled`` (binary missing) or
    ``PdflatexRenderError`` (compilation failed; ``log_text``
    attached).

  • ``data/governed/model_risk/templates/quarterly.tex.j2`` — Jinja2
    template using square-bracket delimiters (``[[ … ]]`` and
    ``[% … %]``) so curly braces stay free for LaTeX. Uses
    ``lmodern`` + ``microtype`` per the existing Guides convention;
    sections for purpose, limitations, validation summary, drift
    indicators, override stats, anti-gaming, reproducibility, known
    weaknesses, and remediation. The first 12 hex chars of the
    ``input_digest`` are stamped into the page header so reviewers
    can tell two PDFs apart at a glance.

  • ``data/governed/model_risk/backlog.yaml`` — source of truth for
    the qualitative content (model purpose, limitations, known
    weaknesses, remediation backlog). Edit the YAML and regenerate;
    the ``input_digest`` will change and reviewers comparing two
    PDFs of the same quarter can see that.

  • ``cli.py`` — two new subcommands.
    ``mrm-report generate --quarter 2026Q2 --output report.pdf``
    assembles + renders. Optional flags wire each source artifact
    (``--validation-study``, ``--drift-telemetry``,
    ``--override-stats``, ``--anti-gaming-stats``,
    ``--reproducibility-audit``); ``--tex-only`` skips pdflatex and
    writes raw ``.tex``; ``--log-output`` captures the ``.log``.
    ``mrm-report publish --pdf <p> --quarter <q>`` uploads the PDF
    to object storage at key
    ``model_risk/<quarter>/report.pdf`` and emits an
    ``mrm_report_published`` outbox event with the storage URI,
    sha256, size, and actor.

  • ``tests/test_model_risk_report.py`` (17 tests, all green) —
    covers ``QuarterRef`` round-trip + 7 malformed-input
    parametrizations, end-to-end assembly with the seed backlog,
    determinism of canonical bytes (``test_assemble_quarterly_report
    _deterministic_canonical_bytes``), .tex byte-determinism
    (``test_render_tex_is_deterministic`` — the cheapest signal of
    accidental drift), missing-source handling, LaTeX special-char
    escaping, real PDF generation against a synthetic fixture
    (skipped if ``pdflatex`` is not on PATH; emits a loud warning so
    a no-TeX CI environment cannot silently lose coverage), and the
    ``PdflatexNotInstalled`` path via monkeypatch.

  • ``docs/specs/model_risk_management.md`` — pipeline diagram,
    component tour, determinism contract, operator runbook
    (generate + publish + edit-the-backlog), and an explicit
    "informed by, not compliant with SR 11-7" framing.

Verification markers (grep):
  • ``server/fund/services/model_risk_report.py``:
    ``def assemble_quarterly_report``.
  • ``server/fund/services/model_risk_renderer_pdf.py``:
    ``pdflatex|subprocess``.
  • ``data/governed/model_risk/templates/quarterly.tex.j2``:
    ``\\documentclass|MRM``.
  • ``cli.py``: ``mrm-report generate|mrm-report publish``.
  • ``tests/test_model_risk_report.py``:
    ``assemble_quarterly_report|deterministic``.

Run the MRM-report suite to verify locally:

  PYTEST_DISABLE_PLUGIN_AUTOLOAD=1 python3 -m pytest \
    coherence_engine/tests/test_model_risk_report.py -v
  → 17 passed (including a real pdflatex compile when TeX Live /
    MacTeX is installed; otherwise the PDF test skips with a warning
    and 16 still pass).

  python -m coherence_engine mrm-report generate \
      --quarter 2026Q2 --output /tmp/mrm.pdf
  → emits a 2-page PDF (~165 KB) with the seed backlog content,
    plus a JSON line on stdout carrying ``input_digest``,
    ``report_digest``, and ``pages``.

Prompt 60 prohibitions honored:
  * Do NOT claim legal SR 11-7 compliance: every renderer surface
    repeats ``"informed by, not legally compliant with"``;
    ``MRM_DISCLAIMER`` is rendered verbatim into every report; the
    docs spec opens with the same disclaimer.
  * Do NOT skip the .tex determinism test:
    ``test_render_tex_is_deterministic`` asserts
    ``render_tex(data) == render_tex(data)`` byte-for-byte and is
    the cheapest signal of accidental drift in template ordering or
    in assembler aggregation logic.
  * Do NOT include unredacted PII: only aggregates flow through;
    partner IDs are hashed with ``_PARTNER_HASH_SALT``; override
    ``reason_text`` is intentionally not in the report shape.
  * No edits outside SCOPE. Files modified: cli.py,
    COHERENCE_ENGINE_PROJECT_STATUS.txt,
    COHERENCE_ENGINE_CONTINUATION_PROMPT.txt. Files created:
    server/fund/services/model_risk_report.py,
    server/fund/services/model_risk_renderer_pdf.py,
    data/governed/model_risk/templates/quarterly.tex.j2,
    data/governed/model_risk/backlog.yaml,
    tests/test_model_risk_report.py,
    docs/specs/model_risk_management.md.


RECENT CHANGES — 2026-04-25 (Wave 15, prompt 59/70)
---------------------------------------------------

Conflict-of-interest registry + automated COI gate. Before any
partner meeting is auto-booked or a ``pass`` decision is finalized,
the engine consults the new registry and refuses to route the
application to a partner with a declared relationship to the
founder or company. The registry is a two-table append-only store
plus an admin-issued override table; every check writes a
``COICheck`` row so the disclosure trail is canonical.

  • ``server/fund/services/conflict_of_interest.py`` —
    ``check_coi(db, application, partner_id, *, now=, persist=,
    disclosure_uri=)`` evaluates active declarations matching any
    candidate party ref (founder_id, founder_user_id, email_token,
    company_name) and resolves to ``clear`` /
    ``conflicted`` / ``requires_disclosure``. Hard relationships
    (``employed | family | invested | board | founder``) → hard
    conflict; soft (``advisor``) → disclosure required.
    ``route_for_application`` picks the first conflict-clear
    candidate from a ranked list; conflicted candidates are NEVER
    auto-routed to the same partner (prompt 59 prohibition).
    ``record_override`` enforces the ``MIN_OVERRIDE_JUSTIFICATION_LENGTH
    = 50`` floor and refuses anything shorter.

  • ``server/fund/services/decision_policy.py`` — new
    ``coi_clear`` gate. The policy module deliberately does NOT
    import the registry; the caller threads ``coi_clear`` (bool)
    + ``coi_status`` (string) onto the ``application`` mapping
    (mirroring the prompt-53 KYC + prompt-56 regulatory-pathway
    pattern). ``conflicted`` surfaces ``COI_CONFLICT`` and
    ``requires_disclosure`` surfaces ``COI_DISCLOSURE_REQUIRED``;
    both are in the manual-review reason set so ``pass``
    downgrades to ``manual_review``.

  • ``server/fund/models.py`` — three new ORM models.
    ``COIDeclaration`` (``fund_coi_declarations``) is the
    partner's standing declaration with ``period_start`` /
    ``period_end`` validity bounds and a ``status`` field
    (``active`` | ``revoked``). ``COICheck`` (``fund_coi_checks``)
    is the append-only result row, one per evaluation.
    ``COIOverride`` (``fund_coi_overrides``) is the admin-issued
    release valve with a ≥ 50-character ``justification`` that is
    audited.

  • ``alembic/versions/20260425_000016_coi_registry.py`` —
    creates the three tables with appropriate indexes
    (partner_id, party_id_ref, relationship, status on
    declarations; application_id, partner_id, status on checks;
    application_id, partner_id on overrides). FK is from checks
    + overrides → ``fund_applications.id``; partner_id is a free
    string so partner identity can come from the API key
    fingerprint, the CRM, or any other identity provider.

  • ``server/fund/routers/coi.py`` —
    ``POST /coi/declarations`` (partner / admin),
    ``GET /coi/declarations`` (partner sees own; admin sees all,
    optional ``partner_id`` filter),
    ``POST /coi/check`` (run on demand; persists a ``COICheck``
    row),
    ``POST /coi/override`` (admin only; 422 on a missing or
    too-short justification). Every write path emits an
    :func:`audit_log` event so the disclosure trail is auditable
    end-to-end. Mirrors the partner_api ``_attach_principal``
    pattern (paths are not in ``_is_fund_path``, so the router
    verifies the API key itself).

  • ``tests/test_coi.py`` (19 tests, all green) — covers active
    declaration → gate fires (employed / family / advisor),
    expired / revoked declaration → gate clear, no declaration
    → clear, ``route_for_application`` skips conflicted
    candidates / returns ``None`` when all conflict, decision
    policy ``coi_clear`` gate downgrades ``pass`` to
    ``manual_review`` on both reason codes,
    backward-compatibility (missing ``coi_clear`` is silent),
    ``record_override`` rejects short justifications, and the
    router ``POST /coi/override`` returns 422 on missing /
    too-short justifications, 403 for the ``partner`` role, 201
    on a long justification.

  • ``docs/specs/conflict_of_interest.md`` — operator-facing
    reference: table schemas, the matching algorithm
    (candidate party refs + active-window predicate), gate
    placement (scheduler.propose + decision_policy.evaluate),
    override flow, and the load-bearing prohibitions
    (no auto-routing of a conflicted application; every
    override carries a ≥ 50 char justification; no
    auto-clearing).

Verification markers (grep):
  • ``server/fund/services/conflict_of_interest.py``:
    ``COIDeclaration|COICheck|def check_coi``.
  • ``server/fund/routers/coi.py``: ``declare|override``.
  • ``server/fund/services/decision_policy.py``: ``coi_clear|
    COI_CONFLICT``.
  • ``tests/test_coi.py``: ``coi|conflict``.

Run the COI suite to verify locally:

  PYTEST_DISABLE_PLUGIN_AUTOLOAD=1 python3 -m pytest \
    coherence_engine/tests/test_coi.py -v
  → 19 passed.

Prompt 59 prohibitions honored:
  * Do NOT auto-route a conflicted application to the same
    partner: ``route_for_application`` skips conflicted
    candidates entirely; ``check_coi.coi_clear`` is False for
    ``conflicted`` regardless of any attached override row.
  * Do NOT auto-clear an override; every override carries a
    justification (≥ 50 chars) and is audited:
    ``record_override`` enforces ``MIN_OVERRIDE_JUSTIFICATION_LENGTH
    = 50`` and raises ``COIError(JUSTIFICATION_TOO_SHORT)``;
    the router returns 422; every successful write emits
    ``audit_log("coi_override", ...)``.
  * No edits outside SCOPE. Files modified:
    server/fund/models.py, server/fund/services/decision_policy.py,
    COHERENCE_ENGINE_PROJECT_STATUS.txt,
    COHERENCE_ENGINE_CONTINUATION_PROMPT.txt. Files created:
    server/fund/services/conflict_of_interest.py,
    server/fund/routers/coi.py,
    alembic/versions/20260425_000016_coi_registry.py,
    tests/test_coi.py, docs/specs/conflict_of_interest.md.


RECENT CHANGES — 2026-04-25 (Wave 15, prompt 58/70)
---------------------------------------------------

PII tokenization + audit-log RLS. Sensitive personal data
(email, full legal name, phone, residence address) is now
stored on disk as a deterministic, non-reversible token; the
clear value is held in a sibling per-row AES-GCM ciphertext
column and is reachable only through a scope-gated helper that
writes one INSERT-only audit row per access.

  • ``server/fund/services/pii_tokenization.py`` — the
    tokenizer. ``tokenize(value, kind=, tenant_salt=)`` returns
    ``"tok_<kind>_<32hex>"`` where the hex is the first 16
    bytes of HMAC-SHA-256 over ``kind + ":" + value`` keyed by
    the per-tenant salt. Determinism per tenant lets joins /
    dedup / CRM upsert continue to work without ever loading
    clear PII; HMAC-SHA-256 plus 128-bit truncation gives
    non-reversibility without the salt; the ``kind`` prefix in
    the HMAC input domain-separates fields so equal values
    across kinds never collide. Email values are normalised
    (strip + lowercase) before tokenization. Empty inputs raise
    ``ValueError`` rather than collapsing to a global "empty"
    token. Allowed kinds: ``{email, name, phone, address}``.
    Salt resolution order: explicit kwarg → ``PII_TENANT_SALT``
    env var → ``SecretManager.get("PII_TENANT_SALT")``; missing
    salt raises ``PIITokenizationError``.

  • ``server/fund/services/pii_clear_audit.py`` —
    ``ClearReadPrincipal``, ``read_clear(...)``, and the
    ``PIIClearAuditLog`` ORM model. ``read_clear`` (1) verifies
    the principal carries ``pii:read_clear``, raising
    ``ClearReadDenied`` (a ``PermissionError``) if not, (2)
    decrypts the per-row ciphertext under the row's key id via
    :mod:`per_row_encryption`, (3) inserts an audit row carrying
    the token (never the clear value), the principal id, the
    field kind, the subject table+id, the route, and the
    request id. The audit row is flushed but not committed so
    the request's transaction owns the atomicity contract: an
    audit row exists iff the caller actually observed the clear
    value.

  • ``server/fund/models.py`` — ``Founder`` gains
    ``email_token`` (indexed; the deterministic token),
    ``email_clear`` (per-row AES-GCM ciphertext of the clear
    email), and ``email_clear_key_id`` (foreign reference into
    ``fund_encryption_keys``). The legacy ``email`` column is
    intentionally retained as the **expand** half of an
    expand-backfill-contract rollout — every existing caller
    keeps working, and a follow-up prompt drops ``email`` once
    they are switched to ``email_token`` +
    ``read_clear_email``. ``Founder.read_clear_email(db=,
    principal=, route=, request_id=, reason=)`` is the only
    sanctioned path to the clear email.

  • ``alembic/versions/20260425_000015_pii_tokenization.py`` —
    adds the three founder columns and the
    ``pii_clear_audit_log`` table (six indexed columns:
    principal_id, field_kind, token, subject_id, request_id,
    created_at). On Postgres only: installs the
    ``PII_AUDIT_RLS_POLICIES`` and a defence-in-depth trigger
    ``pii_clear_audit_log_no_update`` that raises on any
    UPDATE / DELETE attempt — catching attempts that bypass RLS
    via a superuser. Best-effort backfill recomputes
    ``email_token`` + encrypts ``email_clear`` for existing
    founders; if the salt is unavailable the backfill exits
    cleanly and re-runs on the next migration.

  • ``server/fund/security/rls.py`` — adds
    ``PII_AUDIT_RLS_POLICIES`` as a sibling registry to
    ``RLS_POLICIES`` (keeps the prompt-22 snapshot test
    intact). Declares INSERT-only for ``service_role``,
    SELECT for ``service_role`` + ``admin``, and **no UPDATE
    or DELETE policy for any role** — the on-disk tampering
    invariant. The migration applies this registry on Postgres.

  • ``tests/test_pii_tokenization.py`` (14 tests) +
    ``tests/test_pii_audit_rls.py`` (9 tests), all 23 green —
    cover tokenizer determinism per (kind, salt), salt /
    kind separation, email normalisation, empty-rejection,
    missing-salt error, ``read_clear_email`` denied without
    scope, ``read_clear_email`` with scope returns clear and
    writes one audit row per call, audit row never carries the
    clear value, and the no-UPDATE / no-DELETE policy contract.

  • ``docs/specs/pii_handling.md`` — operator-facing reference:
    storage shape, tokenization invariant, salt management +
    rotation play, ``pii:read_clear`` scope wiring, the audit
    log schema, the Postgres immutability trigger, and the
    load-bearing prohibitions (no clear PII in logs, no
    UPDATE/DELETE policy on the audit table, no
    non-cryptographic hash for tokenization, no in-place salt
    rotation).

Verification markers (grep):
  • ``server/fund/services/pii_tokenization.py``: ``def
    tokenize`` + ``hmac_sha256``.
  • ``server/fund/services/pii_clear_audit.py``: ``class
    PIIClearAuditLog`` + ``read_clear``.
  • ``server/fund/security/rls.py``: ``pii_clear_audit_log``.
  • ``docs/specs/pii_handling.md``: tokenization / salt /
    rotation.
  • ``tests/test_pii_tokenization.py``: tokenize +
    deterministic.


RECENT CHANGES — 2026-04-25 (Wave 14, prompt 55/70)
---------------------------------------------------

CRM bidirectional sync — Affinity (primary) + HubSpot
(alternate) behind a single ``CRMBackend`` protocol. Synchronizes
``Founder`` / ``Application`` records to a partner-facing CRM and
absorbs partner-side edits via signed webhooks; a daily
reconciliation cron repairs any deliveries the webhook listener
missed.

  • ``server/fund/services/crm_backends.py`` — ``AffinityBackend``
    and ``HubSpotBackend``. Each exposes ``upsert_founder``,
    ``upsert_application``, ``verify_webhook``, ``parse_webhook``,
    and ``fetch_recent_updates``. Affinity webhooks are verified
    with ``hex(HMAC-SHA-256(secret, raw_body))`` in
    ``Affinity-Webhook-Signature`` (the ``sha256=`` prefix is
    accepted); HubSpot v3 webhooks are verified with
    ``base64(HMAC-SHA-256(secret, raw_body))`` in
    ``X-HubSpot-Signature-v3``. ``CRMUpdate`` is the
    vendor-agnostic dataclass produced by ``parse_webhook``.

  • ``server/fund/services/crm_sync.py`` — three flows.
    Outbound: ``enqueue_outbound_upsert(db, application_id=...,
    reason=...)`` writes a ``crm_upsert_requested`` event into
    ``fund_event_outbox`` whenever ``Application.status`` or
    ``Decision.decision`` changes; a downstream worker actually
    issues the upstream HTTP call. Inbound:
    ``apply_inbound_update(db, update)`` resolves the local
    application (by id, then by founder email), reads the prior
    snapshot from the latest ``crm_inbound_applied`` event for
    ``(provider, external_id)``, applies last-writer-wins for
    tags/notes/deal-stage, NEVER mutates ``Decision.decision``
    (the payload carries ``verdict_locked: true``), and treats CRM
    nulls as "no signal" (carry-forward, not clear).
    Reconciliation: ``reconcile_crm_deltas(db, backend, *, now,
    window=24h)`` calls ``backend.fetch_recent_updates`` for the
    trailing window, replays each ``CRMUpdate`` through
    ``apply_inbound_update``, and emits a
    ``crm_reconciliation_completed`` event with
    applied/skipped/unresolved counts.

  • ``server/fund/routers/crm_webhooks.py`` —
    ``POST /webhooks/crm/affinity`` and
    ``POST /webhooks/crm/hubspot``. Both return HTTP 401 on
    signature failure and never mutate state without a verified
    signature; verified payloads are parsed by the backend and
    applied via ``apply_inbound_update``. Apply is idempotent —
    duplicate deliveries return ``{"applied": false, "reason":
    "already_current"}``.

  • ``server/fund/services/scheduled_jobs.py`` — cron-style
    registry. ``crm_daily_reconciliation`` runs at 07:00 UTC;
    ``build_default_crm_backends()`` constructs only the backends
    whose required env vars are present (a missing
    ``HUBSPOT_PRIVATE_APP_TOKEN`` is logged-and-skipped, not
    fatal).

  • ``tests/test_crm_sync.py`` (28 tests, all green) — covers
    backend signature verify accept/reject, parse_webhook field
    extraction, outbound enqueue persists outbox events, inbound
    last-writer-wins / never-overwrites-verdict / resolve-by-email
    / unresolved no-op / idempotent-when-current / no-clear-on-null
    semantics, reconciliation emits events with the correct
    window bounds and is idempotent against the same fixture
    diff, and TestClient-driven 401-on-bad-signature /
    200-on-valid / 200-on-duplicate-no-op for both providers.

  • ``docs/specs/crm_sync.md`` — full spec including the
    load-bearing prohibitions: webhook signatures cannot be
    skipped; the verdict is policy-only; CRM null is not a clear.

  • ``.env.example`` — adds ``AFFINITY_API_KEY``,
    ``AFFINITY_WEBHOOK_SECRET``, ``AFFINITY_API_BASE``,
    ``HUBSPOT_PRIVATE_APP_TOKEN``, ``HUBSPOT_WEBHOOK_SECRET``,
    ``HUBSPOT_API_BASE``.

Verification markers (grep):
  • ``server/fund/services/crm_sync.py``: ``def apply_inbound_update``
    + ``reconcile_crm_deltas``.
  • ``server/fund/services/crm_backends.py``: ``AffinityBackend``,
    ``HubSpotBackend``.
  • ``server/fund/routers/crm_webhooks.py``: ``webhook``,
    ``signature``.
  • ``tests/test_crm_sync.py``: ``reconcile``, ``webhook``.


RECENT CHANGES — 2026-04-25 (Wave 11, prompt 39/70)
---------------------------------------------------

Browser-mode (WebRTC) founder interview surface — the in-page
alternative to the Twilio voice path (prompt 38). Both paths
emit the same ``interview_session_completed`` outbox event so
downstream scoring is mode-agnostic.

  • ``apps/founder_portal/src/app/interview/[sessionId]/page.tsx``
    — Next.js dynamic route. Renders the ``InterviewUi`` component
    keyed by the session id minted server-side.

  • ``apps/founder_portal/src/lib/webrtc_recorder.ts`` — wraps
    platform ``MediaRecorder`` (mime
    ``audio/webm; codecs=opus``) to emit fixed-length 5-second
    chunks. Sequence numbers are issued internally — callers
    cannot reorder them. Microphone errors are surfaced via
    ``onError``; the loop never silently swallows a failed chunk
    callback.

  • ``apps/founder_portal/src/lib/chunked_upload.ts`` — three-step
    pipeline per chunk: ``initiate`` (POST ``chunks:initiate`` →
    signed URL + ``chunk_id``), ``PUT`` direct to object storage,
    ``complete`` (POST ``chunks:complete`` → server records SHA-256
    + size). Plus a ``finalize`` helper for the
    ``:finalize`` round-trip. Each phase retries with exponential
    backoff (100ms, 300ms, 900ms, capped at 5s) up to three
    attempts.

  • ``apps/founder_portal/src/components/interview_ui.tsx`` —
    interview lifecycle (idle → recording → finalizing →
    completed/error). Serializes uploads behind a single promise
    chain so the recorder cadence cannot race the server's
    monotonic-seq guard. Stops the recorder on unmount.

  • ``server/fund/services/voice_intake.py`` — new
    ``start_browser_session(application_id)`` mints a
    ``channel="browser"`` :class:`InterviewSession`; new
    ``stitch_chunks(session)`` downloads every completed chunk
    by ``seq``, runs ``ffmpeg -f concat -safe 0 -i list.txt -c
    copy out.webm`` (codec-copy concat — every chunk shares
    opus parameters from a single MediaRecorder instance), and
    PUTs the result at ``interviews/<session>/full.webm``. New
    ``finalize_browser_session`` stitches + emits exactly one
    ``interview_session_completed`` event tagged
    ``channel="browser"`` and is idempotent on
    ``status == "completed"``.

  • ``server/fund/routers/interview_browser.py`` — three POSTs:
    ``/api/v1/interviews/{session}/chunks:initiate`` (server
    refuses gaps and replays via
    ``voice_intake._next_expected_seq``), ``/chunks:complete``
    (verifies bytes at the signed URL — never trusts client-
    supplied SHA-256 — and flips the chunk row to
    ``"completed"``), and ``:finalize`` (kicks the stitcher,
    returns ``idempotent=true`` on a second call against an
    already-completed session). Bytes never proxy through the
    router.

  • ``server/fund/models.py`` — new :class:`InterviewChunk` row:
    id, session_id, application_id, seq, chunk_uri,
    chunk_sha256, size_bytes, content_type, status, created_at,
    completed_at. Unique constraint on ``(session_id, seq)``.

  • ``alembic/versions/20260425_000007_interview_chunks.py`` —
    creates ``fund_interview_chunks`` with FK constraints to
    ``fund_interview_sessions`` and ``fund_applications``,
    indexes on session_id / application_id / seq / status, and
    a ``uq_fund_interview_chunks_session_seq`` unique
    constraint enforcing per-session monotonic ordering at the
    storage layer.

  • ``tests/test_browser_interview.py`` — 7 tests, all pass:
    ``start_browser_session`` row shape; deterministic stitch
    output (SHA-256 equals concat-of-payloads); seq-gap
    rejection; finalize-and-idempotent; router rejects
    out-of-order seq with 409; complete records SHA-256 + size;
    finalize router emits exactly one event with idempotent
    second call. ffmpeg is faked via a Python shim placed on
    ``$PATH`` so CI does not depend on a system ffmpeg.

  • ``apps/founder_portal/__tests__/interview.spec.ts`` —
    Playwright spec mocks ``MediaRecorder`` + ``getUserMedia``
    via ``addInitScript``; verifies that two emitted chunks
    walk the full initiate → PUT → complete sequence in order
    and that ``:finalize`` is invoked on stop.

  • ``docs/specs/browser_interview.md`` — end-to-end flow
    diagram, sequence-ordering contract, idempotency rules,
    storage layout, failure-mode table, and configuration
    (``FFMPEG_BINARY`` env override).

Prohibitions honored: chunk uploads do not proxy through the
backend; client-side seq numbers are never trusted without
server-side monotonicity verification; ffmpeg non-zero return
codes raise ``VoiceIntakeError`` rather than silently producing
truncated output. Files outside SCOPE were not modified.
