Twilio Voice ingress for phone-based founder interviews.

  • ``server/fund/services/twilio_adapter.py`` — ``RequestValidator``
    (re-exported from the official ``twilio`` SDK when installed,
    otherwise a vendored byte-for-byte port of the documented
    HMAC-SHA1 signature algorithm), ``verify_twilio_signature``,
    ``TwilioClient`` protocol, and a test seam
    (``set_twilio_client_for_tests``) so the suite never calls a paid
    Twilio API.

  • ``server/fund/services/voice_intake.py`` —
    ``start_call(application_id, phone_number, ...)`` mints an
    :class:`InterviewSession` (``channel="voice"``) and asks the
    Twilio client to dial. Topics are loaded deterministically from
    ``data/prompts/registry.json`` (prompt 08): only ``status="prod"``
    entries with a registered voice line are surfaced. TwiML is
    rendered by hand (no SDK dependency) so the bytes are stable
    against a pinned snapshot. ``store_recording`` puts the audio
    through the object-storage adapter and writes an
    :class:`InterviewRecording` row keyed by ``(session, topic)``.
    ``finalize_session`` emits exactly one
    ``interview_session_completed`` outbox event and is idempotent.

  • ``server/fund/routers/twilio_webhooks.py`` — three POSTs:
    ``/webhooks/twilio/voice`` (initial TwiML — greeting + first
    topic + ``<Record>``), ``/webhooks/twilio/recording``
    (recording-completion: object-storage write, DB row, next-topic
    TwiML or final ``<Hangup/>``), ``/webhooks/twilio/status``
    (terminal call-status updates trigger the
    ``interview_session_completed`` emission). Signature verification
    is mandatory; ``TWILIO_VALIDATE_WEBHOOK_SIGNATURE=false`` may
    only opt out in ``dev`` (the gate ignores the override in
    ``staging`` / ``prod``). The signed URL is reconstructed from
    ``X-Forwarded-*`` so it matches what Twilio actually signed.

  • ``server/fund/models.py`` — new :class:`InterviewRecording`
    table: id, application_id, session_id, topic_id, recording_uri,
    recording_sha256, duration_seconds, provider_recording_sid,
    status, started_at, completed_at. Recording bytes never enter
    the database — only the URI + SHA-256.

  • ``alembic/versions/20260425_000006_interview_recordings.py`` —
    creates ``fund_interview_recordings`` with FK constraints back to
    ``fund_applications`` and ``fund_interview_sessions`` and indexes
    on application_id, session_id, topic_id, provider_recording_sid,
    and status.

  • ``server/fund/schemas/events/interview_session_completed.v1.json``
    — outbox event schema (additionalProperties=false): topics array
    with ``recorded|skipped|failed`` per-topic status, recording_uri,
    recording_sha256, duration_seconds; topics_covered / topics_total;
    optional provider_call_sid.

  • Configuration (``.env.example``):
    - ``TWILIO_ACCOUNT_SID``
    - ``TWILIO_AUTH_TOKEN``  (HMAC key; never logged)
    - ``TWILIO_FROM_NUMBER`` (E.164 caller-id)
    - ``TWILIO_VALIDATE_WEBHOOK_SIGNATURE`` (default ``true``)

RECENT CHANGES — 2026-04-25 (Wave 10, prompt 37/70)
---------------------------------------------------

API gateway middleware delivered as a stack of four concerns wired
onto the FastAPI app via ``server/fund/middleware/install_gateway_middleware``:

  • ``RateLimitMiddleware`` — token-bucket keyed on API-key prefix
    (when ``X-API-Key`` / ``Authorization: Bearer`` is present) or
    client IP. Refill rate = the API-key row's
    ``rate_limit_per_minute`` if known, falling back to
    ``RATE_LIMIT_DEFAULT`` (env, default 120). Backend is Redis (Lua
    bucket) when reachable and the worker stack is on ARQ; otherwise
    a process-local bucket. Denials return 429 with
    ``Retry-After`` and ``{"error":"rate_limited",
    "retry_after_seconds":N}``.

  • ``RequestSigningMiddleware`` — gates ``/api/v1/internal/*``.
    Headers ``X-Coherence-Timestamp`` (RFC 3339) and
    ``X-Coherence-Signature: v1=<hex>`` carry an HMAC-SHA-256 over
    ``f"{ts}\\n{METHOD}\\n{path}\\n{sha256(body)}"`` keyed on
    ``REQUEST_SIGNING_SECRET``. ±300 s skew window
    (``REQUEST_SIGNING_MAX_SKEW_SECONDS``); replay protection via a
    bounded LRU of the most recent 10 000 ``(ts, sig)`` pairs.
    Denied signatures are logged truncated to the first 8 hex chars;
    secrets are never logged. SHA-1 / MD5 are not accepted.

  • ``install_cors`` — explicit allow-list from
    ``CORS_ALLOWED_ORIGINS`` (comma-separated). A literal ``*``
    raises at install time outside the dev environment. Methods:
    GET/POST/PUT/DELETE/OPTIONS. Allowed headers include
    ``Authorization``, ``Content-Type``, ``X-Request-ID``,
    ``X-Coherence-Signature``, ``X-Coherence-Timestamp``,
    ``X-API-Key``. ``X-Request-ID`` is the only exposed header.

  • ``RequestIdMiddleware`` — reads or mints ``X-Request-ID``,
    stores it on ``request.state`` and a ``ContextVar`` so log
    formatters can pick it up via ``RequestIdLogFilter``, and echoes
    it back on every response (including 4xx denials from deeper
    layers).

Configuration (``server/fund/config.py``):
  • ``CORS_ALLOWED_ORIGINS``
  • ``RATE_LIMIT_DEFAULT`` (per-minute fallback)
  • ``REQUEST_SIGNING_SECRET`` (required for ``/api/v1/internal/*``)
  • ``REQUEST_SIGNING_MAX_SKEW_SECONDS``

Tests (16, all passing):
  tests/test_middleware_rate_limit.py    — token-bucket exhaustion,
                                           Retry-After + body shape,
                                           per-prefix isolation,
                                           health-path skip.
  tests/test_middleware_request_signing.py — valid sig 200,
                                             tampered body 401,
                                             replay 401, skew 401,
                                             public path skip,
                                             missing headers 401.
  tests/test_middleware_cors.py          — request-id round-trip,
                                           preflight allow / deny,
                                           wildcard prod-failure,
                                           wildcard dev-allowed.

Spec: ``docs/specs/api_gateway.md``.

  above. Down-migration drops everything.

* ``server/fund/services/decision_overrides.py`` — write-side policy
  for the override flow. Validates ``reason_code`` against the closed
  enum (``factual_error``, ``policy_misalignment``,
  ``regulatory_constraint``, ``manual_diligence``), enforces a 40-char
  floor on ``reason_text``, and requires a ``justification_uri`` memo
  for any ``pass → reject`` override. Idempotent on the
  ``(application_id, status="active")`` pair: a duplicate write returns
  the existing row without re-emitting the event; an explicit
  ``unrevise=True`` flag is the only way to supersede the prior row.
  Every successful write emits a ``decision_overridden.v1`` outbox
  event so downstream founder-notification + portfolio consumers pick
  up the new verdict. Re-exports ``require_role`` as a thin wrapper
  around :func:`enforce_roles` so the partner surface reads as a
  single coherent unit.

* ``server/fund/routers/partner_api.py`` — JSON-only router mounted at
  ``/partner`` and ``/api/v1/partner``. Endpoints:
  * ``GET /partner/pipeline`` (cursor-paginated; filters: ``domain``,
    ``verdict``, ``mode``)
  * ``GET /partner/applications/{id}`` (full detail, decision artifact,
    active override)
  * ``POST /partner/applications/{id}/override`` (validates payload,
    emits audit + event)
  * ``GET /partner/audit`` (read-only feed of operator actions)
  RBAC: every route gates on ``partner`` or ``admin`` via
  ``require_role``; viewer / analyst tokens get a structured 403. The
  router attaches a principal locally (mirroring ``admin_ui.py``) so
  ``FundSecurityMiddleware``'s fund-path matcher does not need to
  expand. The partner router is wired in ``server/fund/app.py`` on
  both the legacy and ``/api/v1`` mount paths for parity with the rest
  of the fund surface.

Frontend additions (``apps/partner_dashboard/``):

* Mirrors the founder-portal scaffolding (Next.js 14, App Router,
  Tailwind, Vitest, Playwright). ESLint + ``next/core-web-vitals``,
  separate Vercel deployment target on port 3002.

* ``src/lib/supabase.ts`` — same SSR cookie wiring as the founder
  portal; the role check pulls from ``user.app_metadata.role`` and is
  centralized in ``isPartnerOrAdmin``. ``SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY`` is
  intentionally absent from ``.env.example`` (service-role operations
  belong on the backend, never on the edge).

* ``src/lib/api_client.ts`` — typed client over ``/api/v1/partner/*``
  endpoints with a ``PartnerApiError`` for envelope-aware error
  surfacing.

* ``src/lib/pipeline_filter.ts`` — pure URL-param parser /
  serializer. Closed enums for ``verdict`` and ``mode``; unknown
  values silently degrade to "any". Limit is clamped to 100. Round-
  trip serialization omits the default limit so links stay clean.

* ``src/components/decision_artifact_viewer.tsx`` — collapsible tree
  view of a decision artifact: per-section ``<details>`` for summary,
  coherence-vs-threshold bars, optional per-layer score bars (markers
  ``decision_artifact|per_layer``), and the failed-gates / reason-code
  list.

* ``src/app/pipeline/page.tsx`` — server-rendered pivot table.
  Filters live in URL search params so refresh + share-links work.
  Cursor-based pagination via the backend's ``next_cursor`` field.

* ``src/app/applications/[id]/page.tsx`` — application detail with the
  artifact viewer, an override-status panel (active override vs.
  automated decision), and a CTA into the override page.

* ``src/app/applications/[id]/override/page.tsx`` — server-action
  form. Client-side validation in ``./validate.ts`` (≥40 char reason
  text, closed reason-code enum, memo required for any reject
  override). Server action posts to the backend and redirects on
  success; on validation / API failure it round-trips through
  ``?error=`` so the form re-renders with the human-readable cause.

* ``src/app/audit/page.tsx`` — read-only audit-log view. Filters on
  action and application id; pretty-prints structured details.

Tests:

* ``tests/test_decision_overrides.py`` — 14 cases covering service-
  level validation (unknown reason code, short reason text,
  pass→reject memo requirement, idempotent duplicate, unrevise
  superseding, event payload shape) and router-level RBAC
  (unauthenticated 401, viewer 403, partner 201, admin 201, short
  reason 400, idempotent second call 200, pipeline filter ok, audit
  log emission).

* ``apps/partner_dashboard/__tests__/pipeline.spec.ts`` — Playwright
  spec exercising the URL filter parser (defaults, known-enum
  acceptance, unknown-value rejection, limit clamping, round-trip
  serialization) and the override form validator (reject without
  memo, short reason text, complete payload, unknown reason code).

CI:

* ``.github/workflows/partner_dashboard.yml`` — pnpm install + lint +
  ``tsc --noEmit`` + ``next build`` + Vitest + Playwright; secondary
  job runs ``python -m pytest tests/test_decision_overrides.py -v``.

Verification (run locally, 2026-04-25):

  → 14 passed in 3.56s


RECENT CHANGES — 2026-04-25 (Wave 10, prompt 34/70)
---------------------------------------------------

Founder portal fleshed out: a multi-step application form with
``localStorage`` autosave, direct-PUT signed-URL file upload (deck +
supporting docs), a real-time polling hook with exponential backoff,
and a stage-by-stage status timeline. All UI is keyboard-navigable
with axe-core (WCAG 2 A/AA) gating zero violations on every page.
Files never proxy through the Next.js layer — the backend issues a
signed URL and the browser PUTs bytes directly to the storage backend.

Backend additions (``server/fund/routers/applications.py``):

* ``POST /api/v1/applications/{id}/uploads:initiate`` — body
  ``{ filename, content_type, size_bytes, kind }``, returns
  ``{ upload_id, upload_url, headers, expires_at, key, uri,
  max_bytes }``. The router dispatches signed-URL minting on the
  active storage backend (S3 ``generate_presigned_url("put_object")``;
  Supabase ``/storage/v1/object/<bucket>/<key>`` with bearer
  authorization; local synthetic ``local://upload/...`` URL for
  in-process tests). Defense-in-depth ownership check on the founder
  JWT path; service-role path keeps the existing role gate.
  Validation: filename matches ``^[A-Za-z0-9._\\- ]{1,255}$``;
  content_type ∈ pdf / pptx / ppt / png / jpeg / plain; size_bytes
  in (0, 25 MiB]; kind ∈ {deck, supporting}. Upload state is
  persisted in the existing ``IdempotencyRecord`` table under a
  namespaced ``upload:{application_id}`` endpoint key, keeping the
  change schema-free. The intended URI is also stamped onto
  ``Application.transcript_uri`` for the deck slot so a partial
  upload still leaves a forensic trail.

* ``POST /api/v1/applications/{id}/uploads:complete`` — body
  ``{ upload_id }``. Verifies the object actually exists in the
  storage backend (``backend.get(uri)``), then records the
  *server-observed* size on the upload record. Crucially, the
  client-supplied ``size_bytes`` from ``:initiate`` is NEVER trusted
  for verification — it is only used as a pre-flight rejection
  signal. Fully idempotent: re-calling with the same ``upload_id``
  short-circuits to the previously-stored response envelope. Returns
  409 ``UPLOAD_NOT_FOUND`` if the client never PUT.

Frontend additions (``apps/founder_portal/``):

* ``src/components/multi_step_form.tsx`` — five steps: Company →
  Product → Market → Ask → Upload. Per-step validation runs on Next;
  keyboard-driven (``aria-current="step"`` on the indicator,
  ``aria-invalid``/``aria-describedby`` on every field, ``role="alert"``
  for error text, live ``aria-live="polite"`` autosave hint). Draft is
  keyed on a UUID ``draft-id`` and persisted to ``localStorage`` as a
  versioned blob with a 14-day TTL; on successful submit the draft is
  cleared. Sensitive fields are not serialized once the application
  is created — only in-flight form values, never decision artifacts
  or PII tied to a submitted application.

* ``src/components/file_upload.tsx`` — ``<input type="file">`` with an
  ARIA progress bar; uses ``XMLHttpRequest`` so upload progress is
  observable (fetch() doesn't expose Upload progress in browsers as
  of 2026). Disabled state during in-flight upload so the user can't
  double-trigger.

* ``src/lib/upload.ts`` — three-step helper:
  ``initiateUpload`` (POSTs to ``/api/auth`` action ``upload_initiate``)
  → ``putToSignedUrl`` (direct ``XHR PUT`` to the signed URL with the
  backend-issued headers; the browser never sees storage credentials)
  → ``completeUpload``. ``UploadError`` distinguishes ``initiate`` /
  ``put`` / ``complete`` failure phases.

* ``src/hooks/use_application_status.ts`` — polls
  ``GET /api/auth?action=application_status`` every 5 s. On error,
  exponentially backs off (5s → 10s → 20s → 40s → cap 60s) and resets
  to 5 s on the next success. Stops polling once the application
  reaches a terminal status (``decision_pass`` / ``decision_fail`` /
  ``decision_manual_review`` / ``escalated``). Cancellation is wired
  through a ``cancelledRef`` so unmounts during an in-flight fetch
  cannot leak setState calls.

* ``src/components/status_timeline.tsx`` — four-stage timeline (Intake
  → Interview → Scoring → Decision) rendered from the polled status
  plus the decision artifact payload when available. Each stage gets
  a tone-coded card with an explicit ``sr-only`` status label so
  screen readers announce state transitions.

* ``src/components/application_status_view.tsx`` — composes the hook,
  the timeline, and a lazy fetch of the decision artifact. The artifact
  is fetched once on entry to a terminal status, not on every poll.

* ``src/lib/api_client.ts`` extended with ``getApplication``,
  ``initiateUpload``, ``completeUpload``. The ``Authorization:
  Bearer <supabase token>`` injection pattern is unchanged.

* ``src/app/api/auth/route.ts`` extended with three new actions over
  the existing ``/api/auth`` POST/GET seam:
  ``upload_initiate``, ``upload_complete``, ``application_status``
  (GET). Each forwards to the SDK and translates ``BackendApiError``
  into ``{ error, code }`` JSON.

Tests:

* ``tests/test_upload_initiate.py`` (CREATE) — 7 pytest cases:
  ``initiate`` returns a signed URL with expiry in the 60–700 s
  window, with a key prefix of ``applications/{app_id}/deck/`` and a
  ``coh://local/default/...`` canonical URI; oversized payload and
  disallowed content-type are rejected with 422; ``complete``
  finalizes after a backend put and reports the **storage-observed**
  size (not the client's claimed size); ``complete`` is idempotent
  across repeated calls; ``complete`` returns 409 ``UPLOAD_NOT_FOUND``
  when the client never PUT; ``initiate`` against an unknown
  application returns 404. Run with
  ``python3 -m pytest tests/test_upload_initiate.py -v -p no:pytest-qt``
  → 7 passed.

* ``apps/founder_portal/__tests__/apply_flow.spec.ts`` (CREATE) —
  Playwright happy path: walks all four data steps, submits the form,
  uploads a deck against a mocked signed URL, and lands on the status
  page where the polled status is asserted in the timeline.

* ``apps/founder_portal/__tests__/a11y.spec.ts`` (CREATE) — axe-core
  via ``@axe-core/playwright`` 4.10.0. Asserts zero WCAG 2 A/AA
  violations on the landing page, every step of the apply form, and
  the application status page.

Prohibitions enforced:

* Files are never proxied through the Next.js layer — the backend
  mints a signed URL, the browser PUTs to it directly.
* The client-supplied ``size_bytes`` is never trusted on
  ``:complete``; the server reads ``len(backend.get(uri))``.
* Autosave drops the draft once the application is created and never
  serializes the resulting decision artifact, ID, or any
  ``founder_id``-bound row to ``localStorage``.

No new runtime backend dependencies. New frontend dev dep:
``@axe-core/playwright`` (test-only).

Verification:
  python3 -m pytest tests/test_upload_initiate.py -v -p no:pytest-qt
    # 7 passed
  cd apps/founder_portal && pnpm playwright test
    # apply_flow.spec.ts + a11y.spec.ts (run after `pnpm install` to
    #  pull @axe-core/playwright)

SUPERSEDED — 2026-04-25 (Wave 9, prompt 32/70)
--------------------------------------------------

Feature-flag service. Replaces ad-hoc ``if config.experimental_x:``
gates with one typed registry, one resolver, and a hard audit
invariant for any flag that affects decision-policy semantics. The
default deployment runs entirely on the local YAML registry; the
LaunchDarkly and PostHog adapters are *lazy-imported* so neither
SDK is a hard dependency.

Architecture:

* ``data/governed/feature_flags.yaml`` (NEW) — authoritative registry
  with ``schema_version: feature-flags-v1``. Each flag declares
  ``key`` / ``type`` (boolean | string-enum | int-percent) /
  ``default`` / ``restricted`` / ``client_visible`` / ``owner`` /
  ``description`` (and ``enum`` for string-enum). The loader rejects
  the schema-version mismatch, missing fields, an invalid declared
  default, and the ``restricted: true + client_visible: true`` combo
  at boot. Six seed flags shipped: ``anti_gaming.enabled``,
  ``decision_policy.shadow_mode``, ``scoring.uncertainty_floor``
  (all restricted), ``backtest.replay_engine``,
  ``ui.show_decision_artifact_link``, ``ui.investor_portal_beta``.

* ``server/fund/services/feature_flags.py`` (NEW) — ``FeatureFlags``
  resolver with ``get_bool`` / ``get_string`` / ``get_percent``.
  Resolution order: backend (LD/PostHog) → in-memory YAML override →
  registry default → caller-supplied default → ``MissingFlag``.
  Values cached for 60s; ``invalidate_cache()`` runs on every
  ``set_*`` call. ``FlagSpec.coerce`` enforces type semantics
  (boolean accepts ``true``/``false``/``yes``/``no``/``0``/``1``;
  int-percent must be 0-100; string-enum must be in the declared
  ``enum`` — otherwise the backend value is logged + ignored,
  fall-through to YAML default rather than breaking the pipeline).

* ``server/fund/services/feature_flag_backends.py`` (NEW) —
  ``FeatureFlagBackend`` Protocol plus ``NullBackend``,
  ``LaunchDarklyBackend``, ``PostHogBackend``. Both remote backends
  ``import`` their SDK lazily inside ``__init__`` and raise
  ``FeatureFlagBackendError`` with a remediation message when the
  package or the API key is missing. ``build_backend()`` reads
  ``COHERENCE_FUND_FEATURE_FLAGS_BACKEND`` and returns
  ``NullBackend`` for ``""`` / ``"local"`` / ``"yaml"`` / ``"null"``.

* Restricted-flag audit invariant: ``FeatureFlags.set_restricted(...)``
  is the only path that may flip a flag with ``restricted: true``.
  It (a) writes a JSONL audit row to
  ``data/governed/feature_flag_audit.log`` (``audit_id``,
  ``occurred_at``, ``key``, ``flag_type``, ``old_value``,
  ``new_value``, ``actor``, ``source``, ``reason``); (b) emits a
  ``decision_policy_flag_changed.v1`` event so backtest replay can
  reconstruct historical flag state. ``set_unrestricted`` rejects
  restricted flags; ``set_restricted`` rejects non-restricted flags;
  a missing ``event_publisher`` raises ``RestrictedFlagViolation``.

* ``server/fund/schemas/events/feature_flag_changed.v1.json`` (NEW) —
  ``DecisionPolicyFlagChangedV1``, additionalProperties=false, with
  required ``key`` / ``flag_type`` / ``restricted`` (const ``true``)
  / ``old_value`` / ``new_value`` / ``actor`` / ``source``.

* ``server/fund/services/event_publisher.py`` (MOD) — new
  ``EventPublisher.publish_decision_policy_flag_changed(audit_row)``
  that validates against the new schema (best-effort via jsonschema,
  same fallback as the registered event types) and persists through
  the existing ``EventOutbox``. ``feature_flags.jsonl_event_emitter``
  is the no-DB fallback used by the CLI: appends a fully formed
  envelope to ``data/governed/feature_flag_events.jsonl``.

* ``cli.py`` (MOD) — new ``flags`` subparser with ``flags list``
  (table | json — KEY / TYPE / VALUE / SOURCE / RESTRICTED) and
  ``flags set --key K --value V [--actor A --reason R]``. Restricted
  flags require ``--actor`` and ``--reason``; the CLI uses the JSONL
  emitter so audit + event hit disk even without a DB session.

Tests (``tests/test_feature_flags.py``, 28 cases, all passing):

* Registry parsing: every flag type round-trips; schema-version
  mismatch / missing enum / restricted+client_visible / invalid
  default each raise ``FeatureFlagError`` at boot.
* Resolution order: YAML default served when no backend; backend
  value overrides YAML; backend string ``"true"`` coerced to
  ``True`` for booleans; backend value outside ``enum`` ignored
  (YAML default wins); ``MissingFlag`` for unknown keys; type
  mismatch (``get_bool`` on a string-enum flag) raises
  ``FlagTypeError``.
* Cache: a backend value mutation is invisible until
  ``invalidate_cache()``.
* Restricted-flag audit invariant: ``set_restricted`` writes the
  JSONL audit row with the expected shape AND calls the publisher
  exactly once; missing actor / missing reason / wrong direction
  (``set_restricted`` on non-restricted, ``set_unrestricted`` on
  restricted) all raise ``RestrictedFlagViolation``; constructor
  with ``event_publisher=None`` raises on the first restricted flip.
* Backend factory: default ``NullBackend``; ``"nonsense"`` provider
  raises; LaunchDarkly without ``LAUNCHDARKLY_SDK_KEY`` raises;
  PostHog without ``POSTHOG_PROJECT_API_KEY`` raises.
* Public-flags filter: ``flags.public_flags()`` excludes every
  ``restricted: true`` flag (defense in depth on top of the loader).
* JSONL emitter: produces a valid ``decision_policy_flag_changed``
  envelope with ``restricted: true``.
* Governance YAML loads through the singleton path with the seed
  registry.

Spec: ``docs/specs/feature_flags.md`` documents the registry schema,
the resolution order + caching, the restricted-flag audit invariant
(the emitter contract is load-bearing), how to consume flags from
Python and Next.js, and the prod boundary on
``/api/v1/flags/public`` (restricted flags never appear there).

Verification:
  python -m pytest tests/test_feature_flags.py -v   # 28 passed
  python -m coherence_engine flags list             # 6 flags, source=yaml
  python -m coherence_engine flags set --key anti_gaming.enabled \\
      --value false --actor "ops@coherence" --reason "INC-204"
    # writes ffaud_*; emits decision_policy_flag_changed.v1

Prohibitions held: no bypass of the audit path for restricted flags;
no hard dependency on launchdarkly-server-sdk or posthog (both lazy);
``/api/v1/flags/public`` documented to expose only ``client_visible``
non-restricted flags; no edits outside SCOPE.


SUPERSEDED — 2026-04-25 (Wave 9, prompt 31/70)
--------------------------------------------------

12-factor configuration audit + multi-environment gating. Every config
read now flows through one Pydantic v2 ``Settings`` model; every
behavior-split between environments goes through one gate module; an
AST auditor walks the codebase and records remaining violations as a
governance artifact.

Architecture:

* ``server/fund/config.py`` (REWRITTEN) — ``FundSettings`` is now a
  ``pydantic_settings.BaseSettings`` model. The runtime environment is
  a strict ``Literal["dev","test","staging","prod"]`` field
  (``environment``) resolved exactly once at startup from
  ``COHERENCE_FUND_ENV`` / ``APP_ENV`` (with alias normalization for
  ``production``/``development``/``stage``/etc.). A
  ``model_validator(mode="after")`` enforces prod invariants:
  ``STORAGE_BACKEND=local``, ``COHERENCE_FUND_AUTO_CREATE_TABLES=true``,
  ``sqlite:///`` URLs, and ``SECRET_MANAGER_PROVIDER=disabled`` are
  all rejected outright when ``environment == "prod"``. Backwards-
  compatible UPPER_CASE alias properties (``settings.DATABASE_URL``,
  ``settings.WORKER_BACKEND``, ...) preserve every existing call site.
  ``FundSettings.to_redacted_dict()`` returns the resolved settings
  with ``SecretStr`` fields blanked, used by ``config show``.

* ``server/fund/services/env_gates.py`` (NEW) — single source of truth
  for env-conditional behavior. Pure functions: ``is_prod()``,
  ``is_staging_or_prod()``, ``allow_dry_run_backends()``,
  ``allow_debug_routes()``, ``allow_local_storage_backend()``,
  ``allow_auto_create_tables()``, ``allow_print_secret_value()``,
  ``require_https()``, ``strict_secret_resolution()``. Each gate
  documents *why* the split exists; new gates must too. All read
  ``settings.environment`` (never ``os.environ``).

* ``deploy/scripts/audit_twelve_factor.py`` (NEW) — AST walker that
  flags four rule families:
    - ``env_read_outside_config`` (``os.environ`` / ``os.getenv`` outside
      the allowlist) — ERROR in ``server/fund/``, WARN in
      ``deploy/scripts/`` / ``cli.py`` / ``alembic/``.
    - ``hardcoded_url`` (``http(s)://host``; ``*.local`` /
      ``localhost`` allowed) — WARN.
    - ``print_in_runtime_code`` (print outside CLI/scripts/tests) —
      WARN.
    - ``http_call_without_timeout`` (``requests``/``httpx`` calls
      missing ``timeout=``) — WARN.
  Deterministic JSON output; exit 2 if any errors.

* ``data/governed/config_audit_report.json`` (NEW) — first run of the
  auditor recorded as a governance artifact. Counts: total=145
  (error=50, warn=95). The 50 errors are all in ``server/fund/`` and
  represent the legacy backlog that future Wave 9 prompts will
  remediate (out-of-scope to touch in this prompt).

* ``cli.py`` (MODIFIED) — new ``config audit`` and ``config show``
  subcommands. ``config audit`` runs the auditor in-process via
  ``importlib`` (``deploy/scripts/`` is not a package), exits 0 on no
  errors / 2 otherwise. ``config show`` prints the redacted Settings
  as JSON or a table. The ``secrets manifest`` and ``secrets resolve``
  subcommands now read ``settings.environment`` instead of poking
  ``os.getenv("COHERENCE_FUND_ENV")`` directly, and ``secrets resolve``
  delegates the prod-block check to ``env_gates.allow_print_secret_value()``.

Tests (``tests/test_twelve_factor_audit.py``, 15 cases, all passing):

* Auditor against synthetic clean / bad fixture files (each rule
  family fires on the bad fixture; clean fixture yields zero
  findings).
* Allowlist semantics: env reads in ``server/fund/config.py`` are
  silent; env reads in ``deploy/scripts/`` are warn-only.
* ``Settings`` invariants: dev default; alias normalization for
  ``production``/``staging``; rejection of unknown env tokens;
  rejection of ``STORAGE_BACKEND=local``, ``sqlite:`` URLs,
  ``AUTO_CREATE_TABLES=true``, and ``SECRET_MANAGER_PROVIDER=disabled``
  in prod.
* ``env_gates.is_prod()`` returns ``True`` only when
  ``environment == "prod"``; ``allow_dry_run_backends`` /
  ``allow_debug_routes`` / ``allow_print_secret_value`` flip
  correctly.
* ``to_redacted_dict()`` blanks ``SecretStr`` fields.
* UPPER_CASE alias properties preserve the legacy API.

Spec: ``docs/specs/twelve_factor.md`` documents the env taxonomy, the
gate pattern, the allowlist, and the remediation backlog.

  python -m pytest tests/test_twelve_factor_audit.py -v   # 15 passed
  python -m coherence_engine config audit --format summary  # exit 2, 50 errors
  python -m coherence_engine config show                    # JSON, secrets redacted

Prohibitions held: no implicit hostname-based env detection; no

RECENT CHANGES — 2026-04-25 (Wave 9, prompt 30/70)
--------------------------------------------------

Background worker layer rebuilt around Arq (pure-async, Redis-backed)
with a ``WORKER_BACKEND={poll,arq}`` env switch. The legacy DB-polling
worker remains the failsafe — flipping back is a single env-var change
plus a service restart, no code deploy required. Both backends call
the *same* pure-function task units, so business logic lives in one
place regardless of the queue substrate.

Architecture:

* ``server/fund/workers/`` (NEW package) — three modules wrap the
  existing service layer without duplicating it:
    - ``tasks.py`` — pure-function task units shared by both backends:
      ``run_scoring_job(application_id) -> dict``,
      ``dispatch_outbox_batch(limit) -> int``,
      ``run_backtest_async(config) -> dict``.
    - ``dispatch.py`` — async enqueue helpers
      (``enqueue_scoring_job``, ``enqueue_outbox_dispatch``,
      ``enqueue_backtest``). Each is a no-op when ``WORKER_BACKEND=poll``
      so request handlers can call them unconditionally. Arq-side
      idempotency is enforced via ``_job_id``: the first call with a
      given ``idempotency_key`` schedules; subsequent calls return
      ``None``.
    - ``arq_worker.py`` — ``WorkerSettings`` class
      (``functions=[score_job, dispatch_outbox, run_backtest]``,
      ``max_jobs=4``, ``max_tries=3``, ``job_timeout=900``,
      ``keep_result=86400``); async stubs offload sync bodies via
      ``asyncio.to_thread`` so the event loop stays responsive; lazy
      ``arq`` import keeps the dep optional for poll-only deployments.

* ``server/fund/scoring_worker.py`` (MODIFIED) — extracted
  ``run_scoring_job(application_id, *, db=None)`` as the pure-function
  unit of work. ``process_once`` / ``run_loop`` (legacy polling
  loop) are unchanged; they still drain the same ``ScoringJob`` queue
  and remain the failsafe.

* ``server/fund/config.py`` (MODIFIED) — adds ``WORKER_BACKEND``
  (default ``poll``), ``REDIS_URL`` (default
  ``redis://localhost:6379/0``), ``ARQ_QUEUE_PREFIX``
  (default ``coherence_fund``).

* ``server/fund/app.py`` (MODIFIED) — exposes the three enqueue helpers
  on ``app.state`` so request handlers can wire them through FastAPI's
  ``BackgroundTasks`` (never inline) — request-side Redis hiccups must
  never block the response. Adds an ``on_event("shutdown")`` hook that
  closes the Arq pool. The polling worker remains the request-handler-
  agnostic failsafe.

Tests:

* ``tests/test_arq_worker.py`` — pure-function smoke
  (``run_scoring_job`` end-to-end against in-memory SQLite),
  enqueue idempotency on a stub Arq pool (same key → second call
  deduped), distinct-keys-schedule-separately, missing-key
  ``ValueError``, no-op behavior on poll backend, and a
  ``pytest.importorskip("arq")``-guarded ``WorkerSettings`` smoke.
  ``11 passed`` with ``arq`` installed; ``10 passed, 1 skipped`` on a
  clean image.

* ``tests/test_worker_backend_switch.py`` — verifies the env switch:
  ``WORKER_BACKEND=arq`` causes ``enqueue_scoring_job`` to call
  ``pool.enqueue_job``; ``WORKER_BACKEND=poll`` returns ``None`` and
  never reaches the pool; the existing polling worker still drains a
  freshly-created ``ScoringJob`` row to ``completed`` under
  ``poll`` mode (regression guard for the failsafe path).

* ``tests/__init__.py`` and adjacent fund-backend tests untouched.

Deployment artifacts:

* ``deploy/arq/coherence-fund-arq-worker.service`` — systemd unit
  invoking ``python -m coherence_engine.server.fund.workers.arq_worker``;
  ``TimeoutStopSec=950`` exceeds ``job_timeout`` so the kernel does not
  SIGKILL during a graceful drain.
* ``deploy/arq/run_arq_worker.sh`` — shell launcher used by the unit
  and by ad-hoc operator runs.
* ``deploy/arq/values.yaml`` — Helm values block for the umbrella
  chart (``arqWorker.enabled=false`` by default; replicaCount, env,
  resources, livenessProbe, terminationGracePeriodSeconds).
* ``deploy/arq/upstash.env.example`` — Upstash Redis env template
  (TLS endpoint only — REST API is incompatible with Arq).
* ``deploy/arq/README.md`` — file index.

Documentation:

* ``docs/ops/worker_runbook.md`` (NEW) — backend-selection matrix,
  start/drain/restart procedures, Upstash quirks (TLS vs REST API),
  re-enqueueing a stuck job (``asyncio.run(enqueue_scoring_job(...))``
  with a unique idempotency key), failure-handling and observability
  (``arq.score_job.start`` / ``arq.score_job.done`` log markers,
  ``worker_ops_snapshot`` reuse), and the env/WorkerSettings
  configuration reference.

Verification:

  PYTEST_DISABLE_PLUGIN_AUTOLOAD=1 \
    python3 -m pytest tests/test_arq_worker.py \
                      tests/test_worker_backend_switch.py -v
  → 11 passed (or 10 passed, 1 skipped if ``arq`` is not installed).
