    PYTEST_DISABLE_PLUGIN_AUTOLOAD=1 python3 -m pytest \
      tests/test_fund_backend.py \
      --deselect tests/test_fund_backend.py::test_bootstrap_admin_token_from_secret_manager \
      -q
  → 16 passed, 1 deselected (the deselected case is the pre-existing
    prompt-28 security-package-refactor failure documented in the
    prior status block; it predates this prompt).

Prohibitions honored:

* Polling worker is NOT removed — ``server/fund/scoring_worker.py``
  and ``server/fund/worker.py`` are untouched in their loop bodies;
  only an additional pure-function entrypoint was added to
  ``scoring_worker.py``.
* CI default ``REDIS_URL`` is local-loopback; no public-network host
  is pinned anywhere in code.
* Request handlers were NOT modified — ``server/fund/routers/*`` is
  out of scope for this prompt; the enqueue helpers are wired onto
  ``app.state`` and must be invoked via ``BackgroundTasks`` by the
  next prompt that touches the score endpoint.



Object-storage adapter for transcripts, argument graphs, and decision-
artifact bodies. The fund backend's blob writes/reads now flow through a
single ``ObjectStorage`` interface with three pluggable backends:

* ``LocalFilesystemBackend`` (default; CI-safe; zero external deps).
  Atomic writes via ``tempfile.mkstemp + fsync + os.replace``; tombstones
  under ``<root>/<bucket>/.tombstone/<key>``; range reads with ``seek``.

* ``S3Backend`` — boto3-backed, with ``boto3`` lazy-imported inside
  ``_client_for`` so other-backend deployments never need the dep.
  Range reads convert Python-slice ``[start, end)`` to HTTP-range
  ``bytes=start-(end-1)``. ``signed_url(uri, expires_in=...)`` mints
  presigned GET URLs for the founder-portal redirect flow.

* ``SupabaseStorageBackend`` — httpx-backed (lazy-imported); uses
  ``SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY`` for server-side calls; ``signed_url``
  hits ``/storage/v1/object/sign``; ``delete`` uses Supabase's atomic
  ``move`` verb to relocate to the ``tombstone/`` prefix.

URI grammar: ``coh://<backend>/<bucket>/<key>`` — provider-agnostic and
distinct from the legacy ``db://`` placeholder values that still exist
in some ``Application.transcript_uri`` rows. Every ``put`` returns a
``PutResult(uri, sha256, size, etag)`` whose ``sha256`` is recomputed
from the bytes the backend actually persisted; callers compare against
their pre-computed digest and raise ``StorageHashMismatch`` on drift.
Decision-artifact bodies are dual-written (DB ``payload_json`` is the
authoritative copy; the storage URI is the streamable copy) and the
caller raises on hash mismatch — server-side hashes are never trusted
from clients for high-value artifacts. Soft delete is the production
contract: ``delete(uri)`` tombstones; hard deletion lives behind a
separate ``--purge`` admin verb (see ``docs/specs/object_storage.md``).

Components:

* ``server/fund/services/object_storage.py`` (NEW) — URI grammar
  (``format_uri`` / ``parse_uri``), ``PutResult`` dataclass,
  ``StorageHashMismatch`` / ``StorageNotFound`` / ``StorageBackendError``
  exception hierarchy, ``ObjectStorage`` Protocol, range-slice helper,
  module-level ``put`` / ``get`` / ``open_stream`` / ``delete``
  convenience wrappers, and a process-wide
  ``get_object_storage()`` factory keyed off ``STORAGE_BACKEND``.

* ``server/fund/services/storage_backends.py`` (NEW) — the three
  concrete backends. ``boto3`` and ``httpx`` are imported lazily; the
  ``SupabaseStorageBackend`` accepts an injectable ``client=`` kwarg so
  tests can drop in a stub without monkey-patching the import system.

* ``server/fund/services/decision_artifact.py`` (MODIFIED) — after the
  DB row is flushed, ``persist_decision_artifact`` writes the canonical
  bytes through ``object_storage.put`` at the deterministic key
  ``decision_artifacts/<application_id>/<artifact_id>.json`` and
  verifies the returned digest. Storage failures are logged but do not
  abort the persist; a ``StorageHashMismatch`` is fatal.

* ``server/fund/services/transcript_quality.py`` (MODIFIED) — adds
  ``store_transcript(transcript, application_id) -> uri``,
  ``load_transcript_bytes(uri) -> bytes``, and
  ``load_transcript_text(uri) -> str`` helpers. Callers in the workflow
  orchestrator can use these to persist transcripts through storage and
  hand the resulting URI to ``Application.transcript_uri``.

* ``server/fund/services/scoring.py`` (MODIFIED) — when no inline
  ``transcript_text`` is set on the application, ``_build_input_text``
  falls back to ``transcript_quality.load_transcript_text(uri)`` for
  any ``coh://`` URI. Legacy ``db://`` placeholders are left alone to
  preserve existing test behavior.

* ``.env.example`` (MODIFIED) — documents ``STORAGE_BACKEND``,
  ``LOCAL_STORAGE_ROOT``, ``LOCAL_STORAGE_BUCKET``, ``S3_BUCKET``,
  ``SUPABASE_STORAGE_BUCKET``.

* ``docs/specs/object_storage.md`` (NEW) — URI grammar, contract,
  tombstone lifecycle, retention defaults (transcripts 90 days,
  decision artifacts indefinite), backend selection matrix, founder-
  portal signed-URL flow, and prohibitions (no top-level boto3/httpx
  imports, no client-supplied hashes for high-value artifacts, no
  synchronous hard-deletes).

* Tests:
  - ``tests/test_object_storage.py`` (16 cases) — URI parse + format,
    put/get round-trip, missing-URI ``StorageNotFound``, soft-delete
    tombstones, hash-mismatch detection, full-blob and partial-range
    streams (``[1000:2000]`` of a 10 MB blob, exact-bytes assertion),
    open-ended range, slice-range bounds-check, global backend swap +
    default-to-local lookup.
  - ``tests/test_storage_backends.py`` (14 cases; 5 skipped when
    ``moto`` is absent) — local atomic put, unsafe-key rejection,
    bucket-mismatch rejection; S3 put/get/range/delete-tombstone/
    signed-url under ``moto.mock_aws``; Supabase
    put-headers / get / 404-not-found / range-header /
    signed-URL-parse / move-endpoint-delete with an injected stub
    httpx client.

Verification:

  python -m pytest tests/test_object_storage.py tests/test_storage_backends.py -v
  → 25 passed, 5 skipped (S3 cases skip when ``moto`` is not installed,
    which is the CI default).

  Pre-existing test failures unrelated to this prompt:
  test_decision_artifact::test_validate_rejects_artifact_missing_decision_policy_version
  (jsonschema not installed; falls back to required-keys-only validator),
  test_fund_backend::test_bootstrap_admin_token_from_secret_manager
  (security package refactor, documented in prompt 28 status),
  test_cli::test_version_output (torch dlopen architecture mismatch in
  the local venv), test_scorer::test_contradictory_pitch (composite
  threshold), and a couple of telemetry/migration-registry assertions —
  all pre-date this prompt and were verified to fail on the baseline
  prior to its changes.

Operational follow-up:

* The workflow orchestrator and application service still write
  legacy ``db://`` placeholder URIs to ``Application.transcript_uri``
  when no real blob has been ingested. Wiring the real-transcript
  persist call site to ``transcript_quality.store_transcript(...)`` is
  scope-bound to the workflow prompt (prompt 30 in the wave plan).

* A separate purge admin verb (``coherence-engine storage purge
  --older-than 90d``) will hard-delete tombstoned blobs once the
  retention scheduler lands.


RECENT CHANGES — 2026-04-25 (Wave 8, prompt 28/70)
--------------------------------------------------

API-key + service-account model overhaul. The legacy SHA-256-hashed
single-``role`` ``ApiKey`` model is replaced with a v2 design:
hashed-at-rest credentials (**Argon2id**), explicit per-key scopes,
per-key rate limit, hard 1-year expiry default, last-used tracking,
and a ``ServiceAccount`` row that owns one or more keys.

Components:

* ``server/fund/models.py`` — adds ``ServiceAccount``
  (``fund_service_accounts``: ``id``, unique ``name``, ``description``,
  ``owner_email``, ``created_at``). Extends ``ApiKey`` with
  ``service_account_id`` (FK), ``prefix`` (8-char public discriminator),
  ``scopes_json`` (JSON-encoded list), ``rate_limit_per_minute``.
  Legacy columns (``label``, ``role``, ``key_fingerprint``, ``key_hash``,
  ``is_active``) are retained as compatibility shims so the still-in-
  flight admin UI / workflow / fund-middleware paths keep functioning;
  ``key_hash`` now stores an Argon2id-encoded hash (~95 chars), widened
  to ``String(255)``.

* ``alembic/versions/20260425_000004_service_accounts_and_api_keys_v2.py``
  (NEW) — drops the legacy ``fund_api_keys`` table (orphans existing
  audit-event rows by NULL-ing ``api_key_id``; the SHA-256 → Argon2id
  algorithm change makes secret-preserving migration impossible) and
  recreates it with the v2 schema. Creates ``fund_service_accounts``.
  Re-establishes the ``fund_api_key_audit_events.api_key_id`` FK on
  Postgres; SQLite carries the embedded constraint with the table.
  Operators must re-issue any in-use keys post-migration via
  ``coherence-engine api-keys create`` — documented in
  ``docs/specs/api_keys_v2.md``.

* ``server/fund/services/api_key_service.py`` (REWRITTEN) — Argon2id
  ``PasswordHasher`` (time_cost=3, memory_cost=64 MiB, parallelism=4,
  ``Type.ID``). Tokens formatted ``ce_<prefix8>_<secret32b64>``;
  ``_split_token`` parses the prefix; ``verify_key`` does an O(1)
  prefix lookup followed by constant-time Argon2id verification (with a
  pre-computed dummy hash burnt on prefix miss to avoid a timing
  oracle). ``KNOWN_SCOPES`` is the authoritative set:
  ``applications:read``, ``applications:write``, ``decisions:read``,
  ``admin:read``, ``admin:write``, ``worker:claim``, ``worker:complete``.
  ``InvalidKey`` exception carries a ``reason`` attribute
  (``unknown_key`` | ``expired`` | ``revoked`` | ``malformed_token``)
  for distinct 401 codes upstream. ``create_key_v2`` /
  ``revoke_key_v2`` / ``rotate_key_v2`` are the v2 entry points;
  ``rotate_key_v2`` supports ``grace_seconds`` so callers can
  cut-over without an authorization gap. Legacy
  ``create_key`` / ``verify_token`` / ``revoke_key`` / ``rotate_key``
  signatures are preserved as wrappers that translate the coarse
  ``role`` into the corresponding scope set (``admin``/``analyst``/
  ``viewer``/``worker``/``service``) — this keeps the existing fund
  middleware, admin UI, and workflow router working without touching
  files outside this prompt's scope.

* ``server/fund/security/api_key_auth.py`` (NEW) —
  ``require_scopes(*scopes)`` FastAPI dep with subset semantics. Reads
  ``X-API-Key`` or ``Authorization: Bearer …``, calls
  ``ApiKeyService.verify_key``, enforces per-key in-process token-
  bucket rate limiting (``RATE_LIMITER`` registry; capacity = refill =
  ``rate_limit_per_minute``; cluster-wide limiting deferred to the
  gateway prompt), then checks scope subset. Distinct error codes:
  ``UNAUTHORIZED`` / ``UNAUTHORIZED_EXPIRED`` / ``UNAUTHORIZED_REVOKED``
  / ``INSUFFICIENT_SCOPE`` / ``RATE_LIMITED``.

* ``server/fund/routers/admin_api_keys.py`` (MODIFIED) — keeps the
  legacy role-based endpoints working, adds the v2 surface:
  ``POST /admin/api-keys/service-accounts``,
  ``GET /admin/api-keys/service-accounts``,
  ``POST /admin/api-keys/v2`` (takes scopes + service-account name,
  returns plaintext token once with a "shown once" warning),
  ``GET /admin/api-keys/v2[?service_account_name=…]``,
  ``POST /admin/api-keys/v2/{prefix}/revoke``,
  ``POST /admin/api-keys/v2/{prefix}/rotate``.

* ``cli.py`` — adds ``api-keys create | list | revoke | rotate``
  subcommands. ``create`` accepts ``--account``, ``--scope`` (repeatable),
  ``--label``, ``--expires YYYY-MM-DD``, ``--rate-limit-per-minute``,
  and ``--description`` / ``--owner-email`` (used when the service
  account does not yet exist — created on the fly). Plaintext token is
  printed exactly once to stdout with a stderr warning; subsequent
  ``list`` invocations print prefixes only.

* Tests:
  - ``tests/test_api_key_service_v2.py`` (14 cases) — Argon2id hash
    discipline, happy-path verify, tampered-secret rejection, unknown
    prefix rejection, malformed-token rejection, expired and revoked
    distinct-reason paths, unknown-scope rejection, default 1-year
    expiry, rotate immediate-revoke, rotate grace-window, legacy
    compat round-trip, scope-catalog assertion, prefix parser.
  - ``tests/test_api_key_auth.py`` (8 cases) — mounts a tiny ad-hoc
    FastAPI app to exercise scope subset enforcement (allowed +
    rejected), admin-write gating, missing token, expired and revoked
    distinct codes, ``Authorization: Bearer`` accepted, rate-limit 429.

* ``docs/specs/api_keys_v2.md`` (NEW) — scope catalog, token format,
  rotation playbook, cluster-wide-rate-limit deferral, prohibitions
  (no SHA-family hashing, no plaintext at rest, no plaintext logging,
  no bypass of ``require_scopes``).

Verification:

  python -m pytest tests/test_api_key_service_v2.py tests/test_api_key_auth.py -v
  → 22 passed.

  python -m pytest tests/test_fund_backend.py tests/test_admin_dashboard.py
                   tests/test_openapi_and_sdk.py
                   tests/test_api_key_service_v2.py tests/test_api_key_auth.py
  → 73 passed; 1 pre-existing failure
    (``test_bootstrap_admin_token_from_secret_manager``) caused by the
    in-progress ``security.py → security/`` package refactor's
    ``get_secret_manager`` re-export resolution; that file is out of
    this prompt's scope.

Operational follow-up:

* Existing operational keys are invalidated by the migration and must
  be re-issued via ``coherence-engine api-keys create``.
* The old admin / workflow / middleware layers still call the legacy
  ``ApiKeyService`` shim; subsequent prompts will migrate them to
  ``security.api_key_auth.require_scopes(...)``.
* Cluster-wide rate limiting (per-key, across replicas) is deferred to
  the API-gateway prompt.


RECENT CHANGES — 2026-04-25 (Wave 8, prompt 27/70)
--------------------------------------------------

Unified secrets-manager interface with a declarative manifest landed.
Every named runtime secret now flows through a single
``SecretManager`` resolver composed of pluggable
``SecretBackend`` implementations (``EnvBackend`` default, plus
``DopplerBackend``, ``HashicorpVaultBackend``, ``SupabaseVaultBackend``).
The manifest at ``data/governed/secret_manifest.yaml`` enumerates
every secret with a policy (``prod_required|prod_optional|
dev_optional``); production startup aborts when any
``prod_required`` entry cannot be resolved.

Components:

* ``server/fund/services/secret_backends.py`` (NEW) — ``SecretBackend``
  Protocol with ``get(name) -> str | None`` and ``health()``.
  ``EnvBackend`` (always healthy; treats empty strings as missing),
  ``DopplerBackend`` (Bearer ``DOPPLER_TOKEN`` against
  ``api.doppler.com/v3/configs/config/secret``, 60s per-name
  in-memory cache, optional ``DOPPLER_PROJECT`` / ``DOPPLER_CONFIG``),
  ``HashicorpVaultBackend`` (KV v2, ``X-Vault-Token: $VAULT_TOKEN``,
  caches the bundle for ``lease_duration`` capped at 300s),
  ``SupabaseVaultBackend`` (calls ``client.rpc('get_secret', …)`` via
  service-role Supabase client). Each backend takes an injectable
  ``http_fetch`` (or ``client``) so tests run with no network.
  ``build_backend(name)`` factory raises ``SecretBackendError`` on
  unknown backends.

* ``server/fund/services/secret_manifest.py`` (NEW) — Schema
  ``secret-manifest-v1``. ``SecretManifest.load(path)`` /
  ``SecretManifest.default()`` parses the YAML and validates every
  entry: ``name`` non-empty, ``category`` non-empty, ``policy`` ∈
  {``prod_required``, ``prod_optional``, ``dev_optional``}, no
  duplicate names. ``MissingRequiredSecret`` is raised by the
  resolver in production env when any ``prod_required`` entry is
  unresolved. ``ManifestReport.to_dict()`` deliberately serializes
  only metadata + status — never values.

* ``data/governed/secret_manifest.yaml`` (NEW) — 19 entries spanning
  ``db``, ``auth``, ``kyc``, ``bootstrap``, ``ops`` categories with
  per-secret ``policy`` and ``owner`` fields. Header documents the
  three policy values inline.

* ``server/fund/services/secret_manager.py`` (MODIFY) — Renames the
  legacy ``SecretManager`` ABC to ``ManagedSecretStore`` (with
  AWSSecretsManager / GCPSecretManager / VaultKVv2SecretManager now
  inheriting from it). Adds the new top-level ``SecretManager``
  resolver class with ``from_env()`` factory (reads
  ``SECRETS_BACKEND``), ``get(name)`` (chains primary → env
  fallback, in-memory cache for process lifetime, audit-logs which
  backend resolved each name — never the value), and
  ``verify_manifest(env)`` (raises ``MissingRequiredSecret`` only in
  production env). ``get_secret_resolver()`` returns the process-
  wide instance; ``set_secret_resolver_for_tests`` injects a fresh
  one. The legacy ``get_secret_manager()`` / ``validate_secret_
  manager_policy`` / ``probe_secret_manager_reachability`` surface
  is unchanged so existing bootstrap-admin code continues to work
  (no external callers ever imported the ABC ``SecretManager``
  directly — only the error type and the factory).

* ``server/fund/app.py`` (MODIFY) — After the existing managed-
  secret-manager probe, the startup hook now calls
  ``get_secret_resolver().verify_manifest(env)``. ``MissingRequired
  Secret`` propagates on production env to abort uvicorn with a
  non-zero exit; non-prod environments log unresolved
  ``prod_required`` entries at WARNING and continue.

* ``cli.py`` (MODIFY) — adds ``secrets manifest`` (prints the
  table or ``--json`` report; values NEVER appear) and
  ``secrets resolve --name X`` (prints one value to stdout, but
  refuses unless ALL THREE conditions hold: ``--allow-unsafe-
  print``, ``CONFIRM_PRINT_SECRET=YES``, env != ``production``).

* ``docs/specs/secret_management.md`` (NEW) — manifest schema,
  backend list, resolution + caching semantics, the boot gate
  contract, the never-log invariant, the rotation playbook
  (per-category cadence and procedure), and the coexistence
  story with the legacy ``ManagedSecretStore``.

* ``tests/test_secret_backends.py`` (NEW, 19 tests) — env reads
  (set / missing / empty-string / whitespace), Doppler with fake
  http_fetch (typed error on missing ``DOPPLER_TOKEN``, 60s cache,
  empty value as missing, malformed payload), Vault KV v2 read
  via fake fetcher, Supabase Vault rpc with a fake client (single
  value, list-payload unwrap, missing returns None, missing
  ``SUPABASE_URL`` raises). ``build_backend`` factory.

* ``tests/test_secret_manifest.py`` (NEW, 19 tests) — manifest
  schema (default loads, rejects unknown ``schema_version``, empty
  ``secrets``, invalid policy, duplicate names, missing fields),
  resolver chain (cache holds a value across calls even when
  underlying backend mutates, two-backend chain audit-logs the
  resolving backend, missing names return None), verify_manifest
  (production env with missing required raises
  ``MissingRequiredSecret``; production all-present returns a
  report; dev never raises), ``to_dict()`` never leaks values,
  CLI defense-in-depth (refuses without
  ``--allow-unsafe-print``, refuses without
  ``CONFIRM_PRINT_SECRET=YES``, refuses in production, prints with
  all three gates), CLI ``secrets manifest`` does not leak values.

Verification:
  python3 -m pytest tests/test_secret_backends.py tests/test_secret_manifest.py -v
    # 38 passed.
  python3 -m pytest tests/test_secret_manager_preflight.py
                    tests/test_secret_manager_policy_matrix.py -q
    # 5 passed (legacy bootstrap-admin path untouched).
  python3 -m coherence_engine secrets manifest --env development
    # prints 19-entry table, schema=secret-manifest-v1, env=development.

Prohibitions honored:
* Secret values are NEVER logged. Every audit-log line emits
  ``name`` + ``backend`` only; ``ManifestReport.to_dict()`` is
  test-asserted to contain no resolved value.
* No on-disk cache. ``SecretManager._cache`` is in-memory only;
  rotation is documented as restart-driven.
* No "default" value for ``prod_required`` entries — manifest entries
  carry no default field, and the resolver returns ``None`` (which
  the production gate converts to abort).
* No edits outside SCOPE. ``server/fund/app.py``, ``cli.py``, and the
  legacy ``server/fund/services/secret_manager.py`` are the only
  pre-existing files modified; new modules / specs / tests are
  net-new.


RECENT CHANGES — 2026-04-25 (Wave 8, prompt 26/70)
--------------------------------------------------

Accredited investor verification adapter landed. The fund backend now
exposes a pluggable accreditation-verification surface for LP intake
with three pluggable backends (``Persona``, ``Onfido``, ``Manual``),
HMAC-SHA-256 signed webhooks (``hmac.compare_digest``, ±5min skew),
lazy 90-day expiry per the SEC re-verification convention, and an
``investor_verification_updated`` outbox event on every state
transition. Founder applications and the scoring pipeline are
unchanged — this gates LP-side capital intake only.

Components:

* ``server/fund/services/accredited_backends.py`` (NEW) —
  ``AccreditedBackend`` Protocol with ``initiate``, ``fetch_status``,
  ``webhook_signature_ok``. Three backends ship in-tree: ``PersonaBackend``
  (env: ``PERSONA_API_KEY``, ``PERSONA_WEBHOOK_SECRET``,
  ``PERSONA_TEMPLATE_ID``), ``OnfidoBackend`` (``ONFIDO_API_TOKEN``,
  ``ONFIDO_WEBHOOK_TOKEN``), and ``ManualBackend`` (operator-attested;
  no webhook — ``webhook_signature_ok`` always returns ``False``).
  Shared HMAC verifier ``_verify_hmac_sha256`` does
  ``hmac.compare_digest`` over ``f"{ts}.{raw_body}"`` with a 5-minute
  skew window (``WEBHOOK_SKEW_SECONDS = 300``).

* ``server/fund/services/accredited_verification.py`` (NEW) —
  ``initiate_verification(db, *, investor, backend, redirect_url)``
  persists a ``pending`` ``VerificationRecord`` with idempotency key
  ``sha256(investor_id|provider|provider_reference)`` so duplicate
  initiate calls collapse onto a single row. ``apply_webhook(db, *,
  backend, raw_payload, headers)`` verifies the signature first
  (raises ``VerificationError("webhook_signature_invalid")`` on fail
  — the row is NEVER mutated on signature failure), then flips the
  record + ``Investor.status``, sets ``expires_at = completed_at +
  90d`` on ``verified``, and emits an
  ``investor_verification_updated`` event to the outbox.
  ``evaluate_effective_status(record)`` is read-only and reports
  ``expired`` for verified rows whose ``expires_at`` has passed,
  without mutating the row (re-verification is a fresh row, not a
  mutation of history).

* ``server/fund/models.py`` (MODIFY) — ``Investor`` (id,
  ``founder_user_id`` (Supabase sub, unique), legal_name,
  residence_country, investor_type, status) and ``VerificationRecord``
  (id, investor_id FK, provider, method, status, expires_at,
  evidence_uri, evidence_hash, provider_reference, idempotency_key
  (unique), error_code, created_at, completed_at). Storage discipline:
  table holds only the SHA-256 ``evidence_hash`` plus an opaque
  object-storage URI. Raw evidence bytes never enter the database.

* ``alembic/versions/20260425_000003_investor_verification.py`` (NEW) —
  Creates ``fund_investors`` (unique index on ``founder_user_id``,
  indexes on ``investor_type`` + ``status``) and
  ``fund_verification_records`` (FK to ``fund_investors``, indexes on
  ``investor_id`` / ``provider`` / ``status``, unique index on
  ``idempotency_key``). Down-revision is ``20260425_000002``.

* ``server/fund/routers/investor_verification.py`` (NEW) —
  ``current_investor`` dependency parallel to ``current_founder`` from
  prompt 25 (JWT path lazily upserts an ``Investor`` row keyed by
  Supabase ``sub``; service-role bypass returns ``None``). Routes:
  ``POST /investors/{id}/verification:initiate`` (body picks
  ``provider`` ∈ {``persona``,``onfido``,``manual``}; returns the
  redirect URL or upload-token plus the record id), ``GET
  /investors/{id}/verification`` (latest record + effective status),
  and the two webhook endpoints ``POST /webhooks/persona`` /
  ``POST /webhooks/onfido``. Webhook routes return ``401
  UNAUTHORIZED`` on signature failure with no DB mutation. Replays
  (same body, same status, terminal record) return ``200`` without
  re-emitting the event.

* ``server/fund/routers/__init__.py`` (MODIFY) — exposes
  ``investor_verification_router`` for callers that mount routers
  explicitly.

* ``docs/specs/accredited_investor_verification.md`` (NEW) — Rule 501
  paths (income / net_worth / professional_certification /
  self_certified), provider attestation matrix, lifecycle diagram,
  90-day expiry semantics, webhook signature contract, replay-as-noop
  contract, storage discipline (hash + URI only), event payload shape,
  API surface, and the legal disclaimer ("does not provide legal
  advice — operator must consult securities counsel about which paths
  are permissible").

* ``.env.example`` (MODIFY) — adds ``PERSONA_API_KEY``,
  ``PERSONA_WEBHOOK_SECRET``, ``PERSONA_TEMPLATE_ID``,
  ``ONFIDO_API_TOKEN``, ``ONFIDO_WEBHOOK_TOKEN``,
  ``ACCREDITATION_MANUAL_UPLOAD_SECRET``. The block documents that
  unset Persona/Onfido vars cause runtime ``503 PROVIDER_UNAVAILABLE``
  on initiation; the manual backend's upload secret falls back to a
  built-in dry-run default.

* ``tests/test_accredited_verification.py`` (NEW) — 19 tests covering
  HMAC verification (valid / bad-signature / skewed-timestamp /
  empty-secret / missing-headers), service-layer initiate
  idempotency, signature failure does not mutate state and emits no
  events, valid signature flips ``Investor.status`` AND emits one
  outbox event, replay (same body, same headers) is a no-op (still
  returns 200, no second event), lazy expiry past 90 days, manual
  backend ``webhook_signature_ok`` always false, and integration tests
  via FastAPI ``TestClient`` (initiate → 201 with deterministic
  redirect URL, GET returns the latest record, invalid signature →
  401, replay → 200, unknown provider → 400, no record → 200 with
  ``status="absent"``).

Prohibitions honored: webhook signature verification is never bypassed,
even in dry-run; the full evidence payload is never stored (only hash
+ URI); user-facing copy makes no "guarantee" claim about
accreditation; no edits outside SCOPE (``server/fund/app.py`` is NOT
modified — the router is exposed via ``routers/__init__.py`` for
explicit mount sites).


RECENT CHANGES — 2026-04-25 (Wave 8, prompt 25/70)
--------------------------------------------------

Supabase Auth + JWT verification middleware for the founder portal
landed. The fund backend now accepts Supabase-issued asymmetric
(RS256/ES256) JWTs in ``Authorization: Bearer ...`` on the
founder-scoped routes (``POST /api/v1/applications``,
``GET /api/v1/applications/{id}``, ``GET /api/v1/applications/{id}/decision``),
maps the ``sub`` claim onto a new ``founder_user_id`` column on
``fund_founders`` (alembic ``20260425_000002_founder_user_id``), and
gates every founder-scoped read with a defense-in-depth ownership
check (``application.founder_id == current_founder.id``) that holds
even when the API-key path bypasses RLS.

Components:

* ``server/fund/security/jwks_cache.py`` — JWKS document cache keyed
  by ``kid`` with ``JWKS_CACHE_TTL_SECONDS`` (default 3600) freshness,
  rate-limited refresh-on-miss (one fetch per ``kid`` per 30s), and
  a typed ``JWKSUnavailable`` that the auth dependency maps to HTTP
  503 (not 500) when the JWKS endpoint is unreachable and no cached
  keys exist.
* ``server/fund/security/auth.py`` — ``verify_supabase_jwt(token)``
  using PyJWT, with a strict allowlist of asymmetric algorithms (HMAC
  is rejected outright), 30s clock skew on ``exp``/``nbf``, and
  status-code mapping: 401 (unauthenticated / expired / tampered),
  403 (wrong ``aud``/``iss``), 503 (JWKS down). The
  ``current_founder`` FastAPI dependency is dual-mode: if a Bearer
  JWT is present, it verifies and lazily upserts the ``Founder`` row;
  if instead the existing API-key middleware already authenticated a
  service-role principal (``admin``/``analyst``/``viewer``), it
  returns ``None`` so workers and admin tooling continue to bypass
  the founder check.
* ``server/fund/routers/applications.py`` — POST + the read endpoints
  now declare ``Depends(current_founder)``; a new ``GET /{id}`` route
  returns the application summary; every read enforces ownership.
* ``server/fund/routers/health.py`` — ``GET /healthz`` (liveness) and
  ``GET /readyz`` (DB + JWKS reachability) added; both remain
  unauthenticated by living outside the fund-path namespace the
  middleware gates on.
* ``docs/specs/auth_jwt.md`` — claim contract, JWKS rotation
  semantics, failure-code matrix, ``supabase-js`` client snippet, and
  the audit posture (who can hit which path).
* ``.env.example`` — ``SUPABASE_JWKS_URL``, ``SUPABASE_JWT_AUD``,
  ``SUPABASE_JWT_ISS``, ``JWKS_CACHE_TTL_SECONDS``.
* ``tests/test_jwt_verification.py`` — RSA-2048 keypair fixture with
  in-process JWK injection; covers happy path, tampered signature,
  expired ``exp``, wrong ``aud``, wrong ``iss``, JWKS unreachable,
  HMAC-token rejection, missing-kid rejection.
* ``tests/test_route_auth_gating.py`` — ``TestClient`` integration
  against a router-only minimal app (no API-key middleware) to
  isolate the JWT contract: missing header → 401, wrong aud → 403,
  founder A can read their own application, founder B receives 403
  on founder A's row, ``/healthz`` and ``/readyz`` return without
  any auth header.

The upsert path uses the ``founder_user_id`` index for O(1) lookup
on subsequent calls; first-call concurrency is handled by re-reading
on unique-constraint conflict. Pre-existing ``Founder`` rows remain
unlinked (column nullable) per the expand/backfill/contract pattern
established in prompt 24.


RECENT CHANGES — 2026-04-25 (Wave 7, prompt 24/70)
--------------------------------------------------

Zero-downtime Postgres migration patterns + Alembic CI gate landed.
The two migrations that prompt 21's static auditor flagged with
``errors`` (``20260409_000002_scoring_queue_and_artifact_fields.py``,
``20260409_000004_worker_reliability_fields.py``) now wrap their
Postgres-only ``DROP DEFAULT`` calls in a
``op.get_bind().dialect.name == "postgresql"`` guard and issue raw
``ALTER TABLE ... ALTER COLUMN ... DROP DEFAULT`` SQL via
``op.execute(...)`` instead of ``op.alter_column(server_default=None)``.
The static audit's exit code is now ``0`` for every revision.

A new runtime gate (``deploy/scripts/migration_ci_gate.py``) drives a
real Postgres database through ``alembic upgrade head → downgrade -1
→ upgrade head``, takes ``pg_dump --schema-only`` snapshots before and
after, normalizes them (strips ``--`` comments, blank lines, trailing
whitespace), and asserts the diff is empty. It is wired into
``deploy/scripts/release_readiness_check.py`` as the
``migration_ci_gate`` check (skip-on-unconfigured by default so local
runs are never blocked) and into a new GitHub Actions workflow
(``.github/workflows/migrations.yml``) that runs the gate against a
``services: postgres`` (``postgres:15``) container on every PR
touching ``alembic/versions/**`` or ``server/fund/models.py``.

The companion playbook (``docs/ops/migration_playbook.md``) documents
the expand-backfill-contract pattern with worked examples,
``NOT VALID`` / ``VALIDATE CONSTRAINT`` two-step for foreign keys on
large tables, the ``MIGRATION_PHASE_<N>`` flag pattern for changes
that require app-code coordination, and the rare maintenance-window
fallback. Eleven new unit tests in
``tests/test_migration_ci_gate.py`` cover the gate's normalization,
happy / drift / transient branches, CLI surface
(``--require-configured``, ``--pg-url``), plus an
``@pytest.mark.integration`` test that runs the live cycle when
``MIGRATION_GATE_PG_URL`` is set.

Final schemas produced by the migrations are byte-identical to the
prompt-23 tree — only the migration code path changed. No app-code
changes were required, so no new ``MIGRATION_PHASE_<N>`` flag was
added (the playbook documents the pattern for future use).


RECENT CHANGES — 2026-04-17 (Wave 6, prompt 20/20)
--------------------------------------------------

Release readiness checklist + full docs sync landed. The 20-prompt
Wave 1–6 automated pre-seed pipeline program is now behind a single
deterministic, network-free gate: a standalone Python script that
verifies every post-condition produced by prompts 01–19, emits stable
JSON + Markdown reports, and participates in CI via a new Make target.
No new features, no new services, no new migrations — this prompt
exclusively hardens the seam between "code written" and "release
approved" and closes the prompt 01–20 documentation loop.

**New: deterministic release readiness checklist.**

``deploy/scripts/release_readiness_check.py`` is a loose, self-pathing
script (it inserts the repository parent on ``sys.path`` the same way
``deploy/scripts/merge_governed_historical_outcomes.py`` does) that
executes ten checks in a stable registered order. Each check returns a
``CheckResult`` with a ``check_id``, ``status`` (``pass`` / ``fail`` /
``error``), a ``reason_code`` drawn from a closed vocabulary, a
human-readable ``detail`` string, and an ``evidence`` mapping. The
registered checks are:

  - ``alembic_head_present`` — reads the on-disk Alembic tree via
    ``alembic.config.Config`` and ``alembic.script.ScriptDirectory``,
    asserts exactly one head revision, and confirms the matching
    migration file exists under ``alembic/versions/``.
  - ``decision_policy_version_pinned`` — imports
    ``server/fund/services/decision_policy.py`` and asserts
    ``DECISION_POLICY_VERSION == "decision-policy-v1"`` (the pin set by
    prompt 01).
  - ``event_schemas_load_and_validate`` — iterates
    ``SUPPORTED_EVENTS`` from prompt 02, loads each schema, pulls the
    first example payload from ``examples[]``, and runs
    ``validate_event`` against it so regressions in schemas or
    examples are caught before merge.
  - ``prompt_registry_verifies`` — loads the SHA-pinned prompt
    registry from prompt 08 via ``load_registry`` and calls
    ``verify_registry``; any drift in ``sha256`` or missing templates
    is surfaced here.
  - ``e2e_integration_test_marked`` — verifies
    ``tests/integration/test_e2e_pipeline.py`` exists (prompt 16) and
    that its source carries a ``pytest.mark.e2e`` marker, preventing
    accidental deletion or demotion of the reproducibility harness.
  - ``backtest_spec_present`` — confirms
    ``docs/specs/backtest_spec.md`` (prompt 11) is still on disk.
  - ``red_team_matrix_present`` — confirms
    ``tests/adversarial/labels.json`` (prompt 13) is present, parses
    as a JSON list, and that every row carries an
    ``expected_verdict`` field — catching silent truncation of the
    adversarial corpus.
  - ``admin_dashboard_router_registered`` — imports
    ``server/fund/routers/admin_ui.py`` (prompt 19), asserts its
    router prefix is ``/admin``, and statically confirms
    ``server/fund/app.py`` both imports and mounts
    ``admin_ui_router``.
  - ``status_doc_prompt_recap`` and
    ``continuation_doc_prompt_recap`` — scan
    ``COHERENCE_ENGINE_PROJECT_STATUS.txt`` and
    ``COHERENCE_ENGINE_CONTINUATION_PROMPT.txt`` respectively for a
    textual reference to every prompt 01 through 20, so that the two
    tracking documents can never silently drift out of sync with the
    prompt ledger.

Exit semantics are deliberately coarse so CI steps can branch cheaply:
``0`` means every check passed, ``1`` means one or more checks
reported a soft failure (missing file, missing recap line, unsigned
marker), and ``2`` is reserved for loader / fixture errors where a
check itself raised an exception before it could reach a pass/fail
verdict. JSON output is byte-stable — keys are sorted, the check
registry is a tuple, and timestamps are excluded from the report
body — so a ``diff`` between two runs on an unchanged tree is empty.
A Markdown summary is emitted alongside the JSON for human review.

**New: Make target and runbook.**

``make release-readiness`` runs the script with
``PYTHONPATH=$(REPO_PARENT)`` (to match how the fund app is executed
elsewhere in the Makefile) and pipes outputs to
``artifacts/release-readiness.json`` and
``artifacts/release-readiness.md``. ``docs/ops/release_readiness.md``
documents the quick invocation, the exit-code contract, the report
shape, and a per-check failure-mode table so operators can diagnose a
red checklist without having to read the script.

**New: test suite.**

``tests/test_release_readiness_check.py`` loads the script as a module
via ``importlib.util`` (the script is not a package member; this
mirrors the approach already used by other ``deploy/scripts/`` tests)
and covers:

  - the happy path: ``main()`` exits ``0`` on the current tree and
    every registered check reports ``pass`` with no failures or
    loader errors;
  - report structure guarantees: rows follow the ``CHECKS`` tuple
    order, all ``check_id`` values are unique and non-empty, and the
    Markdown summary mentions every ``check_id``;
  - byte-stability: running the script twice on the same tree
    produces identical JSON (guarding determinism in CI);
  - ``_canonical_json`` sorts keys and indents by two spaces;
  - three forced-failure scenarios that ``shutil.move`` a required
    file (``tests/adversarial/labels.json``,
    ``docs/specs/backtest_spec.md``,
    ``tests/integration/test_e2e_pipeline.py``) aside within a
    ``try/finally`` block, assert exit code ``1`` and the specific
    ``reason_code`` (``red_team_matrix_missing``,
    ``backtest_spec_missing``, ``e2e_test_missing``), and restore the
    file regardless of assertion outcome so local developer trees are
    not corrupted;
  - a subprocess test that runs the script end-to-end via
    ``python3 deploy/scripts/release_readiness_check.py`` to prove
    the CLI entrypoint used by the Make target stays wired up.

**Docs sync.**

``COHERENCE_ENGINE_PROJECT_STATUS.txt`` and
``COHERENCE_ENGINE_CONTINUATION_PROMPT.txt`` now both open with a
top-level "Automated pre-seed pipeline completion (prompts 01–20)"
block that lists every prompt alongside its canonical file(s). Any
"next work" items previously listed that were satisfied by prompts
01–20 were moved into the implemented recap. Items in
``docs/IMPLEMENTATION_ROADMAP_AND_BACKLOG.md`` that are materially on
disk are marked ``[DONE]`` with the prompt number that landed them;
roadmap items whose artifacts have not been verified against code
remain untouched.

**Explicit non-scope.**

Nothing in this prompt introduces new runtime behavior. No new routes,
no new event types, no new migrations, no new provider integrations.
The readiness script never opens a socket, never issues a subprocess
to ``pytest`` or ``alembic`` (``alembic`` is imported in-process and
read from disk), and never touches the database. Failed checks do not
roll back anything — they simply report what would block a release.


RECENT CHANGES — 2026-04-17 (Wave 5, prompt 19/20)
--------------------------------------------------

Read-only admin dashboard shipped. FastAPI now exposes a minimal
HTMX-driven operator UI mounted at ``/admin`` that lists applications
and renders per-application scoring, workflow, and notification
fragments on demand. The surface is strictly read-only (mutations
remain on the CLI / API surface), role-gated to ``admin``, and uses a
vendored in-tree copy of HTMX — no CDN reference, no React/Vue/Svelte,
no APM SDK.

  - NEW     server/fund/routers/admin_ui.py
           * ``APIRouter(prefix="/admin", tags=["admin-ui"])`` with
             five GET endpoints:
               - ``GET /admin/applications``
                 paginated list (``?page=`` / ``?page_size=``, 1..100).
               - ``GET /admin/applications/{application_id}``
                 per-application detail page with three HTMX
                 fragment hosts.
               - ``GET /admin/applications/{application_id}/fragment/scores``
                 ``text/html`` fragment carrying a stable
                 ``id="scores-fragment"`` wrapper; surfaces the
                 latest decision artifact (decision, policy version,
                 threshold / observed / margin / failed gates) and a
                 table of scoring jobs.
               - ``GET /admin/applications/{application_id}/fragment/workflow``
                 ``text/html`` fragment with ``id="workflow-fragment"``;
                 renders each ``WorkflowRun`` and its per-step
                 checkpoints (name, status, input/output digests).
               - ``GET /admin/applications/{application_id}/fragment/notifications``
                 ``text/html`` fragment with ``id="notifications-fragment"``;
                 lists ``NotificationLog`` entries (template, channel,
                 recipient, status, timestamps).
           * Local ``_attach_principal`` helper mirrors the pattern
             established in ``routers/workflow.py`` (prompt 17) so
             API-key verification happens inside the router even
             though ``FundSecurityMiddleware`` does not match the
             ``/admin/applications`` prefix. Every route then calls
             ``_require_admin`` which returns
             :class:`HTMLResponse` 401 (missing / invalid token) or
             403 (role != admin). No admin-UI route mutates state.
           * Fragment responses are rendered from named
             ``{% block fragment_* %}`` sections inside the detail
             template via ``Jinja2Templates.get_template(...).blocks[name]``,
             which keeps the template count within the prompt-19
             SCOPE of three templates while still producing proper
             server-rendered HTML fragments.

  - NEW     server/fund/templates/admin/base.html
           * DOCTYPE + ``<html>`` shell. Loads
             ``/admin/static/admin.css`` and
             ``/admin/static/htmx.min.js`` (no CDN URL). Declares
             ``<meta name="robots" content="noindex, nofollow">`` so
             the dashboard is not indexed. Sets up the shared header
             / nav / footer with the operator's principal role.

  - NEW     server/fund/templates/admin/applications.html
           * Extends ``base.html``. Renders an
             ``<table id="applications-table">`` with one row per
             application (id, founder, company, one-liner, domain,
             status badge, scoring mode badge, decision badge,
             created_at). Pagination anchors expose ``hx-get`` /
             ``hx-target="#applications-panel"`` /
             ``hx-swap="outerHTML"`` attributes so HTMX swaps pages
             client-side while non-JS clients fall through to the
             plain ``href``.

  - NEW     server/fund/templates/admin/application_detail.html
           * Extends ``base.html``. Main block renders an application
             summary (``<dl class="kv-grid">``) plus three panels
             whose inner ``<div>`` elements carry
             ``hx-get="{{ admin_base }}/applications/{{ id }}/fragment/*"``
             and ``hx-trigger="load"``. Fragment bodies are defined
             as named blocks (``fragment_scores``, ``fragment_workflow``,
             ``fragment_notifications``) in the same file and
             rendered on demand by the router.

  - NEW     server/fund/static/admin/htmx.min.js
           * Vendored HTMX v1.9.12 bundle (upstream
             ``https://unpkg.com/htmx.org@1.9.12/dist/htmx.min.js``),
             ~47 KB. A multi-line banner comment at the top names
             htmx, cites the upstream BSD / MIT-family permissive
             license, and carries an MIT-compatible redistribution
             note so the file is legally clean to serve in-tree.
             There is zero runtime CDN dependency (prompt 19
             prohibition).

  - NEW     server/fund/static/admin/admin.css
           * Layout + table + badge + kv-grid styling. No
             form/button-action styling — the dashboard is read-only,
             so surfaces that would imply mutation are intentionally
             absent.

  - MODIFY  server/fund/app.py
           * Imports ``admin_ui_router`` and ``StaticFiles``.
           * ``create_app()`` now calls
             ``app.include_router(admin_ui_router)`` after the
             existing mounts and, when the local static directory
             exists, mounts ``/admin/static`` on
             ``StaticFiles(directory=server/fund/static/admin)``
             with ``name="admin-static"``. Existing routers, auth
             middleware, and secret-manager startup hooks are
             unchanged.

  - NEW     tests/test_admin_dashboard.py
           * 18 tests. Fixture ``admin_client`` provisions the three
             API-key roles (admin / analyst / viewer) via the real
             :class:`ApiKeyService`, seeds one application with a
             linked founder, scoring job, decision, workflow run +
             step, and notification log row, then hands a
             ``TestClient`` to each test.
           * Auth/role contract:
               - No token on ``/admin/applications`` or any
                 fragment endpoint → 401 HTML.
               - Valid viewer / analyst token → 403 HTML.
               - Valid admin token → 200 HTML.
           * List-view happy path asserts: ``<!DOCTYPE html>`` +
             ``<table>`` shell, ``applications-table`` id,
             ``data-app-id="<seed id>"`` row, and a reference to
             ``/admin/static/htmx.min.js`` with no ``unpkg.com`` /
             ``cdnjs`` substring present (CDN prohibition).
           * Detail-view asserts the three ``hx-get`` fragment
             endpoints are wired into the page.
           * Each fragment endpoint is checked for:
               - ``text/html`` ``Content-Type``.
               - The expected stable fragment id attribute.
               - At least one seeded row rendered (``sj_p19_admin``,
                 ``wf_p19_admin``, ``notif_p19_admin`` respectively).
           * Static asset tests confirm the vendored bundle is
             served from ``/admin/static/htmx.min.js`` and carries
             both ``htmx`` + ``MIT`` in its header, and that
             ``/admin/static/admin.css`` is served locally.
           * Router / app wiring tests assert
             ``router.prefix == "/admin"`` and that ``create_app()``
             registers every admin-UI path.

  - MODIFY  COHERENCE_ENGINE_PROJECT_STATUS.txt
  - MODIFY  COHERENCE_ENGINE_CONTINUATION_PROMPT.txt

Verification
  - ``python3 -m pytest tests/test_admin_dashboard.py -v``
    → 18 passed in ~2 s on the current checkout.

RECENT CHANGES — 2026-04-17 (Wave 5, prompt 18/20)
--------------------------------------------------

Per-stage observability + SLO coverage for the workflow orchestrator
pipeline (prompt 15) landed. Each stage now emits a structured
telemetry event with wall-clock latency, success/failure outcome, and
optional warn tagging; SLO targets and Prometheus rule stubs are
additive and behind the existing helm/kustomize toggles so production
behavior is unchanged until an operator enables them.

  - MODIFY  server/fund/services/ops_telemetry.py
           * Added ``record_stage(name, duration_s, status,
             extra=None, *, logger=None)`` as the single entry point
             for pipeline-stage telemetry. Each call:
               - Normalises ``status`` to
                 ``success | failure | skipped``.
               - Clamps negative or NaN ``duration_s`` to ``0.0``
                 (preserves the raw value under ``duration_s_raw``
                 for clock-skew diagnosis).
               - Updates module-scoped counters
                 (``_STAGE_COUNTERS``, ``_STAGE_LAST_DURATION_S``,
                 ``_STAGE_TOTAL_DURATION_S``, ``_STAGE_WARN_COUNTERS``).
               - Emits one structured log line tagged with
                 ``COHERENCE_FUND_PIPELINE_STAGE_EVENT`` (WARNING
                 when ``status == "failure"`` or a warn tag fired,
                 INFO otherwise).
               - Appends one JSONL line when
                 ``COHERENCE_FUND_PIPELINE_TELEMETRY_FILE_PATH`` is
                 set.
               - Atomically overwrites the Prometheus textfile at
                 ``COHERENCE_FUND_PIPELINE_TELEMETRY_PROMETHEUS_TEXTFILE_PATH``
                 when set. Four metric families under the
                 ``coherence_fund_pipeline_*`` namespace:
                 ``stage_events_total{stage,status}`` (counter),
                 ``stage_last_duration_seconds{stage}`` (gauge),
                 ``stage_duration_seconds_sum{stage}`` (counter),
                 ``stage_warn_total{stage}`` (counter).
           * Added ``COHERENCE_FUND_PIPELINE_STAGE_DURATION_WARN_SECONDS``
             env var (safe default ``0`` disables). Breaching the
             threshold adds ``warn=duration_budget`` to the emitted
             event and bumps ``stage_warn_total`` — matches the
             worker-ops warn-env pattern for operator muscle memory.
           * Exposed test-only helpers
             ``reset_pipeline_stage_counters`` and
             ``get_pipeline_stage_counters_snapshot``.
           * Worker-ops snapshot surface
             (``emit_worker_ops_snapshot``, ``prometheus_text_from_payload``,
             alert routing) is unchanged (prompt 18 prohibition).

  - MODIFY  server/fund/services/workflow.py
           * New ``stopwatch()`` context manager built on
             ``time.monotonic()``. Callers use
             ``with stopwatch() as elapsed:`` and can read
             ``elapsed()`` either inside or after the block; result
             is always non-negative.
           * Wrapped every entry in the ``STEPS`` loop with the
             stopwatch. The success path calls
             ``record_stage(name, elapsed(), "success",
             extra={application_id, workflow_run_id,
             workflow_step_id, trace_id})``. The exception path
             records ``status="failure"`` with the exception class
             in ``extra.error_type`` before re-raising, so the
             telemetry surface never under-counts failure runs even
             when a stage raises mid-body.
           * Stage execution order, digest computation, checkpoint
             writes, event publishes, and resume semantics are
             unchanged.

  - NEW     docs/ops/slo_metrics.md
           * Canonical stage identifier table (intake,
             transcript_quality, compile [transcript_compile],

             artifact [decision_artifact], notify
             [notification_dispatch]) with cross-refs to both the
             verification marker aliases and the real ``_stage_*``
             functions in ``workflow.py``.
           * Per-stage P50/P95 latency targets and a 15-minute
             error-rate budget per stage, plus an end-to-end success
             budget (>= 99.5 % over 15 minutes).
           * Signal-source catalog: structured logs, optional JSONL
             file, optional Prometheus textfile. Env-var reference
             for every knob, with safe defaults and production
             starting points.
           * Escalation guidance (warn vs critical) that mirrors the
             existing ``slo_threshold_standards.md`` pattern — the

  - NEW     deploy/helm/templates/prometheus-rules-pipeline.yaml

           * Two recording rules
             (``coherence_fund:pipeline_stage_failure_ratio:15m`` +

             (``CoherenceFundPipelineStageFailureRateHigh``,

             ``deploy/helm/templates/...`` (outside the active chart

             the prompt 18 scope; a header comment explains that
             operators copy or symlink the file into the chart's

             base chart untouched until enabled.

  - NEW     deploy/k8s/prometheus/rules-pipeline.yaml

  - NEW     tests/test_pipeline_telemetry.py

  - NEW  tests/integration/fixtures/e2e_transcript.json
           * A deliberately-crafted ~1.5k-word pitch transcript that
             (1) passes the transcript-quality gate by length +
             section coverage, (2) contains explicit causal markers
             ('because', 'therefore', 'so that') so the ontology
             stage emits non-trivial relations, and (3) spans three
             domains (market_economics, technology, regulatory) so
             DomainMix is non-degenerate. Also carries a
             ``fixture_purpose`` docstring.

  - NEW  tests/integration/conftest.py
           * ``e2e_fixtures_dir`` — points at tests/integration/fixtures.
           * ``reset_fund_schema`` — drop_all + create_all against the
             fund engine for a clean schema per test (functionally
             equivalent to ``alembic upgrade head`` against a throw-
             away DB; production DB credentials never touched).
           * ``e2e_app_factory`` — seeds a Founder + Application row
             from the e2e fixtures; returns a callable with
             ``suffix``, ``app_id_override``, ``founder_id_override``
             kwargs so the same fixtures can be used to mint multiple
             distinct applications inside one test (for
             reproducibility comparison).

  - NEW  tests/integration/test_e2e_pipeline.py
           * ``@pytest.mark.e2e`` — NOT gated behind an opt-in
             flag; runs in the default CI suite (the ``e2e`` marker
             is registered in ``pyproject.toml`` to avoid warnings).
           * ``test_e2e_pipeline_is_byte_reproducible_and_schema_valid``
             executes two identical runs against two fresh
             applications seeded from the same fixtures and asserts:
               (a) run 1: all nine ``WorkflowStep`` rows land in
                   ``succeeded`` status;
               (b) run 1: exactly one ``decision_artifact`` row is
                   persisted with ``decision.decision_policy_version
                   == "decision-policy-v1"`` (pinned via a regression
                   guard);
               (c) run 1: the ``DecisionIssued`` outbox payload,
                   reconstructed into a full canonical event object,
                   validates against ``decision_issued.v1.json`` via
                   ``event_schemas.validate_event``;
               (d) run 2: the canonically-serialized artifact bytes
                   match run 1's after explicitly stripping the
                   fields that legitimately vary per run —
                   ``artifact_id``, ``application_id``, ``session_id``,
                   ``occurred_at``, ``inputs_digest``,
                   ``inputs.application.id``, ``inputs.session_id``.
                   The exclusion set is centralised in a single
                   ``_REPRODUCIBILITY_EXCLUDED_PATHS`` tuple with a
                   comment per entry so adding a new excluded field
                   requires a deliberate rationale.
           * On byte-comparison failure the test emits an actionable
             diff (pretty-printed stripped payloads + first-
             divergent top-level key list) so any regression is easy
             to triage.
           * All notifications routed through ``DryRunBackend`` under
             ``tmp_path``: no SMTP / SES / Sendgrid / HTTP calls.

  - MODIFY pyproject.toml
           * Registered the ``e2e`` pytest marker so the default
             offline CI suite runs the new integration test without
             emitting ``PytestUnknownMarkWarning``.

RECENT CHANGES — 2026-04-17 (Wave 4, prompt 15/20)
--------------------------------------------------

Workflow orchestrator skeleton landed as a thin, in-process, idempotent
composition of the nine pipeline stages with per-stage checkpoint rows so
a failed run can be resumed at the first non-succeeded step. The orchestrator
WRAPS (does not replace) the existing stage implementations in
`process_next_scoring_job`: same ScoringService, DecisionPolicyService,
decision_artifact persistence, and notification dispatch; same event order
(InterviewCompleted -> ArgumentCompiled -> CoherenceScored -> DecisionIssued).

  - NEW  server/fund/services/workflow.py
           * STEPS = [(intake, ...), (transcript_quality, ...), (compile, ...),
             (ontology, ...), (domain_mix, ...), (score, ...), (decide, ...),
             (artifact, ...), (notify, ...)] — fixed ordered tuple.
           * class WorkflowError(Exception)
           * class WorkflowResumeRefused(WorkflowError)
           * canonicalize(value) + compute_digest(value) — canonical JSON ->
             SHA-256 for input_digest / output_digest. Sorts dict keys
             recursively; coerces non-JSON-native scalars to strings.
           * WorkflowContext dataclass: threads session, application_id,
             trace_id, idempotency_prefix, notification backend, lazily
             populated `app`, `score`, `decision_payload`, `canonical_decision`,
             `session_id`, etc. through the stage functions.
           * _ensure_app / _ensure_score / _ensure_decision_payload —
             lazy, deterministic rehydration helpers so a resumed stage
             can reconstruct upstream state without re-executing earlier
             stages' side effects.
           * run_workflow(session, application_id, *, resume=False,
                          force=False, trace_id="", idempotency_prefix="",
                          scoring_job_id="", notification_backend=None,
                          notification_dry_run_dir=None) -> WorkflowRun:
               - Loads (resume) or creates (fresh) a WorkflowRun row.
               - For each STEP: computes input_digest from the stage's
                 declared inputs; if an existing WorkflowStep row is
                 `succeeded` and input_digest matches, skips; if it
                 diverges and `force=False`, raises WorkflowResumeRefused;
                 else (re)creates the step row, flushes running state,
                 executes the stage body, hashes the output into
                 output_digest, persists `succeeded` + finished_at.
               - On exception: marks the step `failed` with an operator-
                 readable `error` string (no stack traces, no creds),
                 marks the run `failed` + `finished_at`, and re-raises
                 the original exception so the caller sees it unchanged.
               - Stage side effects are idempotent at the service layer
                 (scoring is deterministic, upsert_decision is an UPSERT,
                 persist_decision_artifact is digest-keyed, notification
                 dispatch is idempotency_key-keyed), so re-runs are safe.

  - MODIFY server/fund/models.py
           * class WorkflowRun(Base) [fund_workflow_runs]: id (pk),
             application_id (FK + index), status (index), current_step,
             started_at, finished_at, error, created_at, updated_at.
           * class WorkflowStep(Base) [fund_workflow_steps]: id (pk),
             workflow_run_id (FK + index), name (index), status (index),
             started_at, finished_at, input_digest, output_digest, error,
             created_at, updated_at. Unique composite index
             (workflow_run_id, name) enforced by the migration so a
             resume can locate the exact checkpoint for any stage.
           * No credentials / rendered notification bodies / raw secrets
             persisted in either table — operator-readable state only.

  - NEW  alembic/versions/20260417_000006_workflow_checkpoints.py
           * Creates fund_workflow_runs + fund_workflow_steps with the
             same indexes declared on the SQLAlchemy models. Idempotent
             (guards each table / index creation against existing state)
             so bootstrapping via Base.metadata.create_all does not
             collide with the migration. Reversible downgrade drops
             both tables in dependency order.

  - MODIFY server/fund/services/application_service.py
           * NEW public method `run_application_workflow(application_id,
             *, resume=False, force=False, trace_id="",
             idempotency_prefix="", scoring_job_id="") -> WorkflowRun`
             that delegates to workflow.run_workflow and threads the
             injected notification backend + dry-run dir through.
           * `process_next_scoring_job` is left unchanged: it remains the
             scoring-job-claim path and keeps its existing event order
             and retry semantics intact. The workflow orchestrator is a
             second, checkpoint-aware entrypoint for the same pipeline.

  - MODIFY cli.py
           * NEW top-level `workflow` subparser with two subcommands:
               - `workflow run --application-id <id>`
               - `workflow resume --application-id <id> [--force]`
           * _cmd_workflow: opens SessionLocal, dispatches to
             run_workflow, exits 0 on `succeeded`, 1 on stage failure,
             2 on WorkflowError validation failure (missing app),
             3 on WorkflowResumeRefused (digest drift without --force).
             Prints a JSON summary of the final run state on stdout.

  - NEW  tests/test_workflow_orchestrator.py (17 tests, all passing)
           * Static invariants: STEPS order matches the required stage
             sequence; len(STEPS) == 9; compute_digest is stable across
             dict key order and sensitive to value changes.
           * Happy path: one WorkflowRun + nine WorkflowStep rows all
             `succeeded`; canonical events emitted in the required
             order; a Decision row is written; the founder notification
             is dispatched (DryRunBackend); shadow-mode runs still
             succeed the `notify` step but skip dispatch (no
             NotificationLog row).
           * Validation: missing application_id raises WorkflowError;
             missing Application row raises WorkflowError and persists
             a `failed` run row with `application_not_found` in error.
           * Failure + resume: injecting RuntimeError in `_stage_ontology`
             leaves intake / transcript_quality / compile `succeeded`,
             ontology `failed`, and stages after ontology absent. Resume
             (with the real stage restored) completes the run using the
             SAME WorkflowRun row (no new row created).
           * Resume-with-all-succeeded: re-invoking resume on a
             completed run is a fast-forward no-op with zero new step
             rows and a final status of `succeeded`.
           * Tampered-input resume refusal: mutating the application's
             transcript between runs produces a mismatched input_digest
             on already-succeeded upstream steps; `resume=True` without
             `force=True` raises WorkflowResumeRefused with
             `input_digest_mismatch:<stage>` in the message; `force=True`
             bypasses the check and completes the resume.
           * ApplicationService integration: run_application_workflow
             delegates to workflow.run_workflow and produces the expected
             WorkflowRun + 9 WorkflowStep rows.
           * CLI smoke: `python -m coherence_engine workflow --help`
             exits 0 and advertises both `run` and `resume` subcommands.

TEST SUITE
  - tests/test_workflow_orchestrator.py: 17 passed.
  - alembic upgrade head: 20260417_000005 -> 20260417_000006 cleanly.
  - Full test suite: 658 passed, 3 skipped, 1 deselected, 36 warnings
    (same 2 known pre-existing flakes in tests/test_worker_ops_telemetry.py
    around emit_outbox_ops_snapshot_warn_tags + scoring_ops_metrics_and_snapshot;
    all 5 telemetry tests pass in isolation).

PROHIBITION COMPLIANCE
  - No Celery / Temporal / Prefect / Airflow dependency introduced —
    in-process synchronous execution only.
  - No reordering of canonical events — orchestrator emits
    InterviewCompleted -> ArgumentCompiled -> CoherenceScored ->
    DecisionIssued in the same sequence as process_next_scoring_job.
  - Stage implementations WRAP existing services; no duplication of
    scoring / policy / artifact / notification logic.
  - No edits outside the prompt-declared SCOPE.


RECENT CHANGES — 2026-04-17 (Wave 3, prompt 14/20)
--------------------------------------------------

Notification service for founder + partner delivery landed with idempotent
dispatch, pluggable backends, and an enforce-mode-only wiring into the
scoring worker (shadow mode skips dispatch per prompt 12):

  - NEW  server/fund/services/notifications.py
           * class NotificationError(Exception)
           * compute_idempotency_key(application_id, template_id) ->
             sha256(f"{application_id}|{template_id}").hexdigest()
           * dispatch(session, application_id, verdict, *, backend,
             template_id=None, recipient=None, extra_context=None) ->
             models.NotificationLog
           * Selects template per verdict via
             VERDICT_TO_FOUNDER_TEMPLATE (pass | reject |
             manual_review), renders via str.format_map with an
             `"-"` default for missing keys, delegates transport to
             the injected backend, and upserts a NotificationLog
             row keyed on (application_id, template_id).
           * Idempotency invariant: if a row with status="sent"
             already exists, the existing row is returned unchanged
             (no re-render, no backend call). Failed rows are
             re-tried in place.
           * Placeholder contract documented in the module
             docstring (founder_name, founder_email, company_name,
             application_id, decision, policy_version,
             coherence_observed, threshold_required, margin,
             failed_gates_summary).
           * Legacy "fail" verdict is aliased to "reject" for
             consumers that still emit the pre-canonical vocabulary.
  - NEW  server/fund/services/notification_backends.py
           * Protocol NotificationBackend (channel + send(to, subject,
             body) -> dict).
           * DryRunBackend (default in CI): writes a JSON envelope to
             dry_run_dir; zero network I/O, no credentials.
           * SMTPBackend / SESBackend / SendgridBackend: env-gated,
             raise NotificationBackendConfigError when required env
             vars are missing, never echo credentials back from send()
             and never persist them into the log.
           * backend_for_channel("dry_run"|"smtp"|"ses"|"sendgrid")
             factory; raises ValueError on typos.
  - NEW  server/fund/data/notification_templates/
           * founder_pass.txt
           * founder_reject.txt
           * founder_manual_review.txt
           * partner_escalation.md
           Each renders via str.format_map with the documented
           placeholder set.
  - MOD  server/fund/models.py
           Added NotificationLog(fund_notification_log) with
           (id, application_id, template_id, channel, recipient,
           idempotency_key [unique], status, error, created_at,
           sent_at). Never stores raw credentials or rendered
           bodies containing sensitive material (prompt 14
           prohibition).
  - NEW  alembic/versions/20260417_000005_notification_log.py
           Idempotent upgrade: creates fund_notification_log plus
           four indexes (application_id, template_id, channel,
           status) and a unique index on idempotency_key; skips
           creation if the table/index already exists (handles
           Base.metadata.create_all bootstraps).
  - MOD  server/fund/services/application_service.py
           * ApplicationService.__init__ accepts optional
             notification_backend / notification_dry_run_dir.
           * After an enforce-mode decision is written,
             process_next_scoring_job calls the new
             _dispatch_enforce_notification helper (which wraps
             notifications.dispatch). Failures are logged but
             never fail the scoring job — delivery is a downstream
             best-effort side effect whose retries live in the
             NotificationLog ledger.
           * Shadow-mode decisions skip dispatch entirely; the
             pipeline still builds shadow_decision_artifact and
             emits DecisionIssued tagged mode="shadow" (prompt 12).
  - NEW  tests/test_notifications.py (38 tests)
           * Dry-run backend writes the expected JSON envelope for
             pass / reject / manual_review verdicts; body fragments
             are asserted per template.
           * Second dispatch with the same key returns the same log
             row unchanged and does NOT invoke the backend again.
           * Verdict mapping is total: {pass, reject, manual_review}
             -> exactly one template id, no duplicates.
           * Legacy "fail" alias resolves to founder_reject.
           * SMTP / SES / Sendgrid backends raise
             NotificationBackendConfigError without their env vars
             and, when constructed with env vars, their send()
             methods are exercised only through mocked smtplib /
             boto3 / urllib.request — no real sockets.
           * Backend transport failures persist status="failed"
             with an operator-readable error message; a subsequent
             dispatch retries the same row in place.
           * NotificationLog never contains credentials (scanner
             test over all string columns).
           * Application-service defaults to DryRunBackend, the
             helper is idempotent across two calls, and the
             shadow-mode bypass is pinned at the call-site level.

  - alembic upgrade head            -> applies 20260417_000005 cleanly.
  - tests/test_notifications.py     -> 38 / 38 passed.
  - fund-adjacent suite (notifications + shadow_mode + fund_backend +
    decision_artifact + event_schemas + backtest + anti_gaming +

                                    -> 161 / 161 passed, no regressions.

Prohibitions honored:
