    target_account_ref column carries that token only. The migration
    + docs spec out the storage discipline.

    set_backend_factory_for_tests seam swaps backends with in-tree
    synthetic instances that emit deterministic intent / confirmation
    refs.
  * No edits outside SCOPE. Files modified: server/fund/models.py,

PROMPT 52 — E-SIGNATURE ADAPTER (DOCUSIGN / DROPBOX SIGN) FOR SAFE NOTES
  Goal: a single internal interface (ESignatureProvider) for sending
  SAFE / term-sheet documents through one of two providers (DocuSign,
  Dropbox Sign / formerly HelloSign), tracking lifecycle status,
  verifying webhook signatures, and persisting only the SIGNED PDF
  (never the unsigned body) to object storage. Templates ship as
  PLACEHOLDERS — production use requires securities-counsel review.
  This software does not provide legal advice.

  - NEW  alembic/versions/20260425_000010_signature_requests.py
         fund_signature_requests (id, application_id, document_template,
         template_vars_hash, provider, provider_request_id, status,
         signed_pdf_uri, signers_json, idempotency_key, created_at,
         sent_at, completed_at) with unique index on idempotency_key
         and indices on application_id / status / provider_request_id.
  - MOD  server/fund/models.py
         SignatureRequest ORM row backing the migration. The model
         docstring documents the storage discipline (only the
         template id + vars hash are persisted, never the unsigned
         body) and the operator obligation (templates are placeholders
         until reviewed by securities counsel).
  - NEW  server/fund/services/esignature.py
         ESignatureProvider protocol (prepare / send / void /
         fetch_signed_artifact / webhook_signature_ok), Signer +
         PreparedDocument + SendResponse + SignedArtifact value
         types, ESignatureService owning the SignatureRequest
         lifecycle: prepare renders the template IN MEMORY and
         discards the body; send re-renders + dispatches to the
         provider and asserts the vars hash hasn't drifted;
         apply_webhook is idempotent and uploads the signed PDF to
         object storage on `signed`.
  - NEW  server/fund/services/esignature_backends.py
         DocuSignBackend (reads DOCUSIGN_INTEGRATION_KEY,
         DOCUSIGN_USER_ID, DOCUSIGN_RSA_PRIVATE_KEY,
         DOCUSIGN_CONNECT_HMAC_SECRETS) +
         DropboxSignBackend (reads DROPBOX_SIGN_API_KEY).
         Connect HMAC v2 verifier
         (verify_docusign_webhook_signature) iterates active
         secrets × X-DocuSign-Signature-N headers and uses
         hmac.compare_digest. Dropbox Sign verifier
         (verify_dropbox_sign_webhook_signature) recomputes
         HMAC-SHA-256(api_key, event_time + event_type) and
         compare_digest's against event.event_hash; the backend
         additionally accepts the X-DropboxSign-Signature
         raw-body HMAC header.
  - NEW  server/fund/data/legal_templates/safe_note_v1.docx.j2
         Plain-text Jinja2 placeholder for the YC post-money SAFE.
         NOT counsel-reviewed. Variables: company_name,
         investor_name, investor_entity, purchase_amount_usd,
         valuation_cap_usd, discount_rate_pct, effective_date,
         signer_company_name, signer_investor_name.
  - NEW  server/fund/data/legal_templates/README.md
         States the operator obligation explicitly: replace each
         template with a counsel-approved version before any
         production signature request. This software does not
         produce legal advice.
  - NEW  server/fund/routers/esignature_webhooks.py
         POST /webhooks/esignature/docusign and
         POST /webhooks/esignature/dropbox-sign. Both routes call
         backend.webhook_signature_ok against the raw body +
         headers BEFORE any state mutation; signature failure
         returns HTTP 401 with no DB writes. Successful
         deliveries call ESignatureService.apply_webhook which
         is idempotent on duplicates. Test seams
         set_docusign_backend_for_tests +

Prompt 52 prohibitions honored:
  * Webhook signature verification is NEVER skipped. Both routes
    return 401 on a missing or invalid signature header and do not
    write to the database. There is no env-gated dev bypass.
  * The placeholder SAFE template is NOT published as
    counsel-reviewed -- the README and the docs spec both state
    explicitly that production templates must be reviewed by the
    operator's securities counsel and that this software does not
    provide legal advice.

    returns a PreparedDocument whose body is in-memory only;
    ESignatureService.prepare and .send both delete the document
    reference after dispatch. The database stores only the template
    id and a SHA-256 of the canonical-JSON variable map.

PROMPT 53 — KYC/AML ADAPTER FOR FOUNDERS (PERSONA / ONFIDO)
  Goal: founder-side sanctions / PEP / ID / AML screening, mandatory
  upstream of any capital instruction. Persists a KYCResult row per
  founder with annual refresh cadence. Re-screen on every funding
  event. Distinct from prompt 26's accredited-investor flow (which
  gates LP intake under Rule 501) -- separate tables, separate
  provider env vars, separate routers, separate webhook URLs so a
  leaked LP-flow secret cannot forge a founder webhook.

  - NEW  alembic/versions/20260425_000011_founder_kyc.py
         fund_kyc_results (id, founder_id, provider, status,
         screening_categories, evidence_uri, evidence_hash,

         and indices on founder_id / provider / status.
  - MOD  server/fund/models.py

         opaque evidence reference are persisted -- raw KYC document

         reset_kyc_backend_factory_for_tests.
  - NEW  tests/test_founder_kyc.py

PROMPT 54 — CALENDAR / SCHEDULING ADAPTER (CAL.COM + GOOGLE CALENDAR)
  Goal: auto-book partner meetings on every enforce-mode `pass`
  decision. Two pluggable backends sit behind a Scheduler interface
  -- Cal.com (primary) and Google Calendar (fallback for personal
  calendars). On `pass`, ApplicationService emits
  `scheduling_requested`; the scheduler queries availability,
  proposes the top three slots, and on founder click-through books
  the chosen slot, writes a Booking row, and emits `meeting_booked`.

  - NEW  alembic/versions/20260425_000012_scheduling.py
         fund_meeting_proposals (id, application_id, partner_email,
         founder_email, duration_min, proposed_slots_json [Text JSON
         -- not JSONB so SQLite + Postgres share one definition],
         token [unique], status [pending|booked|expired|cancelled],
         backend, created_at, expires_at, booked_at, cancelled_at)
         and fund_bookings (id, proposal_id [unique FK],
         application_id, backend, provider_event_id, partner_email,
         founder_email, scheduled_start, scheduled_end, status,
         created_at). Indices on application_id, token (unique),
         status; bookings unique on proposal_id.
         down_revision = "20260425_000011".
  - MOD  server/fund/models.py
         MeetingProposal + Booking ORM rows backing the migration.
         Lifecycle docstrings reference docs/specs/scheduling.md.
  - NEW  server/fund/services/scheduler.py
         Scheduler class with propose() / book(); errors
         SchedulerError / ProposalNotFoundError / TokenExpiredError /
         ProposalCancelledError. Token TTL defaults to 72h
         (DEFAULT_PROPOSAL_TTL_HOURS = 72). Hard cap of three
         proposed slots (MAX_PROPOSED_SLOTS = 3). Idempotent book:
         a second call with the same token returns the existing
         Booking with idempotent_replay=True and never invokes the
         backend twice. Helper emit_scheduling_event() publishes
         the scheduling_requested outbox event.
  - NEW  server/fund/services/scheduler_backends.py
         SchedulerBackend protocol. CalComBackend (lazy-imports
         requests; reads CALCOM_API_KEY / CALCOM_API_BASE /
         CALCOM_EVENT_TYPE_ID). GoogleCalendarBackend (lazy-imports
         google-auth + google-api-python-client; reads
         GOOGLE_CALENDAR_OAUTH_*). InMemorySchedulerBackend (test
         seam, raises on double-book). Slot/BookedEvent dataclasses
         are UTC-enforced. _pick_top_three collapses duplicate
         starts and hard-caps at three. scheduler_backend_from_env()
         factory keyed on SCHEDULER_PROVIDER (defaults to "calcom").
  - NEW  server/fund/routers/scheduling.py
         POST /scheduling/proposals (analyst/admin gated; 503 on
         PROVIDER_UNAVAILABLE). POST /scheduling/book (404 on
         unknown token, 410 GONE on expired token, 409 on cancelled,
         200 with idempotent_replay=true on a repeated successful
         booking). Test seams set_scheduler_factory_for_tests /
         set_scheduler_backend_factory_for_tests with reset
         helpers.
  - MOD  server/fund/services/application_service.py
         On `pass` + enforce-mode, emits `scheduling_requested` via
         the existing EventPublisher (idempotency_key
         <scoring_job.idempotency_key>:SchedulingRequested).
         Failure is logged but does NOT fail the scoring job.
         Helper _resolve_partner_email() reads
         SCHEDULER_DEFAULT_PARTNER_EMAIL with a deterministic
         fallback.
  - NEW  tests/test_scheduler.py
         24 tests. Slot validation, in-memory backend cap of 3,

         service-layer propose persists 3 distinct slots with TTL
         == 72h; empty availability marks proposal "expired"; book
         writes Booking + flips status; book idempotent on
         repeated token (single Booking row, idempotent_replay=

    pathway and hard-caps the output; Scheduler.propose also

Prompt 56 — Regulatory pathway selector (Reg D 506(b) /
Reg D 506(c) / Reg CF / Reg S) + jurisdictional gate.

Wave 15 (depends on 26 + 53). Classifies each application
against the *operator-configured* registry of securities
pathways and downgrades a `pass` decision to `manual_review`
when the resolved pathway is not clear. The software does
NOT pick a pathway autonomously and does NOT provide legal
advice; the registry is owned by the operator's licensed
securities counsel.

         schema_version: regulatory-pathways-v1. Ships four

         reg_s) with counsel_signoff_at: null so they default
         to `unclear` until counsel signs off. Global TTL
         counsel_signoff_ttl_days: 90. Per-pathway fields:
         jurisdiction (US | non_US), investor_requirement
         (accredited_verified | self_certified | none),
         advertising (permitted | prohibited), max_investors
         (null = unlimited), integration_window_days,

         counsel_signoff_by.

         (frozen). load_pathway_registry(path=None) parses +
         validates the YAML (rejects schema mismatch, unknown
         jurisdiction, duplicate ids). classify(application,
         *, registry, now=None) -> PathwayMatch with the
         deterministic non-defaulting algorithm (jurisdiction
         filter -> advertising filter -> investor_requirement
         check -> counsel signoff freshness check). Statuses:
         "clear" | "unclear" | "ambiguous". Boolean shortcut:
         regulatory_pathway_clear(application, *, registry,

  - MOD  server/fund/services/decision_policy.py

Prompt 56 prohibitions honored:
  * Do NOT silently default to a pathway: classify()
    returns "ambiguous" -> REGULATORY_PATHWAY_AMBIGUOUS when
    the candidate set is empty or contains > 1 match; the
    decision policy downgrades any pass envelope to
    manual_review for both UNCLEAR and AMBIGUOUS.
  * Do NOT advertise or solicit on a 506(b) pathway: the
    advertising filter only emits 506(b) as the candidate
    when application advertising_mode == "prohibited"; an
    application declaring "permitted" advertising can never
    resolve to 506(b).
  * Do NOT permit pass without counsel signoff when
    configured: _signoff_fresh() returns False for both
    missing signoff_at and stale signoff_at, forcing
    "unclear" and downgrading the decision.
  * No edits outside SCOPE. Files modified:
    server/fund/models.py,
    server/fund/services/decision_policy.py,
    COHERENCE_ENGINE_PROJECT_STATUS.txt,
    COHERENCE_ENGINE_CONTINUATION_PROMPT.txt. Files created:
    the YAML registry, the service module, the migration,
    the test module, the docs spec.

Prompt 57 — Data retention + GDPR/CCPA right-to-delete with
crypto-shredding. Wave 15, depends on prompt 29
(object-storage tombstoning). Adds per-row AES-256-GCM
encryption keys keyed on row id (AAD-bound), a daily
retention sweep that tombstones URIs + crypto-shreds the
per-row key + flips redacted=true, and a two-phase erasure
endpoint with 30-day grace + audit-hold refusal.

  - NEW  server/fund/services/per_row_encryption.py
         AES-256-GCM with 96-bit nonce + AAD = row_id; key
         material fetched from a pluggable
         EncryptionKeyStore (default backed by the new
         fund_encryption_keys table; swappable for KMS).
         Public surface: encrypt(plaintext, db, row_id,
         key_id?) -> (key_id, b64ct), decrypt(b64ct, db,
         row_id, key_id) -> bytes, KeyShreddedError /
         CiphertextCorrupt / KeyNotFoundError.
  - NEW  server/fund/services/crypto_shred.py
         shred_key(db, key_id) zeros key_material_b64 +
         stamps shredded_at + writes shred audit log.
         Idempotent: re-shredding returns False. Unknown
         key_id raises KeyNotFoundError so a typo at the
         caller can never silently fail.
  - NEW  data/governed/retention_policy.yaml
         schema_version: retention-policy-v1. Classes:
         transcript (90d, tombstone_and_shred),
         interview_recording (90d, tombstone_and_shred),
         decision_artifact (indefinite, KEEP),
         audit_log (indefinite, KEEP),
         kyc_evidence (1825d, tombstone_and_shred — BSA
         5yr; verify with counsel),
         founder_pii (2555d, tombstone_and_shred).
  - NEW  server/fund/services/retention.py
         load_retention_policy() validator (rejects keep
         with finite retention_days). apply_retention(db)
         daily sweep walks every class, selects rows past
         horizon (filtering already-redacted ones),
         tombstones every URI via object_storage.delete,
         crypto-shreds the per-row key, marks
         redacted=True with redaction_reason="retention:
         <class>". execute_erasure(db, request_id) targets
         a single ErasureRequest, splits requested classes
         via assess_erasure_classes, refuses audit-hold
         classes with ERASURE_REFUSED_AUDIT_HOLD, emits
         erasure_completed.
  - NEW  server/fund/routers/privacy.py
         POST /privacy/erasure/issue (admin/support):
         mints a one-shot URL-safe verification_token,
         returns plaintext exactly once, persists only the
         SHA-256 hash on a pending ErasureRequest row.
         POST /privacy/erasure (subject): hashes the
         submitted token server-side, looks up the matching
         row, refuses any request that targets an
         on_expiry=keep class with
         ERASURE_REFUSED_AUDIT_HOLD, otherwise schedules
         scheduled_for=now+30d (admin can collapse via
         immediate=true), emits erasure_scheduled. Replays
         are idempotent. Handler returns "scheduled" only —
         never "completed" — per the prompt-57 prohibition.
  - MOD  server/fund/models.py
         New tables: EncryptionKey
         (fund_encryption_keys: id, key_material_b64,
         created_at, shredded_at, shred_reason),
         ErasureRequest (fund_erasure_requests: subject_id,
         subject_type, status, verification_token_hash
         unique, issued_by, requested_at, scheduled_for,
         completed_at, immediate, classes_json,
         refusal_reason, request_id, last_error). New
         columns on fund_applications, fund_kyc_results,
         fund_interview_recordings: <class>_key_id (fk
         analogue to fund_encryption_keys.id), redacted
         bool default false, redacted_at, redaction_reason.
  - NEW  alembic/versions/20260425_000014_retention_and_erasure.py
         Creates fund_encryption_keys + fund_erasure_requests
         tables, adds <class>_key_id + redaction tombstone
         columns to fund_applications,
         fund_interview_recordings, fund_kyc_results.
         All new columns nullable / default-false so the
         migration is safe over a populated DB without
         backfill.
  - NEW  tests/test_retention.py
         Policy YAML loads + validates (rejects keep with
         finite retention_days). Aged transcript →
         tombstoned + key shredded + redacted=True;
         decryption afterward raises KeyShreddedError.
         decision_artifact rows are inspected but never
         touched. Sweep is idempotent. AES-GCM AAD binding
         rejects ciphertext swapped between rows with
         CiphertextCorrupt.
  - NEW  tests/test_erasure_endpoint.py
         Two-phase issue + schedule: subject endpoint
         schedules within 30 days with the expected class
         set. Bogus token → 401 UNAUTHORIZED. Token reused
         against wrong subject_id → 401. Requesting
         decision_artifact → status=refused,
         refusal_reason=ERASURE_REFUSED_AUDIT_HOLD.
         Replays are idempotent (same row, idempotent=true).
         immediate=true requires admin role. The handler
         never returns status=completed before
         execute_erasure runs, and a redacted row maps to
         HTTP 410 Gone with the redaction_reason surfaced.
  - NEW  docs/specs/data_retention.md
         Threat model (GDPR Art.17 / CCPA + audit-hold for
         decision artifacts), policy table, crypto-shred
         mechanics (AES-256-GCM + AAD, encoded blob
         layout), daily retention worker contract, two-

         operator runbook (router wiring + cron + KMS swap
         + token revocation), prompt-57 prohibitions

  - MOD  COHERENCE_ENGINE_CONTINUATION_PROMPT.txt

  python3 -m pytest -p "no:pytest-qt" \
    coherence_engine/tests/test_retention.py \
    coherence_engine/tests/test_erasure_endpoint.py -v
  → 7 + 8 = 15 passed.

Prompt 57 prohibitions honored:
  * Do NOT erase audit-trail data (decisions, audit logs):
    retention.assess_erasure_classes splits any requested
    class set against the policy and refuses the entire
    request with ERASURE_REFUSED_AUDIT_HOLD when any class
    is on_expiry=keep. The daily sweep skips kept classes
    entirely (decision_artifact / audit_log inspected but
    never tombstoned).
  * Do NOT confirm erasure to the requestor before the
    deletion job actually completes: the privacy router
    returns status="scheduled" and never status=
    "completed". The DB row is flipped to "completed" only
    by retention.execute_erasure(), which runs after
    scheduled_for is reached.
  * Do NOT trust client-supplied verification_token without
    server-side validation: the handler hashes the
    submitted token (hash_verification_token) and looks
    up the ErasureRequest row by SHA-256 hash. Subject_id
    mismatch on a real token still returns 401
    UNAUTHORIZED. The plaintext token is never persisted.
  * No edits outside SCOPE. Files modified:
    server/fund/models.py,
    COHERENCE_ENGINE_PROJECT_STATUS.txt,
    COHERENCE_ENGINE_CONTINUATION_PROMPT.txt. Files
    created: per_row_encryption.py, crypto_shred.py,
    retention.py, retention_policy.yaml, privacy.py,
    20260425_000014_retention_and_erasure.py,
    test_retention.py, test_erasure_endpoint.py,
    data_retention.md.


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
RECENT CHANGES — Wave 16, prompt 61/70 (OpenTelemetry distributed tracing)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  - NEW  server/fund/observability/__init__.py
         Package init for the new observability surface.
  - NEW  server/fund/observability/otel.py
         Builds a process-wide TracerProvider, attaches the
         OTLPSpanExporter (gRPC) + ConsoleSpanExporter, runs the
         PIIScrubSpanProcessor before exporters, applies a
         ParentBased(TraceIdRatioBased) sampler whose ratio is
         dev=1.0 / test=1.0 / staging=0.10 / prod=0.01 (override via
         OTEL_TRACES_SAMPLER_ARG), installs the W3C traceparent +
         baggage propagators, and runs the FastAPI / SQLAlchemy /
         HTTPX / Redis auto-instrumentors. OTel is an OPTIONAL
         import: if the SDK isn't present `init_tracing` becomes a
         logged no-op and `get_tracer` returns a no-op proxy whose
         `start_as_current_span` is a context-manager stub.
         `_LazyTracer` re-resolves the global provider on every span
         start so module-level `_TRACER = get_tracer(...)` bindings
         remain correct after `install_in_memory_exporter` swaps the
         provider in tests.
  - MOD  server/fund/config.py
         Adds OTEL_EXPORTER_OTLP_ENDPOINT, OTEL_TRACES_EXPORTER, and
         OTEL_SERVICE_NAME pydantic fields with matching uppercase
         aliases; field names match the standard OTel env vars so
         any vendor / collector that already understands OTel needs
         no shim.
  - MOD  server/fund/app.py
         Calls `init_tracing(service_name=..., environment=...,
         fastapi_app=app)` BEFORE any router is mounted so the
         FastAPI instrumentor wraps the ASGI stack at the outermost
         layer.
  - MOD  server/fund/workers/arq_worker.py
         `on_startup` calls `init_tracing(...)` for the worker
         process; `score_job`, `dispatch_outbox`, and `run_backtest`
         are wrapped with `tracer.start_as_current_span("arq.<name>")`
         spans and tagged with `application.id`, `arq.job_id`, and
         `arq.job_try`.
  - MOD  server/fund/services/scoring.py
         `score_application` opens a parent `score.application`
         span tagged with the application id (no PII) and emits one
         `score.layer.<name>` child span per coherence layer plus a
         `score.domain_comparator` span for the domain comparison
         step. PII fields like `one_liner` are intentionally NOT
         attached to spans.
  - MOD  server/fund/services/object_storage.py
         The module-level `put` / `get` / `open_stream` / `delete`
         convenience wrappers now emit
         `object_storage.<verb>` spans tagged with backend, bucket,
         key, content_type, size_bytes, and (for puts) the
         server-recomputed sha256.
  - NEW  tests/test_otel_tracing.py
         9 tests, all green when the SDK is installed (and skipped
         cleanly otherwise). Covers: surface smoke; basic span
         capture; PII scrub for `user.email` and
         `http.request.header.authorization`; the per-environment
         sampler ratio table; `OTEL_TRACES_SAMPLER_ARG` overrides;
         `score.application` is the parent of every
         `score.layer.<name>` span; `traceparent` propagation across
         a mocked outbound HTTPX call (the propagated trace id
         matches the active span's trace id); object-storage spans
         carry the documented attributes.
  - NEW  docs/ops/otel.md
         Operator-facing reference — module layout, exporter env
         vars, sampling ratio table, PII scrub key list, W3C
         propagation contract, runbook (verify a trace lands,
         force-sample one canary, disable tracing entirely, the
         no-OTel fallback), and the prompt-61 prohibitions.
  - MOD  COHERENCE_ENGINE_PROJECT_STATUS.txt
         Updated header + this change block.
  - MOD  COHERENCE_ENGINE_CONTINUATION_PROMPT.txt
         Prompt-61 block promoted to MOST RECENT PROMPT;
         prompt-60 demoted to SUPERSEDED.

Prompt 61 prohibitions honored:
  * Do NOT export traces with PII attributes:
    `PIIScrubSpanProcessor` redacts every key in `PII_SCRUB_KEYS`
    on `on_end` so every exporter (OTLP / Console / in-memory)
    sees `<redacted>`. The test suite asserts this for both
    `user.email` and `http.request.header.authorization`.
  * Do NOT use 100% sampling in prod: the prod default is 1%
    (`TraceIdRatioBased(0.01)` wrapped in `ParentBased`); the
    documented incident-response play is to canary one instance
    via `OTEL_TRACES_SAMPLER_ARG`.
  * Do NOT make OTel a hard import for tests: the otel module
    wraps every OTel import in `try` and degrades to no-op stubs;
    the test module is `pytest.skipif`'d on a no-OTel
    environment; `InMemorySpanExporter` is the test sentinel.

Prompt 66 — Pre-commit hooks + ruff + mypy strict + frontend lint
──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Wave 17. Lands the unified style + pre-commit gate that prompts
67-70 build on top of (CI lint job, code review SLAs, etc.).

Goal: every commit, both locally and in CI, passes the same set of
hooks. Developers cannot land code that ruff or mypy --strict would
reject, cannot push directly to `main`, cannot smuggle in
trailing-whitespace / large binaries / malformed YAML, and the three
frontend apps lint on the same prettier+eslint baseline.

Files created:
  * .pre-commit-config.yaml — top-level hook manifest. Repos:
      - pre-commit-hooks v4.6.0: trailing-whitespace,
        end-of-file-fixer, check-yaml, check-json, check-toml,
        check-added-large-files (--maxkb=1024),
        check-merge-conflict, no-commit-to-branch (--branch main).
      - astral-sh/ruff-pre-commit v0.6.9: `ruff` (with --fix
        --exit-non-zero-on-fix) and `ruff-format`.
      - local hook `mypy`: invokes `python -m mypy --config-file
        pyproject.toml server core` (require_serial: true).
      - dotenv-linter v3.3.0 against `.env.example`.
      - local eslint hooks per app
        (founder_portal / partner_dashboard / site) using
        `npx --no-install eslint --max-warnings=0` so warnings
        break the build.
    Top-level `exclude` skips generated SDKs (`sdk/`,
    `apps/*/src/sdk/`), lockfiles, and the `.git.broken_*` parking
    folders so we never auto-format generated clients.
  * .editorconfig — `indent_size=4` for Python, `=2` for the
    JS/TS/YAML/MD/Astro/CSS family, tabs for Makefile,
    `trim_trailing_whitespace=false` for `.md`, LF + final-newline
    everywhere. Mirrors what ruff-format and prettier emit.
  * apps/site/.eslintrc.json — `eslint:recommended` +
    `@typescript-eslint/recommended` + `prettier` + the
    `astro-eslint-parser` override for `.astro` files. Ignores
    `dist/`, `.astro/`, `node_modules/`, `public/`, the lighthouse
    helper script.
  * tests/test_pre_commit_runs.py — config-validity smoke test.
    Always-on assertions: YAML parses, every repo declares hooks,
    the required hook IDs are present (trailing-whitespace,
    end-of-file-fixer, check-yaml, check-json, check-toml,
    check-added-large-files, no-commit-to-branch, ruff,
    ruff-format, mypy, dotenv-linter), `pyproject.toml` carries
    `[tool.ruff]` / `[tool.mypy]` / `strict = true`. Two
    skip-when-pre-commit-missing tests: `pre-commit
    validate-config` and a full `pre-commit run --all-files`
    gated behind `RUN_PRE_COMMIT_SMOKE=1` (the live run pulls
    remote hook envs and takes minutes; CI uses the lint job
    instead).
  * docs/specs/code_style.md — reference doc covering the tool
    matrix, ruff rule sets and per-file ignores, mypy strict
    policy (tests are typed, no bare `# type: ignore`,
    suppressions must carry an error code), eslint+prettier
    setup, the pre-commit lifecycle, and the explicit
    prohibitions (no `--no-verify`, no commits to `main`, no
    auto-formatting generated SDKs).

Prompt 67 — Release pipeline (semver + changelog + signed images
              + helm chart)                                  [DONE]
══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════

Wave 17. Adds the tag-triggered release pipeline that publishes
container images, helm chart, GitHub Release, and opens the
post-release VERSION-bump PR.

What landed:

* `scripts/release/changelog.py` — conventional-commit parser +
  Markdown renderer. Pure-Python, deterministic, network-free.
  Recognizes `feat|fix|perf|refactor|docs|test|build|ci|chore|revert`
  with optional `(scope)` and `!` breaking marker; `BREAKING
  CHANGE:` in the body also triggers the breaking section.
  Headers that don't match the conventional-commit pattern are
  preserved (mapped to `chore`) so commits are never silently
  dropped.
* `scripts/release/cut_release.py` — release driver. Reads
  current `VERSION`, parses commits (from git or a JSON
  fixture), infers next semver bump (major if breaking, minor
  if any feat, else patch), renders the release-scoped
  changelog. Flags:
    --since/--until        previous tag → HEAD
    --fixture              JSON commit log (deterministic tests)
    --bump                 override (major|minor|patch|auto)
    --require-readiness    delegate to release_readiness_check.py;
                           non-zero exit aborts the release
    --dry-run              print plan; do not write VERSION/CHANGELOG.md
    --write                edit VERSION + prepend CHANGELOG.md
    --release-notes-out    artifact for `gh release create --notes-file`
    --json-out             machine-readable plan summary
* `Dockerfile` — multi-stage backend image
  (python:3.11-slim-bookworm, builder venv → runtime),
  non-root `app` user, tini PID-1, /live healthcheck,
  OCI labels populated from GIT_SHA/GIT_TAG/BUILD_DATE
  build args.
* `apps/founder_portal/Dockerfile`,
  `apps/partner_dashboard/Dockerfile` — multi-stage
  Next.js 14 standalone images (deps → build → runtime),
  non-root, tini, OCI labels. Founder ports 3001, partner 3002.
* `deploy/helm/Chart.yaml` + `deploy/helm/values.yaml` —
  umbrella chart that wraps the existing
  `deploy/helm/coherence-fund/` subchart via a
  `file://./coherence-fund` dependency. The
  `deploy/helm/charts/coherence-fund` symlink lets
  `helm template deploy/helm` render in-place without
  needing `helm dependency build` first. The
  pre-existing `deploy/helm/templates/prometheus-rules-pipeline.yaml`
  stub stays as-is (gated `if .Values.prometheusRules.enabled`,
  defaults to false).
* `.github/workflows/release.yml` — tag-triggered jobs added
  alongside the existing `workflow_dispatch` deploy path.
  All workflow_dispatch jobs are now gated
  `if: github.event_name == 'workflow_dispatch'`. New jobs
  (gated `github.event_name == 'push' && startsWith(github.ref,
  'refs/tags/v')`):
    release_lint_test       ruff + mypy strict + full pytest
    release_readiness_gate  deploy/scripts/release_readiness_check.py
                            (strict abort on non-zero)
    release_changelog       cut_release.py --require-readiness;
                            uploads CHANGELOG_RELEASE.md +
                            release-plan.json
    release_build_sign      matrix [backend, founder-portal,
                            partner-dashboard]: docker buildx
                            push to GHCR, then `cosign sign --yes`
                            (keyless OIDC) and
                            `cosign attest --type slsaprovenance`
                            on every image digest before any
                            downstream job consumes it.
    release_helm_chart      helm lint + helm template + helm
                            package + helm push (OCI) +
                            `cosign sign` of the chart digest +
                            `cosign sign-blob` of the .tgz
                            (detached signature for offline
                            verification).
    release_publish         build wheel + sdist, gh release create
                            --notes-file CHANGELOG_RELEASE.md
                            with helm tgz + sig + wheel + sdist
                            attached, then opens
                            release/post-<version>-version-bump
                            PR against main.
  Permissions block elevated to id-token:write,
  contents:write, packages:write, pull-requests:write so the
  signing + publish + bump-PR steps can succeed.
* `tests/test_release_pipeline.py` — 10 tests:
    - cut_release.py --dry-run is deterministic across runs
      (same fixture → identical changelog + plan)
    - changelog groups conventional commits into the canonical
      sections in canonical order, breaking header section
      first
    - release notes file is written even with --dry-run
      (it's an output artifact, not a destructive mutation)
    - changelog module unit tests for type classification
      and section ordering
    - umbrella chart has Chart.yaml + values.yaml + the
      charts/coherence-fund subchart link
    - helm template + helm lint when helm is on PATH
      (skipped otherwise)
    - release.yml has the v*.*.* tag trigger and `cosign`
      references
    - Dockerfile is multi-stage, uses `USER app` (no root)
* `docs/ops/release.md` — operator runbook. Explains:
  - the conventional-commits → semver bump table,
  - the per-job pipeline,
  - the cosign verify recipes for image, chart, and
    SLSA provenance attestation,
  - the prohibition guardrails (readiness gate, sign-before-
    consume, mandatory VERSION-bump PR),
  - manual hot-fix flow (still goes through the tag trigger).

Verification (run now):
  python3 scripts/release/cut_release.py --dry-run --since v0.1.7
  → "[dry-run] current=0.1.7 next=0.1.8 bump=patch" + changelog body.
  python3 -m pytest -p "no:pytest-qt" \
    tests/test_release_pipeline.py -v
  → 8 passed, 2 skipped (helm not on PATH locally; runs in CI).
  helm template deploy/helm
  → renders the umbrella chart through the coherence-fund subchart.

Verification markers:

  * scripts/release/cut_release.py : `def main\b|conventional` ✓
  * deploy/helm/Chart.yaml         : `apiVersion: v2|name:` ✓
  * Dockerfile                     : `FROM python:` ✓
  * docs/ops/release.md            : `cosign|semver` ✓

Prompt 67 prohibitions honored:
  * Do NOT push unsigned images to GHCR — every
    docker buildx push step is followed by
    `cosign sign --yes <image>@<digest>` in the same job

Prompt 68 — Cap-table integration (Carta primary, Pulley alternate)
                                                              [DONE]
══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════

Wave 18. Adds the post-investment cap-table sync. Record-keeping
only -- the system records issuances the operator caused via the
investment workflow; it does NOT unilaterally issue securities.

What landed:

* `server/fund/services/cap_table_backends.py` -- pluggable
  `CapTableBackend` protocol with `CartaBackend` (primary) and
  `PulleyBackend` (alternate). `record_issuance` returns a
  deterministic `provider_issuance_id`; `fetch_issuance` reads it
  back. Default in-tree path uses an in-process synthetic ledger
  so reconciliation can be exercised without HTTP.
* `server/fund/services/cap_table.py` -- `CapTableService` owns
  the `CapTableIssuance` lifecycle (`pending -> recorded ->
  reconciled`, terminal `failed`). `record_issuance` enforces the
  load-bearing precondition that the application has BOTH a
  signed `SignatureRequest` (prompt 52) AND a sent
  `InvestmentInstruction` (prompt 51). Idempotent on
  `(application_id, instrument_type, salt)` -- the salt is
  typically the instruction id so two distinct funded instructions
  produce two issuance rows but a webhook replay collapses onto
  one. `reconcile(backend=...)` flags divergences but NEVER
  silently rewrites local rows from provider responses.
* `server/fund/models.py` -- new `CapTableIssuance` ORM row.
* `alembic/versions/20260425_000018_cap_table.py` --
  `fund_cap_table_issuances` table with FK to applications and a
  unique idempotency-key index.
* `server/fund/services/application_service.py` -- new
  `maybe_sync_cap_table(application_id, ...)` hook designed to be
  called from both the e-signature webhook (after `signed`) and
  the capital webhook (after `sent`). Whichever side fires second
  satisfies the precondition gate and performs the sync; the
  other returns `None`. Reads `CAP_TABLE_PROVIDER` env var to
  pick the backend.
* `tests/test_cap_table.py` -- 17 tests: backend round-trip and
  determinism on both Carta and Pulley; precondition gating
  (refuses without signed SAFE OR without sent instruction);
  service idempotency; reconcile happy path + forged divergence
  (asserts local row UNCHANGED) + missing-remote reporting;
  `ApplicationService.maybe_sync_cap_table` returns `None` until
  preconditions met, descriptor afterward, and is idempotent.
* `docs/specs/cap_table.md` -- lifecycle, preconditions,
  reconciliation discipline, env-var matrix, operator obligation.
* `.env.example` -- adds the cap-table block (`CAP_TABLE_PROVIDER`,
  `CARTA_API_TOKEN`/`CARTA_API_BASE`, `PULLEY_API_TOKEN`/
  `PULLEY_API_BASE`).

Verification markers:
  * server/fund/services/cap_table.py
        : `class CapTableIssuance|def record_issuance\b` ✓
  * server/fund/services/cap_table_backends.py
        : `CartaBackend|PulleyBackend` ✓
  * docs/specs/cap_table.md
        : `cap[_ -]?table|issuance` ✓
  * tests/test_cap_table.py
        : `record_issuance|reconcile` ✓

Prompt 68 prohibitions honored:
  * Do NOT record an issuance without verifying the corresponding
    signed SAFE artifact AND funded instruction --
    `CapTableService.record_issuance` calls
    `preconditions_satisfied` (default `verify_preconditions=True`)
    which raises `PreconditionsNotMet` unless both rows are present
    in the required terminal states.
  * Do NOT mutate cap-table records without a matching local row +
    audit trail -- the `CapTableIssuance` row is created BEFORE the
    backend dispatch; provider failure marks the row `failed` (still
    auditable), and `reconcile` only mutates the local `status`
    field after a successful match.
  * Do NOT trust the provider's `provider_issuance_id` as
    authoritative -- local idempotency is keyed off the deterministic
    `idempotency_key`; the provider's id is recorded for audit but
    a divergence between local + provider is FLAGGED, never silently
    accepted (`reconcile` puts mismatched fields in
    `report.divergent` and leaves `row.amount_usd` etc. unchanged).
  * No edits outside SCOPE. Files created:
    server/fund/services/cap_table.py,
    server/fund/services/cap_table_backends.py,
    alembic/versions/20260425_000018_cap_table.py,
    tests/test_cap_table.py,
    docs/specs/cap_table.md.
    Files modified: server/fund/models.py,
    server/fund/services/application_service.py,
    .env.example,
    COHERENCE_ENGINE_PROJECT_STATUS.txt,
    COHERENCE_ENGINE_CONTINUATION_PROMPT.txt.

Prompt 69 — LP reporting pipeline (quarterly NAV, capital-call /
            distribution notices, LP portal)              [DONE]
══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════

Wave 18 continues. Adds the LP-facing reporting layer: per-LP NAV
math, deterministic LaTeX rendering for quarterly statements +
capital-call + distribution notices, and a Next.js LP portal gated
by Supabase Auth + the `lp` role.

What landed:

* `server/fund/services/nav_calculator.py` -- pure-functional
  per-LP NAV math. `compute_nav` takes an `LPCommitment`, the
  fund's `PortfolioPosition`s, an operator-attested `Mark`
  table, and a dated `CashFlow` series; returns a frozen
  `NAVSnapshot` with cost basis, FMV, unrealized gain, NAV
  (FMV + uncalled), and IRR. `compute_irr` delegates to
  `pyxirr` when available and falls back to an in-tree
  Newton-Raphson XIRR with bisection over [-0.999, 10.0].
  Load-bearing: any held position without a signed Mark
  raises `UnsignedMarkError` -- statements are NOT
  publishable in that state.
* `server/fund/services/lp_reporting.py` -- orchestrator and
  Jinja2 / LaTeX render env (square-bracket delimiters,
  `StrictUndefined`, `latex` / `usd` / `pct` / `irr` / `isoday`
  filters, byte-deterministic). `assemble_quarterly_statement`
  returns a sealed `QuarterlyStatement` with `tex_source`,
  SHA-256 `content_digest`, and `statement_id =
  stmt_<sha256(lp|quarter|digest)[:24]>`. `assemble_batch` is
  a thin per-LP loop that never shares intermediate state
  across LPs.
* `server/fund/services/capital_call_notice.py` --
  `CapitalCallNotice` payload, `render_notice` (.tex source +
  digest), `render_pdf` (re-uses the MRM `pdflatex` runner),
  and `dispatch_for_signature(provider=..., ...)` that hands
  the rendered document to a caller-supplied
  `ESignatureProvider` (typically the DocuSign backend from
  prompt 52). Idempotency key is sha256(call_id|lp_id) so
  webhook replays collapse on the provider side.
* `server/fund/services/distribution_notice.py` --
  `DistributionNotice` payload + `render_notice` + acknowledgement
  dispatch helper. `treasurer_approval_ref` is REQUIRED -- a
  payload without it is rejected at render time AND at
  dispatch time. The LP signer role is marked
  `lp_acknowledger` (not `lp_signer`) -- the type-system
  marker that the LP is acknowledging receipt, not authorising
  a wire.
* `data/governed/lp_reports/templates/{quarterly_nav,capital_call,
  distribution_notice}.tex.j2` -- governed LaTeX templates
  mirroring the model-risk renderer's delimiter and escape
  conventions.
* `apps/lp_portal/` -- Next.js 14 (App Router) scaffold on
  port 3002 mirroring `apps/founder_portal/`. Pages: `/`
  (sign-in landing, surfaces `lp` role state), `/lp`
  (overview), `/lp/statements` (quarterly NAV table with
  content-digest fingerprint), `/lp/notices` (capital calls
  + distributions). RBAC in `src/lib/rbac.ts`:
  `app_metadata.roles` MUST include `"lp"` (or legacy
  `app_metadata.role === "lp"`) AND `app_metadata.lp_id`
  MUST be set. Shared guard `requireLpSession()` constructs
  the `LpApiClient` keyed off the session's own `lp_id` --
  no user-supplied id is ever honoured. Backend RLS is the
  second layer.
* `tests/test_nav_calculator.py` -- 10 tests: NAV math on a
  single + multi-position synthetic fund, mark-signoff gate
  (unsigned + missing both raise), input validation
  (over-called, ownership > 1.0, wrong-sign cash flow),
  IRR known-doubling case (recovers ~1.0), zero-IRR case,
  degenerate-series None, multi-flow case bounded check,
  NAV-with-IRR integration.
* `tests/test_lp_reporting.py` -- 15 tests: quarterly happy
  path, byte-deterministic rendering with pinned
  `generated_at`, unsigned-Mark refusal, batch isolation
  across two LPs (Alice never appears in Bob's source and
  vice versa), template paths exist, capital-call deterministic
  render, capital-call idempotency-key uniqueness across
  (call_id, lp_id), capital-call dispatch via fake provider
  with header / signer assertions, distribution rejection
  paths (unknown kind, missing wire ref, missing
  treasurer_approval_ref at dispatch), distribution
  acknowledgement-only dispatch with `lp_acknowledger`
  role assertion.
* `apps/lp_portal/__tests__/rbac.test.ts` -- 9 vitest
  cases: roles[]/legacy-role parsing, lp_id extraction,
  `evaluateLpRole` discriminated-union states
  (unauthenticated, forbidden when role missing,
  forbidden when lp_id missing, allowed when both
  present), explicit cross-LP isolation regression
  (helper never honours an attacker-supplied lp_id).
* `apps/lp_portal/__tests__/lp_api.test.ts` -- header
  stamping, URL encoding of lp_id, error mapping,
  formatter checks.
* `docs/specs/lp_reporting.md` -- module map, NAV math,
  IRR contract, determinism guarantees, capital-call /
  distribution lifecycle, RBAC contract, prohibitions,
  operator obligations.

Verification (local):

Prompt 69 prohibitions honored:
  * Do NOT auto-execute distributions.
    `distribution_notice.dispatch_for_acknowledgement` only
    calls `provider.send` for an LP receipt signature; it
    never touches `CapitalDeployment`. The notice payload
    REQUIRES a `treasurer_approval_ref` (validated at both
    render time and dispatch time) -- a notice can only
    refer to a wire the treasurer has already approved
    under the prompt-51 lifecycle. The treasurer remains
    the sole party authorised to execute that wire.
  * Do NOT publish a quarterly statement without `Mark`
    table entries having operator signoff.
    `nav_calculator.compute_nav` raises `UnsignedMarkError`
    on any held position whose Mark is missing
    `operator_signoff_at` + `operator_id`. The
    LP-reporting orchestrator surfaces the exception and
    does NOT fall back to mark-to-cost. Tests:
    `test_unsigned_mark_blocks_publication`,
    `test_assemble_quarterly_statement_rejects_unsigned_mark`.
  * Do NOT expose LP-A's data to LP-B; RLS enforced.
    Two layers: (a) `apps/lp_portal/src/lib/guard.ts`
    constructs the `LpApiClient` exclusively from the
    session's own `lp_id` -- no path-supplied id is ever
    accepted (regression test in
    `apps/lp_portal/__tests__/rbac.test.ts` covers the
    cross-LP isolation case explicitly); (b) the backend
    continues to enforce row-level security on the LP
    statement / notice tables (the prompt-26 investor-RLS
    migration pattern). `assemble_batch` is a per-LP loop
    that never lets one LP's payload land in another LP's
    render context (test:
    `test_assemble_batch_emits_one_statement_per_lp_and_isolates_data`).
  * Do NOT edit files outside SCOPE. Files created:
    server/fund/services/nav_calculator.py,
    server/fund/services/lp_reporting.py,
    server/fund/services/capital_call_notice.py,
    server/fund/services/distribution_notice.py,
    data/governed/lp_reports/templates/quarterly_nav.tex.j2,
    data/governed/lp_reports/templates/capital_call.tex.j2,
    data/governed/lp_reports/templates/distribution_notice.tex.j2,
    apps/lp_portal/ (full Next.js scaffold:
      package.json, tsconfig.json, next.config.js,
      tailwind.config.ts, postcss.config.js,
      vitest.config.ts, next-env.d.ts, .env.example,
      README.md,
      src/app/layout.tsx, src/app/page.tsx,
      src/app/globals.css,
      src/app/api/auth/route.ts,
      src/app/lp/page.tsx,
      src/app/lp/statements/page.tsx,
      src/app/lp/notices/page.tsx,
      src/lib/{supabase,rbac,guard,lp_api}.ts,
      __tests__/{rbac,lp_api}.test.ts),
    tests/test_nav_calculator.py,
    tests/test_lp_reporting.py,
    docs/specs/lp_reporting.md.
    Files modified: COHERENCE_ENGINE_PROJECT_STATUS.txt,
    COHERENCE_ENGINE_CONTINUATION_PROMPT.txt.

  Follow-ups intentionally left for future prompts:
  * `Mark`, `LPCommitment`, `CapitalCall`, `DistributionNotice`
    persistence is intentionally NOT in `server/fund/models.py`
    yet -- the services operate on dataclass inputs the
    caller supplies, mirroring the prompt-51 `_PrepareRequest`
    pattern. A future prompt will land the migration once the
    LP-side ingest workflow (operator UI for marks, capital-
    call schedule generator) lands; this prompt's SCOPE
    deliberately excludes `models.py` edits.
  * Backend `/api/v1/lp/<lp_id>/{overview,statements,notices}`
    FastAPI endpoints. The portal's `LpApiClient` is wired
    against the contract documented in
    `apps/lp_portal/src/lib/lp_api.ts` but the routes
    themselves are out of SCOPE here (would require
    touching `server/fund/routers/__init__.py` plus a new
    router file).


══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════
Prompt 70 — Reserve-allocation optimizer + decision-policy
            parameter proposals                          [DONE]
══════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════════

Wave 18 closes. Adds the deterministic reserve-allocation optimizer
that recomputes per-domain (CS0_d, alpha_d), the liquidity reserve
target, and the pipeline-volume cap from the validation study's
calibrated cost-of-error coefficients + a 90-day historical replay
frame. The optimizer emits a *proposal*; the operator (with the
partner committee) approves before promotion. No auto-promotion.

What landed:

* `server/fund/services/reserve_optimizer.py` -- pure-functional
  optimizer. `optimize(OptimizerInputs)` returns an
  `OptimizerResult` carrying the proposed and current parameter
  sets, the cost-of-error model derived from the validation
  study report, the byte-deterministic backtest delta
  (pass-rate, false-pass exposure, reserve coverage, objective)
  and the optimizer method (`grid` or `scipy`). Constrained
  formulation: minimize lost-EV cost subject to false-pass
  exposure <= budget. SLSQP path lazy-imports
  `scipy.optimize.minimize` when `--prefer-scipy` is set; the
  default path is a deterministic 9x9 grid over (CS0_d, alpha_d)
  that always seeds the candidate list with the running
  parameters so the proposal is never strictly worse than the
  current setting on the in-sample objective.
* `server/fund/services/policy_parameter_proposals.py` --
  persistence + lifecycle. `PolicyParameterProposalService.create`
  enforces the 30-day rate limit on overlapping domains
  (`PROPOSAL_RATE_LIMITED`); `approve` is admin-only
  (`PROPOSAL_FORBIDDEN` otherwise) and emits
  `policy_parameter_approved.v1` with idempotency key
  `proposal:<id>:approved`. Approval does NOT promote -- a
  separate explicit step (operator runbook) is responsible for
  the policy version bump. `render_review` returns a structured
  diff with `per_domain`, `liquidity_reserve`,
  `pipeline_volume_cap`, and `backtest` keys.
* `server/fund/models.py` -- `PolicyParameterProposal` (id,
  proposed_by, parameters_json, rationale, backtest_report_uri,
  status, approved_by, approved_at, created_at, updated_at) +
  `PolicyParameterApproval` (append-only audit row keyed back
  to the proposal).
* `alembic/versions/20260425_000019_policy_parameter_proposals.py`
  -- creates `fund_policy_parameter_proposals` and
  `fund_policy_parameter_approvals` with index on `status` /
  `created_at` / `proposal_id` / `decision`.
* `cli.py` -- `policy propose|review|approve`. `propose`
  reads `--inputs portfolio_snapshot.json`, optionally
  overrides the validation study via `--validation-study`,
  runs the optimizer + backtest replay, writes the canonical
  JSON to `--output`, and persists a `PolicyParameterProposal`
  row. `review --proposal-id N` prints the diff. `approve
  --proposal-id N --principal-role admin` flips status and
  emits the event; non-admin principals get
  `PROPOSAL_FORBIDDEN`.
* `tests/fixtures/policy/snapshot.json` +
  `tests/fixtures/policy/study.json` -- synthetic 14-row
  historical frame + a stub validation-study report carrying
  the bootstrap point estimates the cost-of-error model
  pulls from.
* `tests/test_reserve_optimizer.py` -- 9 tests: bounds,
  improves-vs-current, byte-determinism on fixed seed,
  same-shape proposals across seeds, cost-of-error model
  derivation, inputs digest + method recorded, negative
  budget rejected, pipeline-cap floor at zero volume, reserve
  fraction bounded.
* `tests/test_policy_parameter_proposals.py` -- 10 tests:
  persistence in `proposed`, 30-day rate limit, allowed
  after window, short-rationale rejected, approve forbidden
  for viewer, approve emits event for admin, double-approve
  raises invalid-transition, reject is admin-only and
  terminal, review surfaces required diff keys, unknown
  proposal raises not-found.
* `docs/specs/reserve_optimizer.md` -- cost-of-error model,
  constrained formulation, decision frequency (monthly),
  rollback plan (re-promote prior approved proposal),
  determinism guarantees.

Verification (local):

  ```
  python3 -m pytest -p no:pytest-qt \
    coherence_engine/tests/test_reserve_optimizer.py \
    coherence_engine/tests/test_policy_parameter_proposals.py -v
  ```
  -> 19 passed in 2.50s on the working tree.

  ```
    --output /tmp/proposal.json \
    --rationale "smoke test rationale exceeding minimum length"
  ```
  -> emits the one-line summary; persists the proposal row;
  `policy review` returns the structured diff;
  `policy approve --principal-role admin` flips status and
  writes the `policy_parameter_approved` outbox row.

Verification markers:
  * server/fund/services/reserve_optimizer.py
        : `def optimize\b|scipy\.optimize` ✓
  * server/fund/services/policy_parameter_proposals.py
        : `class PolicyParameterProposal` (re-exported via
        models alias) ✓; service-class is
        `PolicyParameterProposalService`.
  * cli.py
        : `policy propose|policy approve` ✓
  * docs/specs/reserve_optimizer.md
        : `optimizer|backtest|rollback` ✓
  * tests/test_reserve_optimizer.py
        : `optimize|reserve` ✓

Prompt 70 prohibitions honored:
  * Do NOT auto-promote optimizer output. The optimizer
    NEVER touches the running decision policy. The output
    is a `PolicyParameterProposal` row in `proposed`
    status; only an admin `approve` flips it to
    `approved`, and that transition emits an event but
    does not mutate the policy module's
    `_params_for_domain` defaults. Promotion is an
    explicit operator-runbook step out of SCOPE here.
  * Do NOT propose parameters more than once a month per
    domain. The CLI / service layer enforces a 30-day
    rate limit on overlapping domains
    (`MIN_PROPOSAL_INTERVAL_DAYS = 30`); a second
    proposal raises `PROPOSAL_RATE_LIMITED` (test:
    `test_create_rate_limits_overlapping_domain_within_30_days`).
  * Do NOT skip the backtest replay. Every proposal blob
    carries a populated `BacktestDelta` (pass-rate,
    false-pass exposure, reserve coverage, objective
    before/after); the optimizer always runs the replay
    on the supplied historical rows and the canonical
    bytes are deterministic.
  * Do NOT edit files outside SCOPE. Files created:
    server/fund/services/reserve_optimizer.py,
    server/fund/services/policy_parameter_proposals.py,
    alembic/versions/20260425_000019_policy_parameter_proposals.py,
    tests/test_reserve_optimizer.py,
    tests/test_policy_parameter_proposals.py,
    tests/fixtures/policy/snapshot.json,
    tests/fixtures/policy/study.json,
    docs/specs/reserve_optimizer.md.
    Files modified: server/fund/models.py, cli.py,
    COHERENCE_ENGINE_PROJECT_STATUS.txt,
    COHERENCE_ENGINE_CONTINUATION_PROMPT.txt.

  Follow-ups intentionally left for future prompts:
  * Decision-policy promotion script (the explicit
    operator runbook step that consumes
    `policy_parameter_approved.v1` and writes a new
    pinned parameter set into the running
    `DecisionPolicyService._params_for_domain`).
    Out of SCOPE here -- the prompt is explicit that
    promotion is a separate, explicit step.
  * Per-domain false-pass-budget weighting. The
    optimizer currently splits the total budget evenly
    across `inputs.domains`; an exposure-weighted split
    is a future enhancement keyed off the prompt-44
    domain breakdown.
